proceed

Thing we are building:

Matching System (Client ↔ Cleaner)
This is how PureTask decides which cleaners a client sees first, who gets auto-offers, and how we protect top cleaners from chaotic clients using:

Reliability Score 2.0

Client Risk Score

Flexibility / badges

Availability & distance

Tiers & pricing

1. What this system needs to operate
1.1 Inputs from cleaners
For each cleaner we need:

cleaner_id

Location (home base lat/lng or service area)

Max travel radius (miles/km)

Availability:

Working days

Time windows

Existing bookings (to avoid overlap)

Tier & scores:

reliability_score (0–100)

tier (Developing / Semi Pro / Pro / Elite)

low_flexibility_badge (true/false)

Job constraints:

Max jobs per day (capacity)

Preferred job types (deep, move-out, basic, etc.)

Preferred client type (recurring vs one-off, optional)

Status flags:

is_active, is_suspended, last_job_at, etc.

1.2 Inputs from clients / job
For each job:

job_id

client_id

Location (job lat/lng)

Job type:

basic / deep / move-out / recurring, etc.

Estimated duration & credits/hour

Requested start datetime

Repeat frequency (one-time / weekly / biweekly / monthly)

Special notes / requirements (pets, supplies, etc.)

From client profile:

client_risk_score (0–100)

Risk band (Normal / Mild / Elevated / High / Critical)

Flexibility profile (from reschedules, optional later)

Past cleaner relationship:

Previous cleaners for this client

Whether they want same cleaner again

1.3 Constraints / dependencies
Must respect:

Cleaner availability & capacity

Travel radius

Tier logic (pricing & payouts)

Risk protection rules:

High-risk clients should not always go to top-tier cleaners.

Must integrate with:

Reliability Score 2.0 (for ranking cleaners)

Client Risk Score (for filtering / ranking)

Low Flexibility badge (matching the right clients)

2. High-level goals of the Matching System
Clients get great options quickly, with clear quality tiers.

Top cleaners are protected from high-risk / chaotic clients.

New cleaners get fair exposure without being flooded with bad clients.

Repeat relationships are favored when both sides have good scores.

Sorting is explainable (“you see this cleaner first because X, Y, Z”).

We’ll support two modes:

Search / Browse: client sees a list ranked by the algorithm.

Auto-match / Recommended: platform suggests the “best” cleaner(s) to assign.

3. Matching pipeline (step-by-step)
Step 1 — Build candidate pool
From all active cleaners, we first filter:

is_active = true

Not suspended / banned

Within travel radius of job location

Available at requested time (no overlapping bookings)

Service the job type (deep / move-out / basic flags)

This yields CandidateCleaners[].

If empty → we can:

Expand radius slightly, or

Offer alternate times, or

Suggest posting as “flexible time today/this week”.

Step 2 — Risk-based filtering
We now consider the client_risk_score:

Let:

risk_band:
  0–9    → Normal
  10–19  → Mild
  20–39  → Elevated
  40–59  → High
  60–100 → Critical
We enforce:

Critical (60–100):

Only match with cleaners explicitly allowed for high-risk jobs (e.g., “High Flex / Willing to Take Risk” pool).

No Elite-only matching.

May require manual approval / prepay.

High (40–59):

Do not auto-match to Elite by default.

Prefer Semi Pro / Pro with good reliability but without heavy overprotection.

Still possible to book Elite manually via search, but ranking will slightly push others higher.

Elevated (20–39):

All tiers available.

Ranking penalizes a bit; we favor pairing them with Pro vs Elite.

Normal / Mild (0–19):

Full access to all cleaners; no risk-based restrictions.

Implementation concept:
We can apply a risk filter weight when scoring candidate cleaners for this job.

Step 3 — Repeat vs new cleaner preference
We prioritize existing relationships when they are healthy.

For a given client, if they had previous cleaners:

Fetch any cleaner with:

Past jobs with this client

reliability_score ≥ 70

client_risk_score not High/Critical at time of those jobs

No serious disputes between them

If such “good history” cleaners are available:

Boost them significantly in ranking (clients love continuity).

If reliability is high and they are free at that time:

They may become the top recommended cleaner.

Step 4 — Scoring function (ranking formula)
We now compute a match_score for each candidate cleaner.

We’ll build something simple, additive, and explainable:

match_score =
    w_reliability   * normalized_reliability
  + w_tier          * tier_score
  + w_distance      * distance_score
  + w_history       * history_score
  + w_flex          * flexibility_score
  + w_risk_alignment* risk_alignment_score
Where each component is 0–1, then weighted.

Suggested base weights (tunable):

w_reliability = 0.35

w_tier = 0.20

w_distance = 0.15

w_history = 0.15

w_flex = 0.10

w_risk_alignment = 0.05

Let’s define each:

4.1 Reliability component
normalized_reliability = reliability_score / 100  // 0–1

reliability_component = normalized_reliability
This strongly favors highly reliable cleaners (90–100) over lower.

4.2 Tier component
Map tiers to 0–1:

tier_score =
  Developing → 0.1
  Semi Pro   → 0.4
  Pro        → 0.7
  Elite      → 1.0
This ensures higher tiers rank above lower tiers, all else equal.

4.3 Distance component
We want nearby cleaners first. Let:

distance_km = distance between cleaner base and job.

max_radius_km = cleaner’s allowed radius.

Compute:

normalized_distance_factor =
  1 - (distance_km / max_radius_km)   // 1 near center, 0 at edge

distance_score = clamp(0, 1, normalized_distance_factor)
4.4 History component (repeat clients)
If:

Cleaner has ≥1 past job with this client

And no unresolved disputes / major issues

Then:

history_score = 1.0   // strong boost
Else:

history_score = 0.0
If you want nuance, you can scale by count, but 0 vs 1 is often enough.

4.5 Flexibility component
We use:

Cleaner’s low_flexibility_badge

Client’s flexibility needs (e.g., from frequency of reschedules; optional)

For now:

if client_risk_band in {High, Critical}:
    if cleaner.low_flexibility_badge:
        flexibility_score = 0.0    // bad fit
    else:
        flexibility_score = 1.0    // good fit (more flexible)
else:
    // For normal/mild clients
    if cleaner.low_flexibility_badge:
        flexibility_score = 0.5    // neutral-ish
    else:
        flexibility_score = 1.0
This ensures:

High-risk / chaotic clients are not matched with low-flex cleaners.

Low-flex cleaners get better matches with stable clients.

4.6 Risk alignment component
We want to avoid high-risk clients always hitting Elite.

Define:

if client_risk_band in {Normal, Mild}:
    risk_alignment_score = 1.0   // everything good

if client_risk_band == Elevated:
    if cleaner.tier in {Pro, Semi Pro}:
        risk_alignment_score = 1.0
    else:
        risk_alignment_score = 0.7

if client_risk_band == High:
    if cleaner.tier == Elite:
        risk_alignment_score = 0.3
    else:
        risk_alignment_score = 1.0

if client_risk_band == Critical:
    if cleaner.tier == Elite:
        risk_alignment_score = 0.0
    else:
        risk_alignment_score = 0.5
This is a soft push, not a hard ban (except maybe for Critical + Elite if you want).

4.7 Final match_score
For each candidate:

match_score =
    0.35 * reliability_component
  + 0.20 * tier_score
  + 0.15 * distance_score
  + 0.15 * history_score
  + 0.10 * flexibility_score
  + 0.05 * risk_alignment_score
Then sort descending by match_score.

Top N cleaners (e.g., top 10) are shown / considered for auto-match.

5. How this affects different client types
5.1 Normal, stable client
Low risk

High flexibility in matching

They’ll see:

Elite & Pro cleaners at the top

Sorted by reliability, distance, and past relationship

Best overall experience.

5.2 High-risk, chaotic client
High risk score due to no-shows, late cancels, etc.

System reaction:

Elite cleaners:

Lower risk_alignment_score → rank drops.

Cleaners with low flexibility:

Low flexibility_score → poor ranking.

More flexible/newer cleaners:

Higher flexibility & tier weighting → rank better.

They may also:

Lose grace cancellations

Have fewer last-minute reschedule options

Be forced to prepay depending on band

This protects your best cleaners from being burned out.

5.3 Cleaner with Low Flexibility badge
For normal clients:

Still matched, just with slightly lower flexibility score (0.5).

Their reliability & tier still carry them.

For high-risk clients:

Flexibility score = 0 → they effectively won’t be auto-matched.

This directly implements your “Low Flexibility” concept in matching.

6. Special matching rules
6.1 Recurring jobs
For weekly/biweekly/monthly bookings:

Strongly favor same cleaner as long as:

Reliability ≥ 70

No major disputes

Client risk not High/Critical

If either side’s score drops (e.g., cleaner reliability plummets or client risk skyrockets), the system can:

Suggest a new cleaner to the client.

Or de-prioritize that cleaner for that client.

6.2 Minimum score requirement
You can enforce:

Cleaners with reliability_score < 50 (low Developing) are not shown to new clients.

They may only be matched with:

Discount jobs

Or internal “save this cleaner” programs.

This ties reliability directly to opportunity.

6.3 Geo-expansion fallback
If no candidate cleaner has match_score > threshold:

Option 1:

Expand search radius by X miles and recalc.

Option 2:

Suggest alternate times automatically where top cleaners are available.

Option 3:

Allow client to post job as “flexible within this day” for better matching.

7. Data model sketch
You don’t need to build a new table for “matches” necessarily, but:

Keep existing cleaners & jobs tables.

Use a service that:

Queries candidates

Computes match_score

Returns sorted_cleaners.

Optional logging table:

Table: match_recommendations

id

job_id

client_id

cleaner_id

match_score

rank

generated_at

This is useful for analytics & debugging.

8. What’s “built” now
You now have a full Matching System spec that:

Uses Reliability Score 2.0

Uses Client Risk Score

Respects Low Flexibility badges

Respects availability, radius, tiers

Favors:

repeat relationships

top performers

stable clients

Protects:

Elite cleaners from high-risk clients

Low-flex cleaners from chaos

Remains:

explainable

tunable

implementable in SQL + Node/Base44

2️⃣ New Cancellation & Rescheduling Policy (drop-in page)
You can use this as your new “Cancellation & Rescheduling Policy” page in the Legal Center.

Cancellation & Rescheduling Policy
Last updated: [set date]

We understand that plans change. This policy explains how cancellations and rescheduling work for both clients and cleaners, and how fees are applied. It is designed to protect everyone’s time while keeping the system flexible and fair.

1. Key Definitions
Booking – A confirmed cleaning appointment with a date, time, and assigned cleaner.

Cancellation – Permanently ending a booking so it no longer occurs.

Reschedule – Moving a confirmed booking to a different date and/or time.

Mutual Reschedule – A reschedule request that is accepted by the other party (client or cleaner).

No-Show – When a client or cleaner fails to be present/available for the booking at the agreed time.

Credits are held in escrow when a booking is made and released or refunded according to this policy. (10 credits = $1 USD.)

2. Client Cancellation Fees
Client cancellation fees are based on how much notice you provide before the scheduled start time.

Let “booking time” mean the scheduled start time of the cleaning.

2.1 Standard Cancellation Windows
More than 48 hours before booking

Fee: 0% (Free cancellation)

Result: 100% of escrowed credits are refunded to your PureTask account.

24–48 hours before booking

Fee: 50% of booking amount

Result: 50% of escrowed credits are refunded, 50% are kept as a late cancellation fee.

Less than 24 hours before booking

Fee: 100% of booking amount

Result: 0% refunded, 100% kept as a late cancellation fee.

These rules match your existing policy, but are explicitly tied into rescheduling logic below.

2.2 Grace Cancellations (Clients)
We know emergencies happen. Every client receives 2 grace cancellations that can be used to waive late cancellation fees.

You may apply a grace cancellation to any client-initiated cancellation with:

24–48 hours notice (50% fee), or

Less than 24 hours notice (100% fee)

When you use a grace cancellation:

The cancellation fee is waived (you pay 0%).

100% of escrowed credits are returned to your PureTask account.

The cancellation is still logged internally.

Grace cancellations:

Do not replenish over time.

Cannot be used for no-shows (you must cancel before the booking time to use grace).

Are only available for client-initiated cancellations.

3. Cleaner Cancellations
When a cleaner cancels a confirmed booking:

The client is never charged a fee.

100% of escrowed credits are returned to the client’s PureTask account.

PureTask may attempt to match the client with a new cleaner, but cannot guarantee availability.

Internally:

Cleaner cancellations may affect the cleaner’s reliability score and future access to bookings, especially for short-notice cancellations.

Repeated cancellations may lead to warnings, reduced visibility, or account review.

Cleaners are independent contractors and are never required to pay clients or PureTask for cancelling a job, but unreliability can affect their account standing.

4. No-Show Policy
4.1 Client No-Show
You are considered a no-show if:

The cleaner arrives on time at the service address,

Attempts to contact you (call, text, or in-app messages),

Waits at least 15 minutes at or near the location, and

You are unreachable or unable to provide access to the property.

When a client no-show occurs:

Fee: 100% of the booking amount

Result:

The cleaner is paid for the reserved time

No refund is issued

Grace cancellations cannot be used for no-shows.

Repeated no-shows may affect your ability to book future cleanings.

4.2 Cleaner No-Show
A cleaner is considered a no-show if:

They do not arrive or check in within 30 minutes of the scheduled start time, and

The client’s location and access instructions are accurate.

When a cleaner no-show occurs:

The client receives:

A full refund of escrowed credits

Bonus credits (e.g., 50 credits) as an apology

PureTask may attempt to assign a backup cleaner if possible.

Internally:

Cleaner no-shows cause a serious negative impact on the cleaner’s reliability score and may lead to suspension or removal from the platform.

5. Rescheduling Policy
Rescheduling is different from cancelling. A reschedule moves the booking to a new date/time instead of ending it.

5.1 Mutual Reschedule (Both Parties Agree)
If either the client or the cleaner requests a reschedule and the other party accepts, this is a Mutual Reschedule.

The booking is moved to the new agreed time.

No cancellation fees apply.

Escrowed credits remain in place and move with the booking.

The job keeps the same job ID and pricing.

Mutual reschedules are always free and do not use a grace cancellation.

5.2 Reschedule Requests and Time Windows
When one party requests to reschedule, PureTask records:

Who requested (client or cleaner)

When the request was made

The original and proposed new time

Reschedule requests follow the same time buckets as cancellations:

>48 hours before original start – Early reschedule

24–48 hours before – Mid-window reschedule

<24 hours before – Late reschedule

There is no automatic fee just for requesting a reschedule.

However:

If the reschedule request is not accepted, and

The requester then cannot keep the original time and cancels,

…then the normal cancellation rules apply based on when they cancel.

5.3 What Happens When a Reschedule is Declined
If the other party declines a reschedule request:

The booking remains at the original date and time.

Both parties are expected to honor the original schedule.

If the requester:

Keeps the original time → the booking proceeds with no cancellation fee.

Cancels instead → this is treated as a client or cleaner cancellation, and the cancellation policy above applies (fees, refunds, and internal score impact).

This is especially important when:

A client asks to reschedule within 24 hours, the cleaner declines, and the client can no longer make the original time. In that case, the client cancellation policy (including potential 100% fee and grace options) applies.

5.4 Limits on Rescheduling
To protect everyone’s time:

Each booking typically allows one reschedule.

Additional changes may require cancelling and creating a new booking.

Excessive last-minute reschedules or cancellations may result in:

Stricter application of this policy

Limits on rescheduling options

Account review

These limits are enforced internally based on overall behavior and patterns.

5.5 Cleaner Reschedule Requests
When a cleaner requests to reschedule:

The client can accept or decline.

If accepted, the booking moves to the new time with no fee to the client.

If declined, the cleaner is expected to honor the original time.

If the cleaner:

Cancels instead of honoring the original time → this is a cleaner cancellation (client is fully refunded, no fee).

Fails to show up → this is a cleaner no-show (see Section 4.2).

Internally, frequent or last-minute reschedule requests from cleaners may affect their reliability score and access to future bookings.

6. Emergencies & Force Majeure
In cases of:

Severe weather

Natural disasters

Major power or infrastructure outages

Other events outside of a client’s or cleaner’s reasonable control

PureTask may, at its sole discretion:

Waive cancellation or rescheduling fees

Adjust refunds or payouts

Prioritize safety over strict enforcement of this policy

If you believe your situation qualifies as an emergency, please contact support and provide any relevant details or documentation.

7. Repeated Issues & Account Standing
This policy governs fees and refunds, but PureTask also tracks behavioral patterns to protect the marketplace.

Examples:

Frequent late cancellations

Frequent last-minute reschedules

Repeated no-shows

Abuse of grace cancellations

Abusive or harassing behavior

These patterns may affect:

Your ability to use grace cancellations

Access to certain cleaners or booking types

Your account’s overall standing, up to and including suspension

PureTask evaluates behavior over time and may take action to protect clients, cleaners, and platform integrity.

Below are patches you can merge into your current Terms of Service document.

A. Booking & Payment Terms – Cancellation & Rescheduling
Replace your current Cancellation section under “Booking & Payment Terms” with:

Cancellation & Rescheduling
Clients may cancel bookings subject to the Cancellation & Rescheduling Policy available in our Legal Center. Cancellation fees are based on how much notice is provided before the scheduled start time. In general, cancellations made more than 48 hours in advance are free; cancellations within 24–48 hours may incur a 50% fee; and cancellations less than 24 hours before the scheduled start time may incur a 100% fee. Grace cancellations and emergency exceptions are described in that policy.

Cleaners may cancel bookings at any time; however, clients will not be charged any cancellation fee if a cleaner cancels. PureTask may attempt, but does not guarantee, to assign a replacement cleaner. Cleaner cancellations and no-shows may affect a cleaner’s visibility, reliability score, and continued access to the Platform.

Either party may request to reschedule a booking. Rescheduling requests require mutual agreement. If a reschedule request is declined, the original booking time remains in effect. If the requesting party cannot honor the original time and cancels instead, the cancellation will be handled according to the applicable cancellation window and fees.

B. Trust & Safety / Account Standing
Add or update a paragraph like:

Behavior, Reliability, and Account Standing
To protect the quality and reliability of the marketplace, PureTask may track behavioral patterns such as attendance, on-time arrival, rescheduling frequency, cancellations, no-shows, disputes, and communication quality. Repeated late cancellations, no-shows, abusive conduct, or other behaviors that negatively impact clients, cleaners, or the Platform may result in reduced access to certain features, lower visibility in search results, temporary limitations, or account suspension. PureTask may exercise its discretion in evaluating account behavior and determining appropriate actions consistent with this Policy and our Terms.

C. Independent Contractor Clarification (unchanged but reinforced)
You already state cleaners are independent contractors. You can optionally add one sentence:

PureTask does not require cleaners to accept rescheduled times or specific bookings; cleaners may choose which jobs to accept or decline, provided they honor any bookings they have agreed to perform, subject to the Cancellation & Rescheduling Policy.

Backend Scoring Algorithms (Implementation-Ready Logic)
This is one of the MOST important deliverables in the entire PureTask system because it turns all policies, logic, and behavioral rules into actual functions that your backend (Node.js, SQL, Base44 workflows, n8n, cron jobs) will run.

🔥 PART 1 — Reliability Score Engine (Cleaners)
This is a daily recompute job + event-based updates.

1.1 Required Tables / Fields
cleaners table (existing, add fields)
cleaners {
  id
  reliability_score           // computed 0–100
  reliability_tier            // derived: Developing, Semi Pro, Pro, Elite
  reliability_last_computed   // timestamp
  ...
}
cleaner_metrics table (rolling metrics)
cleaner_metrics {
  cleaner_id
  total_jobs_window                // last 30 jobs or 60 days
  attended_jobs
  no_show_jobs
  on_time_checkins
  photo_compliant_jobs
  communication_ok_jobs
  completion_ok_jobs
  ratings_sum                      // for the window
  ratings_count
}
cleaner_events table (penalties / bonuses)
cleaner_events {
  id
  cleaner_id
  job_id nullable
  event_type enum(
    'late_reschedule',
    'cancel_24_48',
    'cancel_lt24',
    'no_show',
    'dispute_cleaner_at_fault',
    'inconvenience_high',
    'streak_bonus'
  )
  weight int   // negative or positive
  created_at timestamp
  metadata jsonb
}
We will also maintain a derived helper table for reschedule patterns:

cleaner_reschedule_stats {
  cleaner_id
  late_reschedule_count_30days
  ...
}
1.2 Base Reliability Calculation (0–90 points)
AttendanceScore = (attended_jobs / (attended_jobs + no_show_jobs)) * 25

PunctualityScore = (on_time_checkins / attended_jobs) * 20

PhotoScore = (photo_compliant_jobs / attended_jobs) * 15

CommunicationScore = (communication_ok_jobs / attended_jobs) * 10

CompletionScore = (completion_ok_jobs / attended_jobs) * 10

RatingScore = ((avg_rating - 3) / 2) * 10
Clamped between 0 and 10.
Where avg_rating = ratings_sum / ratings_count.

Place in SQL form:

AttendanceScore       = 25 * (attended_jobs::float / NULLIF((attended_jobs + no_show_jobs),0))
PunctualityScore      = 20 * (on_time_checkins::float / NULLIF(attended_jobs,0))
PhotoScore            = 15 * (photo_compliant_jobs::float / NULLIF(attended_jobs,0))
CommunicationScore    = 10 * (communication_ok_jobs::float / NULLIF(attended_jobs,0))
CompletionScore       = 10 * (completion_ok_jobs::float / NULLIF(attended_jobs,0))
NormalizedRating      = ((avg_rating - 3) / 2)
RatingScore           = 10 * LEAST(GREATEST(NormalizedRating, 0), 1)
Then:

BaseBehaviorScore =
  AttendanceScore
+ PunctualityScore
+ PhotoScore
+ CommunicationScore
+ CompletionScore
+ RatingScore
1.3 Streak Bonus Calculation (0–10 points)
We check if cleaner had:

No cancellations in last 7 days

No no-shows in last 7 days

Punctuality ≥ 90% in last 7 days

Photo compliance ≥ 90% in last 7 days

If yes → they get +2 points.

Up to a cap of 10.

SQL logic:

weekly_streak_count = (
  SELECT COUNT(*)
  FROM cleaner_weekly_streaks
  WHERE cleaner_id = X
  AND is_streak = true
  LIMIT 5
);

StreakBonus = LEAST(weekly_streak_count * 2, 10)
1.4 Event Penalties Logic
Weights:

late_reschedule (<24h): −3

cleaner_cancel_24_48: −8

cleaner_cancel_lt24: −12

cleaner_no_show: −25

dispute_cleaner_at_fault: −10

inconvenience pattern: −5 to −10 depending on repeat

SQL to sum penalties:

EventPenalty = COALESCE((
  SELECT SUM(weight)
  FROM cleaner_events
  WHERE cleaner_id = X
  AND created_at > NOW() - INTERVAL '60 days'
), 0)
1.5 Final Reliability Score
RawScore = BaseBehaviorScore + StreakBonus - EventPenalty

ReliabilityScore = LEAST(GREATEST(RawScore, 0), 100)
Tier derivation:

CASE
  WHEN ReliabilityScore < 60 THEN 'Developing'
  WHEN ReliabilityScore < 75 THEN 'Semi Pro'
  WHEN ReliabilityScore < 90 THEN 'Pro'
  ELSE 'Elite'
END
1.6 New Cleaner Ramp-Up Logic
If job_count < 5:

ReliabilityScore =
  (70*(5-job_count) + RawScore*job_count) / 5
🔥 PART 2 — Client Risk Score Engine
This runs daily + on key events.

2.1 Required Tables
client_risk_scores
client_risk_scores {
  client_id
  risk_score     // 0–100
  risk_band      // normal, mild, elevated, high, critical
  updated_at
}
client_risk_events
client_risk_events {
  id
  client_id
  job_id nullable
  event_type enum(
    'late_reschedule_lt24',
    'late_reschedule_pattern',
    'cancel_24_48',
    'cancel_lt24',
    'cancel_after_decline',
    'no_show',
    'dispute_client_at_fault',
    'card_decline',
    'chargeback',
    'inconvenience_high',
    'abuse_flag'
  )
  weight int      // +1, +3, +5, +10, +20 etc.
  created_at
  metadata jsonb
}
2.2 Event Weights (from our finalized rules)
late_reschedule_lt24: +1

late_reschedule_pattern (3 in 14 days): +10

cancel_24_48: +3

cancel_lt24: +5

cancel_after_decline: +1 (stacked)

no_show: +20

dispute_client_at_fault: +10

card_decline: +1 (cap 3)

chargeback: +20

inconvenience_pattern: +5 / +10

abuse_flag: +20

2.3 Daily Compute Logic
Compute base:

BaseRisk = (
  SELECT SUM(weight)
  FROM client_risk_events
  WHERE client_id = X
    AND created_at > NOW() - INTERVAL '60 days'
)
Null-safe:

BaseRisk = COALESCE(BaseRisk, 0)
2.4 Decay Logic
Every 7 days with no negative events:

RiskAfterDecay = GREATEST(BaseRisk - 2, 0)
This will be applied during daily cron:

IF NOT EXISTS (
    SELECT 1
    FROM client_risk_events
    WHERE client_id=X
    AND created_at > NOW() - INTERVAL '7 days'
) THEN
    RiskAfterDecay = GREATEST(BaseRisk - 2,0)
ELSE
    RiskAfterDecay = BaseRisk
END
2.5 Risk Band Derivation
CASE
  WHEN RiskAfterDecay < 10 THEN 'normal'
  WHEN RiskAfterDecay < 20 THEN 'mild'
  WHEN RiskAfterDecay < 40 THEN 'elevated'
  WHEN RiskAfterDecay < 60 THEN 'high'
  ELSE 'critical'
END
🔥 PART 3 — Reschedule Engine Logic (Backend)
This is transactional, runs at moment of request.

3.1 Reason Codes Table
reschedule_reason_codes {
  id
  requester_type   // client | cleaner
  reason_text
}
3.2 Reschedule Request Table
reschedule_events {
  id
  job_id
  requested_by     // client | cleaner
  requested_to     // opposite
  t_request
  t_start_original
  t_start_new
  hours_before_original
  bucket           // lt24, 24_48, gt48
  reason_code
  status           // pending, accepted, declined, expired
  declined_by
  decline_reason_code
  is_reasonable bool
  created_at
}
3.3 Determine bucket
hours_before = EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM (t_start_original - t_request)) / 3600

CASE
  WHEN hours_before <= 0 THEN 'invalid'
  WHEN hours_before <= 24 THEN 'lt24'
  WHEN hours_before <= 48 THEN '24_48'
  ELSE 'gt48'
END
3.4 Determine is_reasonable
Reasonable only if:

is_reasonable =
  cleaner_is_available_for(t_start_new)    AND
  ABS(t_start_new - t_start_original) <= INTERVAL '7 days' AND
  reschedule_count_for_job < 1 AND
  t_request < t_start_original
3.5 If ACCEPTED
If requested_by = client:
If bucket='lt24':

INSERT INTO client_risk_events (client_id, event_type, weight)
VALUES (client_id, 'late_reschedule_lt24', +1)
If patterns (3 in 14 days), another insert:

INSERT ... ('late_reschedule_pattern', +10)
If requested_by = cleaner:
If bucket='lt24':

INSERT INTO cleaner_events (cleaner_id, event_type, weight)
VALUES (cleaner_id, 'late_reschedule', -3)
Update job:

UPDATE jobs
SET start_time = t_start_new
WHERE id = job_id
Set event status:

status = 'accepted'
3.6 If DECLINED
Job remains at original time.

Set:

status='declined', declined_by=X
If requester later cancels → Cancellation Engine handles fees.

🔥 PART 4 — Cancellation Engine Logic (Backend)
Runs when user taps “Cancel Booking”.

4.1 Determine window bucket
Same as reschedule:

hours_before = ...
bucket = 'gt48' | '24_48' | 'lt24' | 'no_show'
(No-show is determined by check-in logic.)

4.2 Fee Table
>48h:   0%
24–48h: 50%
<24h:   100%
no-show: 100%
4.3 Grace Cancellation Logic
If:

requester = client

bucket != no_show

grace_remaining > 0

→ Offer grace.

If used:

fee_pct = 0
grace_used += 1
4.4 Disposition of credits
held = job.held_credits
fee_credits = held * fee_pct
refund_credits = held - fee_credits
Then split fee_credits:

For lt24 or 24–48:
cleaner_pct = 0.70 (24–48) OR 0.80 (<24h)
platform_pct= remainder
SQL:

cleaner_comp = fee_credits * cleaner_pct
platform_comp = fee_credits - cleaner_comp
Refund:

UPDATE clients SET credits = credits + refund_credits
UPDATE cleaners SET pending_credits = pending_credits + cleaner_comp
4.5 Internal Scoring Impact
Client side:
If bucket=24_48:

+3 risk
If bucket=lt24:

+5 risk
If cancel_after_decline flag triggered:

+1 risk
Cleaner side:
If cleaner is the one cancelling:

48 → no penalty

24–48 → −8

<24 → −12

Cleaner no-show:

−25 reliability

Full refund + bonus to client

Client no-show:

+20 risk

Cleaner gets paid 100%

Thing we are building:

Reason Codes + Inconvenience Engine
This is the “context layer” for PureTask:
It explains why things happened (reason codes) and how painful they were (inconvenience score), so your Risk + Reliability systems can react intelligently instead of blindly.

1. What this system needs to operate
1.1 Events that should carry reason codes + inconvenience
We want reason codes and inconvenience scores for:

Reschedules

Client → Cleaner

Cleaner → Client

Cancellations

Client-initiated

Cleaner-initiated

No-shows

Client no-show (for context)

Cleaner no-show (for context)

Major disruptions

Access issues

Wrong address

Strong mismatch in expectations

Each of these events is already logged in our other engines; now we add:

reason_code (structured enum)

Optional free_text_note (short text, internal)

inconvenience_score (1–4 from the affected party)

1.2 Dependencies
This system plugs into:

Client Risk Score Engine

High inconvenience events caused by client → risk patterns.

Reliability Score 2.0

High inconvenience events caused by cleaner → event penalties.

Rescheduling System

Every reschedule has a reason + optional inconvenience feedback.

Cancellation System

Every cancellation has a reason + optional inconvenience feedback.

2. Reason Codes
We need a fixed, small, clear list so data is clean.

2.1 Table: reason_codes
reason_codes {
  id               serial primary key
  code             text unique         -- e.g., 'client_schedule_conflict'
  actor_type       text                -- 'client' | 'cleaner' | 'system' | 'both'
  category         text                -- 'reschedule' | 'cancel' | 'no_show' | 'issue'
  label            text                -- human readable
  description      text                -- for internal use/docs
  is_active        boolean default true
}
2.2 Suggested codes
Client-side reschedule/cancel:

client_schedule_conflict
“Client has a scheduling conflict”

client_work_change
“Work schedule changed”

client_family_emergency
“Family or personal emergency”

client_needs_different_time
“Prefers a different time slot”

client_not_ready_home
“Home not ready (stuff in the way, construction, etc.)”

client_other
“Other (client)”

Cleaner-side reschedule/cancel:

cleaner_schedule_conflict
“Cleaner has a scheduling conflict”

cleaner_previous_job_overrun
“Previous job is running late”

cleaner_transport_issue
“Transportation issue”

cleaner_health_issue
“Health/medical issue”

cleaner_family_emergency
“Family or personal emergency”

cleaner_other
“Other (cleaner)”

No-show / issue context:

client_no_show_access
“Client unavailable / no access at arrival”

address_incorrect_or_confusing
“Address or instructions incorrect”

client_canceled_on_arrival
“Client canceled at the door”

cleaner_no_show_no_contact
“Cleaner did not show or respond”

cleaner_late_extreme
“Cleaner extremely late (>60 min)”

supplies_issue
“Supplies/equipment issue”

safety_or_comfort_concern
“Safety/comfort concern (either side)”

You can expand later, but this is plenty.

3. Inconvenience Score System
This is a 1–4 rating given by the party who did NOT trigger the event.

3.1 Scale
We’ll standardize:

1 – Not inconvenient at all
“This change was fine, no problem.”

2 – Minor inconvenience
“A bit annoying, but acceptable.”

3 – Moderate inconvenience
“Disrupted my plans.”

4 – Major inconvenience
“Really caused problems for me.”

We only ask for this in meaningful disruption scenarios:

Reschedules within 48 hours

Cancellations within 48 hours

No-shows

Big-time shifts

Access/safety issues

No need to ask if:

It’s >48h and a mutual reschedule

It’s clearly trivial / minor shift

4. Data model for inconvenience logging
4.1 Table: inconvenience_logs
inconvenience_logs {
  id                  serial primary key
  job_id              bigint references jobs(id)
  client_id           bigint references clients(id)
  cleaner_id          bigint references cleaners(id)

  caused_by           text   -- 'client' | 'cleaner' | 'system'
  rated_by            text   -- 'client' | 'cleaner' (the other side)

  score               int    -- 1..4
  related_event_type  text   -- 'reschedule' | 'cancel' | 'no_show' | 'issue'
  related_event_id    bigint -- e.g. reschedule_events.id or cancellation_events.id

  reason_code         text   -- optional, from reason_codes or separate mapping
  note                text   -- optional free text
  created_at          timestamp default now()
}
We can store reason_code here to override or add detail, but usually it’s on the reschedule/cancellation record.

5. Where and when we ask for inconvenience
5.1 After reschedule is accepted
If:

Reschedule was <48h before original time, AND

Other party accepted, THEN:

Pop a prompt:

For client when cleaner requested:
“How inconvenient was this change to your schedule?”

For cleaner when client requested:
“How inconvenient was this change to your schedule?”

If they skip → no log.
If they answer → insert into inconvenience_logs.

5.2 After cancellations (late)
If:

Cancellation is 24–48h or <24h

AND the other party had already planned around it

Prompt the non-canceller:

“How inconvenient was this cancellation for you?”

Again, log only if they answer.

5.3 After no-show resolution
When support resolves a no-show (client or cleaner):

Optionally log an inconvenience score from the affected party:

If cleaner no-show → ask client.

If client no-show → ask cleaner (but this is already extremely obvious; it may be redundant).

In practice, we can assume no-shows are always “4” for the victim, so we might only log structured events and skip asking. Either approach works.

6. How Inconvenience feeds Reliability & Risk
6.1 Cleaner Reliability (penalties from inconvenience)
We don’t penalize one-off little annoyances. We penalize patterns:

Consider logs where:

caused_by = 'cleaner'

score >= 3

Within last 30 days

Compute:

high_inconvenience_cleaner_count =
  COUNT(*) WHERE caused_by='cleaner' AND score >= 3 AND created_at > NOW() - INTERVAL '30 days'
Then:

If >= 3 → add one cleaner_event:

event_type = 'inconvenience_high'

weight = -5

If >= 5 → add another:

Additional weight = -5 (total −10 from this dimension)

These appear in cleaner_events and are picked up by Reliability Score 2.0.

6.2 Client Risk (penalties from inconvenience)
Same concept, but for clients:

Consider logs where:

caused_by = 'client'

score >= 3

Last 14 days (tighter window to react faster)

Compute:

high_inconvenience_client_count =
  COUNT(*) WHERE caused_by='client' AND score >= 3 AND created_at > NOW() - INTERVAL '14 days'
Then:

If >= 3 → create client_risk_events row:

event_type = 'inconvenience_pattern'

weight = +5

If >= 5 → additional row:

weight = +5 (total +10)

This is exactly how we described earlier: patterns punish, not single events.

7. Backend workflow (how it actually runs)
7.1 On reschedule / cancel / no-show creation
When a reschedule or cancellation is created:

Capture reason_code from requester.

Store on reschedule_events or cancellation_events.

When the other party sees the updated status (accepted/declined/canceled):

Check if scenario qualifies for inconvenience prompt.

If yes, show UI with 1–4 scale.

7.2 When user submits inconvenience rating
Backend receives:

job_id, score, caused_by, related_event_type, related_event_id

Inserts into inconvenience_logs.

No immediate penalty or score change.

Changes will be picked up in daily scoring cron.

7.3 Daily scoring cron
Cron jobs (or Base44 scheduled flows) do:

Cleaner Reliability Update:

Query inconvenience_logs for caused_by='cleaner' & score>=3 in last 30 days.

For each cleaner crossing thresholds (3 or 5+), insert cleaner_events with weights.

Then recompute reliability scores.

Client Risk Update:

Query inconvenience_logs for caused_by='client' & score>=3 in last 14 days.

Insert client_risk_events for thresholds.

Recompute risk scores.

This matches everything we’ve already committed to.

8. UI experience (high-level)
You’ll design these screens later, but the engine expects:

8.1 Inconvenience prompt

“How inconvenient was this change?”

8.2 Reason selection

Why are you changing this booking?
[work conflict, family emergency, etc.]

Backend receives the code, not the label.

Thing we are building:

Client Reschedule UI Flow
This is the client-side experience for changing a booking date/time.
It needs to:

Be simple and reassuring

Make time windows & fees clear

Respect all our backend rules (mutual reschedule, decline → original time, etc.)

Nudge clients to keep the original time when they’re close to the 24h window

Plug into Risk, Reliability, and Cancellation engines without exposing the guts

I’ll break it into:

Flow overview (screens & states)

Detailed UX for each step

Edge cases (close to start time, high-risk client, no availability)

Data & events emitted from the UI

You can hand this to design + dev and it will map almost 1:1.

1. Client Reschedule Flow – Overview
Entry points:

From Job Details:
Button: Reschedule (primary or secondary CTA)

From Upcoming Jobs list:
Overflow menu item: Reschedule

Main states:

Select New Time

Confirm Changes (with policy info)

Pending Approval (if cleaner must accept)

Reschedule Accepted

Reschedule Declined → Next Step (keep or cancel)

2. Screen-by-Screen UX
2.1 Screen 1 – “Reschedule booking”
Goal: Let the client pick a new time and understand they’re making a request, not instant change (unless we decide to auto-accept).

Header:

Reschedule this cleaning

Subtext:

Choose a new date and time. Your cleaner will confirm the change.

Content:

Booking summary card

Cleaner name + avatar

Date & time (original)

Duration (e.g., 3 hours)

Job type (basic / deep / move-out)

Address

Date & time picker

Calendar (date)

Time slots (based on Cleaner Availability if we have it; otherwise all times but later filtered)

Optional tag “Recommended” next to times where cleaner is free

Inline policy hint (small text):

If >48h before start:

Changes are usually free when requested at least 48 hours in advance.

If 24–48h before start:

Changes within 24–48 hours are allowed, but late cancellations may still be charged a fee.

If <24h before start:

This change is close to your appointment time. If your cleaner can’t accept and you cancel, late cancellation fees may apply.

Reason dropdown (required)
Label: Why are you rescheduling?
Options:

My schedule changed

Work conflict

Family/personal reason

Need a different time

Home isn’t ready yet

Other

Primary CTA:

Request new time

Secondary CTA:

Cancel (go back to job details)

Events emitted when they tap Request new time:

UI → backend: create_reschedule_request with:

job_id

requested_by = client

t_start_new

reason_code

hours_before_original (computed backend)

Backend decides:

Is cleaner available?

Is auto-accept possible or does it go to pending?

2.2 Screen 2 – “Review and confirm” (optional or inline)
You can do this as a separate screen or a confirmation modal.

Copy example:

Confirm reschedule request
Your cleaning is currently scheduled for:
Thu, Mar 14 – 10:00 AM
You’re requesting to move it to:
Thu, Mar 14 – 3:00 PM

Then show:

Notice based on time window:

If >48h:

This change is free if your cleaner accepts. If they decline, your original time will remain.

If 24–48h:

This change is within 24–48 hours of your appointment.
• If your cleaner accepts: there’s no fee.
• If they decline and you cancel: a 50% late cancellation fee may apply (unless you use a grace cancellation).

If <24h:

This change is less than 24 hours before your appointment.
• If your cleaner accepts: there’s no fee.
• If they decline and you cancel instead of keeping the original time: a 100% late cancellation fee may apply (you may use a grace cancellation if available).

Show grace usage if they still have it:

You have 2 grace cancellations remaining that can waive late cancellation fees when used.

Buttons:

Send reschedule request (primary)

Back (secondary)

After submitting, go to Pending state.

2.3 Screen 3 – “Reschedule request sent” (Pending)
Header:

Reschedule request sent

Body content:

Status pill: Pending cleaner approval

Short explanation:

We’ve sent your new time to [Cleaner Name].
Your cleaning is still scheduled for [original date & time] until they accept.

Show both times:

Original time: Thu, Mar 14 – 10:00 AM
Requested time: Thu, Mar 14 – 3:00 PM

Small note:

If your cleaner declines your request, your booking will stay at the original time. If you can’t make the original time, you may cancel subject to our cancellation policy.

Buttons on this screen (or in Job Details view):

View booking details

(Optional) Cancel reschedule request (if we allow withdrawing pending requests)

In Job Details UI while pending:

Replace actions with:

Status: Reschedule pending

Text:

You’ve requested a new time. Your cleaner must accept before it changes.

Disable another reschedule request until resolved.

2.4 State: Reschedule Accepted
When cleaner accepts, client sees:

Banner on Job Details:

✅ New time confirmed
Your cleaner accepted your reschedule request.
New time: Thu, Mar 14 – 3:00 PM

Show a small “Changed from [old date/time]” text for clarity.

All references to job time update to t_start_new.

No mention of fees (because there are none).

We do not need to ask inconvenience score here unless you want a later prompt (this is more relevant on cleaner side for client-requested moves).

2.5 State: Reschedule Declined → Next Step
If cleaner declines the reschedule request, the client must clearly understand:

The original time is still active

Their options now (keep or cancel)

Potential fees if they cancel

Banner on Job Details:

❌ Reschedule request declined
Your cleaner can’t make the new time.
Your cleaning is still scheduled for:
Thu, Mar 14 – 10:00 AM

Actions shown:

Primary: Keep original time

Secondary: Cancel booking

Under Cancel booking, show small text with dynamic message:

If >48h before original start:

Canceling now is free.

If 24–48h:

Canceling now may incur a 50% late cancellation fee. You may use a grace cancellation if available.

If <24h:

Canceling now may incur a 100% late cancellation fee. You may use a grace cancellation if available.

Behavior:

Tap Keep original time → simply dismiss banner, booking remains as-is.

Tap Cancel booking → goes through Cancellation UI flow with full breakdown of fee/grace options.

3. Edge Cases & Smart UX
3.1 Client tries to reschedule very close to start (e.g., <2 hours)
You may want a stricter UX:

Show warning:

This booking is starting very soon. Your cleaner may already be on the way.
If they can’t accept and you cancel, a full late cancellation fee may apply.

Optionally, disallow reschedule within X minutes (e.g., 1 hour) and show:

Please contact support for last-minute changes, or you can cancel your booking (fees may apply).

This keeps chaos low.

3.2 No cleaner availability at new time
When client picks a time outside of cleaner availability:

Show inline message:

Your cleaner is not available at this time. Please choose a different time.

You can either:

Disable those time slots, OR

Let them tap and show a toast/modal:

That time isn’t available. Try another time.

We already use this in the backend “is_reasonable” logic.

3.3 High-risk client (internal behavior)
For now, we do not show the risk score, but we can alter the UX slightly:

For High/Critical risk clients, we might:

Restrict reschedule options <24h (e.g., only show Cancel instead of Reschedule), or

Show a stricter warning before allowing reschedule.

Example stricter message if risk is high:

Due to frequent last-minute changes, your rescheduling options may be limited. Canceling instead of attending may result in full fees.

This is optional; we’ve covered it in policy/engine, but not required at day one.

4. Data & events the UI must trigger
From the client reschedule flow, backend needs the following events:

Create reschedule request

Fired when client taps “Send reschedule request”

Payload:

job_id

requested_by = client

t_start_new

reason_code

(Backend calculates hours_before_original, bucket, is_reasonable, etc.)

Reschedule accepted / declined (received from backend)

UI observes job updates and shows correct banner + options.

Cancel booking after decline

When client taps Cancel booking after decline:

Trigger cancellation flow with:

job_id

triggered_by = client

Flag after_reschedule_declined = true

Keep original time

No API call needed (optional tracking event). Just dismiss/resume.

Telemetry / Analytics events (optional but recommended)

client_reschedule_requested

client_reschedule_accepted

client_reschedule_declined

client_cancel_after_decline

client_reschedule_abandoned (opened flow but didn’t submit)

2.4 Cleaner-side Inconvenience Prompt (FOR CONTRIBUTED SCORING, optional)

3. Edge Case Handling (Cleaner UX)
3.1 If cleaner has overlapping job at requested time
Backend determines availability. If they genuinely cannot make the requested time:

Auto-block accept button.

Message:

You are unavailable at the requested time. Please decline the request.

This protects cleaners and prevents accidents.

3.2 Cleaner wants to reschedule again
If client requested one time, cleaner can decline, but not initiate another reschedule (unless we explicitly allow a “counter-offer” system later).

For now:

If there's already a pending request or recent decline → disable “Request new time”.

3.3 Cleaner extremely close to the job time (e.g., <1 hour before)
We can disallow accept/decline entirely, marking it as:

This job is starting very soon.
Please contact the client or support if you have urgent issues.

Cleaner should still be able to check in / message client.

proceed

Thing we are building:

Inconvenience Score UI
(This is the shared UI used by both clients and cleaners after disruptive events.)

This system must be:

Lightweight (not intrusive)

Emotionally neutral (doesn’t feel like rating the person)

Clear about what the score means

Consistent across mobile & web

Tightly integrated with backend scoring logic AND your overall marketplace fairness model

This deliverable provides:

When & where the UI should appear

What the screen/modal should look like

Exact UX copy

Behavior rules

Event payload sent to backend

Side cases (skipped rating, spam prevention, repeated prompts)

🔥 1. When the Inconvenience Score UI Should Appear
It appears ONLY when the platform decides an event could cause disruption.

Trigger Events
Client last-minute reschedule (<48h) → shown to cleaner

Cleaner last-minute reschedule (<48h) → shown to client

Client cancellation within 48h → shown to cleaner

Cleaner cancellation within 48h → shown to client

No-shows

Cleaner no-show → shown to client

Client no-show → optional to show to cleaner (non-essential because no-show already triggers penalties)

Do NOT show inconvenience UI for:
Mutual reschedules >48h

Early cancellations >48h

Pattern-only events

Grace cancellation usage

Disputes (these have their own flow)

This prevents annoyance and preserves trust.

🔥 2. UI Format Options
There are two valid UX patterns:

A. Modal Prompt (recommended)
Appears as a small modal or bottom sheet

Pops up after the disruptive event is completed

Quick and frictionless

B. Inline Card (backup)
Appears inside Job Details page

Stays until user interacts or dismisses

Lower priority than a modal

We’ll use Modals for important cases, inline cards for lower-priority ones.

🔥 3. Screen Design & UX Copy
Below is the modal version, which is the primary version design should build.

Modal Header
How inconvenient was this change?

Description
This helps PureTask understand how schedule changes affect your day.
Your response won’t affect this booking, but it helps keep the platform fair for clients and cleaners.

This line is very important — it reduces fear.
We never imply this is a personal rating.

Rating Control (1–4 scale)
Option 1 — Horizontal buttons:

1   2   3   4
Not inconvenient                         Very inconvenient
Option 2 — Radio list with icons:

😌 1 – Not inconvenient

🙂 2 – Slight inconvenience

😕 3 – Moderate inconvenience

😣 4 – Very inconvenient

Use whatever aligns with your UI style.
Both work perfectly.

Optional text input
(Low friction; optional field)

Label:
Anything you'd like us to know? (optional)

This feeds metadata → internal only.

Primary Button
Submit

Secondary Button
Skip

Skipping is allowed.
Skipping submits no log.

🔥 4. Behavior Rules
4.1 Modal Timing
Modal appears 1–3 seconds after the event resolves:

Cleaner accepts client’s last-minute reschedule

Cleaner declines & client cancels

Cleaner cancels

Client cancels late

No-show resolution

If user is in the middle of another primary action → delay until idle.

4.2 User Interaction Rules
If they choose Submit → log to backend

If they choose Skip → do nothing

If they close the modal (X) → treat as Skip

We never show the modal again for that event

4.3 Don’t annoy users
Limit to:

Max 1 inconvenience prompt per job per user

Never show two in one session even if multiple events triggered

If user ignores 3 in a row → reduce frequency by 50% for next 30 days
(This can be done later — optional)

🔥 5. Data sent to backend (standard payload)
When user taps Submit:

{
  "job_id": number,
  "cleaner_id": number (if applicable),
  "client_id": number (if applicable),

  "caused_by": "client" | "cleaner",
  "rated_by": "client" | "cleaner",

  "score": 1 – 4,

  "related_event_id": number,
  "related_event_type": "reschedule" | "cancel" | "no_show",

  "reason_code": string (optional),
  "note": string (optional),

  "timestamp": now()
}
This perfectly lines up with the inconvenience_logs table we created.

(Shown to client)

Your cleaner canceled close to the appointment time.
How inconvenient was this for you?

CASE E — Cleaner no-show
(Shown to client)

Your cleaner did not arrive for the appointment.
This helps us hold cleaners accountable and improve reliability.

CASE F — Client no-show
(OPTIONAL for cleaner — usually default score is 4)

The client was unavailable at the time of the booking.
How inconvenient was this for you?

You may choose to auto-log “4” without showing UI for client no-shows — both approaches are valid.

Thing we are building:

Low Flexibility Badge UI
(Cleaner-facing + Client-facing UI that communicates cleaner flexibility in a clear, fair, and non-punitive way, tied to our backend logic.)

The Low Flexibility Badge is not a punishment.
It is a transparency badge that helps:

Set client expectations

Reduce friction

Improve matching accuracy

Explain reschedule limitations

Protect cleaners who prefer fixed, predictable schedules

It must be:

Respectful

Honest

Helpful

Subtle

Non-damaging

This deliverable defines:

When badge appears

Cleaner-side UI

Client-side UI

Matching algorithm UI tie-ins

Badge removal UI messaging

Backend metadata

Design components for Figma

🔥 1. Badge Purpose & Trigger Summary
When the badge appears:
Cleaner declines too many reasonable reschedule requests within the rolling window:

3+ declines in the last 30 days

AND declines were “unreasonable” based on:

Cleaner availability

Time window

Client pattern

Rescheduling rules

When the badge is removed:
Automatically falls off after:

30 days OR

10 clean jobs (no declines)

Whichever comes first

This keeps the system fresh and fair.

🔥 2. Cleaner-Side UI (How cleaner sees the badge)
Cleaners must see:

Why they got the badge

What it means

How to remove it

Your Scheduling Flexibility
If cleaner has the badge:

🔶 Badge Display

Label:

Flexibility: Low
Explanation Text:
You’ve declined several reschedule requests recently.
This may indicate that your schedule is less flexible than average.
Clients will see a small note so they know what to expect.

Removal hint:
This badge will be removed automatically after 30 days
or once you complete 10 jobs without declining a reasonable reschedule request.
Helpful tip:
Tip: Being flexible when possible can increase your rating,
tier progression, and available bookings.
Support link (optional):
Learn more about rescheduling rules

Cleaner WITHOUT the badge:
Flexibility: Normal
You handle reschedules well.
Clients will see normal availability expectations.

Flexibility: High
You've accepted most reschedule requests.
You may receive more recurring clients.
We don’t need to build this now, but it’s possible later.

🚀 Cleaner Availability System
(Backend + UI logic + rules + metadata. Tier 3 item.)

This is a critical support system because it powers:

“Reasonable vs unreasonable” reschedule logic

Whether a cleaner SHOULD accept a request

Whether a cleaner MUST NOT be penalized

Matching logic

Client-facing availability visuals

Future auto-assign features

Preventing accidental overbooking

This deliverable includes:

What the system must accomplish

Cleaner-facing availability UI

Data model

Backend logic

Integrations with reschedule + matching

Edge-case + conflict handling

API contract

🔥 1. What the Cleaner Availability System Must Do
A cleaner must be able to declare:

Days they work

Hours per day they work

Breaks / blocked times

One-time blackout periods

Travel radius

Job overlap rules

Job buffer times (optional future feature)

The system must:

Prevent scheduling conflict

Confirm whether reschedule requests are reasonable

Provide accurate availability slots for clients

Support recurring bookings (future feature)

Feed matching algorithm clean availability windows

🔥 2. Cleaner Availability: UI/UX Design
2.1 Cleaner Availability Home Screen
Header:

Your Availability
Subtext:

Set when you're available for bookings. Clients will only be shown the times you select.

2.2 Week Schedule Grid (Primary UI)
Structure:

Days of week: Mon → Sun

For each day: toggle ON/OFF

If ON → time range selector:

Example:

Monday

[ ON ] 9:00 AM – 5:00 PM

Add another block (+)

Tuesday

[ OFF ]

Wednesday

[ ON ] 10:00 AM – 7:00 PM

Cleaners may set multiple blocks per day:

Example:

9:00–12:00

2:00–6:00

2.3 One-Time Blackout Periods (Important)
Section:

Time Off / Exceptions
[ + Add Time Off ]
Popup:

Start date/time

End date/time

Reason (optional)

This is important for:

Holidays

Doctor appointments

Vacations

Emergencies

Blackout periods override weekly availability.

2.4 Travel Radius Input
Card:

Travel Radius
[ 10 miles ▼ ]
Tooltip:

This determines how far you’re willing to travel for bookings.

This matters later for matching.

2.5 Buffer Times (Future Optional)
Allow cleaner to set:

30 min buffer after each job
This prevents accidental double-booking.

We won’t fully implement buffers now, but the data model supports it.

🔥 3. Data Model
We need three main tables/entities:

3.1 cleaner_availability (weekly repeating rules)
cleaner_availability {
  id            serial primary key,
  cleaner_id    bigint references cleaners(id),
  day_of_week   int,   -- 0=Sun, 1=Mon, ... 6=Sat
  start_time    time,
  end_time      time,
  created_at    timestamp default now(),
  updated_at    timestamp default now()
}
Multiple rows per day are allowed.

3.2 cleaner_blackout_periods (one-time exceptions)
cleaner_blackout_periods {
  id            serial primary key,
  cleaner_id    bigint references cleaners(id),
  start_ts      timestamp,
  end_ts        timestamp,
  reason        text,
  created_at    timestamp default now()
}
3.3 cleaner_profile_settings
cleaner_profile_settings {
  cleaner_id           bigint primary key references cleaners(id),
  travel_radius_mi     int default 10,
  default_buffer_mins  int default 0,
  updated_at           timestamp
}
🔥 4. Backend Logic
4.1 Is cleaner available at time X?
is_cleaner_available(cleaner_id, requested_start, requested_end):
  1. Is day_of_week active?
  2. Does requested_start–end fall inside any availability block?
  3. Does it overlap with any existing job?
  4. Does it overlap with any blackout period?
  5. Does it violate buffer time?
Return:

available: true/false

reason: string (optional)

detail: { conflict_job_id, blackout_id }

4.2 Reasonable vs Unreasonable Reschedule
When a client requests a reschedule:

reasonable if:
  start_new is within cleaner availability AND
  cleaner has no conflict AND
  cleaner has no blackout AND
  change >= 24 hours OR cleaner is flexible

else:
  unreasonable
If request is “unreasonable,” the cleaner declining DOES NOT trigger:

Low Flexibility Badge

Reliability penalty

Any negative event

The availability system protects cleaners.

4.3 Matching Engine Integration
When showing cleaners to clients, matching uses:

match_score += bonus if requested_time within cleaner availability
match_score -= penalty if outside availability
exclude cleaner entirely if conflicting jobs or blackout
This increases booking success rate dramatically.

🔥 5. Edge Case Handling
5.1 Midnight-crossing jobs
If a job ends past midnight:

Compute availability based on actual timestamp, not day_of_week.

5.2 Multi-block days
If cleaner adds:

8 AM–12 PM

2 PM–6 PM

A 1 PM job would be invalid.
System must detect.

5.3 Partial overlaps
If a requested reschedule is:

3 PM–6 PM

Cleaner is available 2 PM–4 PM

System must detect as unreasonable automatically.

5.4 Blackout priority
Blackout ALWAYS overrides weekly rules.

If blackout is:

Monday 10 AM–1 PM

But weekly says “available all Monday”

Blackout wins.

🔥 6. API Contract
GET /cleaner/availability
Returns:

{
  weekly: [
    { day_of_week: 1, start_time: "09:00", end_time: "12:00" },
    ...
  ],
  blackouts: [
    { id: 10, start_ts: "...", end_ts: "...", reason: "Vacation" }
  ],
  settings: {
    travel_radius_mi: 10,
    buffer_mins: 15
  }
}
POST /cleaner/availability
Payload:

{
  day_of_week: 1,
  start_time: "09:00",
  end_time: "17:00"
}
POST /cleaner/blackout
{
  start_ts: "...",
  end_ts: "...",
  reason: "Doctor appointment"
}
GET /availability/check
Query:

cleaner_id
requested_start
requested_end
Response:

{
  available: true/false,
  reason: "...",
  conflict_job: {...},
  blackout: {...}
}
🔥 7. Client-Side Integration (search + reschedule)
Client sees only cleaner availability windows, not blackouts.
Client UI:

Cleaner availability:
Mon: 9 AM – 12 PM, 2 PM – 6 PM
Tue: Unavailable
...
Reschedule UI:

Time slots outside availability are disabled.

If inside availability but cleaner has a conflict → greyed out with tooltip: “Cleaner booked at this time.”

This prevents 95% of reschedule errors.

Cleaners expect:

The system protects them

They aren’t penalized for lacking flexibility

Their availability drives decisions

We already guarantee:

No penalty for declining outside-availability reschedules

No Flexibility Badge for “unreasonable” requests

Easy control over schedule

This makes cleaners trust PureTask.

0. Conventions
DB: PostgreSQL

Primary keys: bigserial

Timestamps: timestamptz

Foreign keys: bigint referencing parent tables

Soft deletes: not included by default (you can add deleted_at later)

I’ll only define new / extended tables relevant to these systems.

1. Core Entities (Clients, Cleaners, Jobs)
1.1 clients
CREATE TABLE clients (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  -- existing fields like name, email, phone, etc.

  grace_cancellations_total   int NOT NULL DEFAULT 2,
  grace_cancellations_used    int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
1.2 cleaners
CREATE TABLE cleaners (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  -- existing fields like name, email, phone, etc.

  reliability_score     numeric(5,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 70,
  reliability_tier      text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'Semi Pro', -- enum-like: Developing/Semi Pro/Pro/Elite

  flexibility_status    text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'normal', -- 'normal' | 'low' | 'high' (future)
  flexibility_badge_active boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
1.3 jobs
CREATE TABLE jobs (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  client_id             bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  cleaner_id            bigint REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  status                text NOT NULL, -- 'created','accepted','in_progress','completed','cancelled','no_show_client','no_show_cleaner'
  job_type              text NOT NULL, -- 'basic','deep','move_out', etc.

  start_time            timestamptz NOT NULL,
  end_time              timestamptz,
  duration_minutes      int,

  held_credits          int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
2. Scores & Events
2.1 client_risk_scores
CREATE TABLE client_risk_scores (
  client_id             bigint PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES clients(id),
  risk_score            numeric(5,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, -- 0-100
  risk_band             text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'normal',  -- 'normal','mild','elevated','high','critical'

  last_recomputed_at    timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
2.2 client_risk_events
CREATE TABLE client_risk_events (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  client_id             bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  job_id                bigint REFERENCES jobs(id),

  event_type            text NOT NULL,  -- 'late_reschedule_lt24', 'late_reschedule_pattern', 'cancel_24_48', ...
  weight                int NOT NULL,   -- +1, +3, +5, +10, +20
  metadata              jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_client_risk_events_client_time
  ON client_risk_events (client_id, created_at);
2.3 cleaner_events (for Reliability penalties/bonuses)
CREATE TABLE cleaner_events (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id            bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  job_id                bigint REFERENCES jobs(id),

  event_type            text NOT NULL,  -- 'late_reschedule','cancel_24_48','cancel_lt24','no_show','dispute_cleaner_at_fault','inconvenience_high','streak_bonus'
  weight                int NOT NULL,   -- negative for penalties, positive for bonuses
  metadata              jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_cleaner_events_cleaner_time
  ON cleaner_events (cleaner_id, created_at);
2.4 cleaner_metrics (aggregated window stats)
CREATE TABLE cleaner_metrics (
  cleaner_id                bigint PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  total_jobs_window         int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  attended_jobs             int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  no_show_jobs              int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  on_time_checkins          int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  photo_compliant_jobs      int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  communication_ok_jobs     int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  completion_ok_jobs        int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  ratings_sum               numeric(10,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  ratings_count             int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

  last_window_start         timestamptz,
  last_window_end           timestamptz,

  updated_at                timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
3. Reschedules, Cancellations, No-Shows
3.1 reason_codes
CREATE TABLE reason_codes (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  code                  text NOT NULL UNIQUE, -- e.g., 'client_schedule_conflict'
  actor_type            text NOT NULL,        -- 'client','cleaner','system','both'
  category              text NOT NULL,        -- 'reschedule','cancel','no_show','issue'
  label                 text NOT NULL,
  description           text NOT NULL,
  is_active             boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT true,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
3.2 reschedule_events
CREATE TABLE reschedule_events (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id                bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id),
  client_id             bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  cleaner_id            bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  requested_by          text NOT NULL, -- 'client' | 'cleaner'
  requested_to          text NOT NULL, -- opposite party
  t_request             timestamptz NOT NULL,
  t_start_original      timestamptz NOT NULL,
  t_start_new           timestamptz NOT NULL,

  hours_before_original numeric(8,2) NOT NULL,          -- computed at creation
  bucket                text NOT NULL,                  -- 'gt48','24_48','lt24'
  reason_code           text REFERENCES reason_codes(code),

  status                text NOT NULL,                  -- 'pending','accepted','declined','expired'
  declined_by           text,                           -- 'client' | 'cleaner'
  decline_reason_code   text REFERENCES reason_codes(code),

  is_reasonable         boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,

  metadata              jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_reschedules_job
  ON reschedule_events (job_id);

CREATE INDEX idx_reschedules_cleaner_time
  ON reschedule_events (cleaner_id, created_at);

CREATE INDEX idx_reschedules_client_time
  ON reschedule_events (client_id, created_at);
3.3 cancellation_events
CREATE TABLE cancellation_events (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id                bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id),

  cancelled_by          text NOT NULL,      -- 'client','cleaner','system'
  t_cancel              timestamptz NOT NULL,

  hours_before_start    numeric(8,2),
  bucket                text,              -- 'gt48','24_48','lt24','no_show'

  reason_code           text REFERENCES reason_codes(code),
  after_reschedule_declined boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,

  fee_pct               numeric(5,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, -- 0-100
  fee_credits           int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  refund_credits        int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

  cleaner_comp_credits  int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  platform_comp_credits int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

  grace_used            boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,

  metadata              jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_cancellations_job
  ON cancellation_events (job_id);

CREATE INDEX idx_cancellations_cancelled_by_time
  ON cancellation_events (cancelled_by, created_at);
4. Inconvenience & Patterns
4.1 inconvenience_logs
CREATE TABLE inconvenience_logs (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id                bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id),
  client_id             bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  cleaner_id            bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  caused_by             text NOT NULL, -- 'client' | 'cleaner'
  rated_by              text NOT NULL, -- 'client' | 'cleaner'
  score                 int NOT NULL,  -- 1..4

  related_event_type    text NOT NULL, -- 'reschedule','cancel','no_show','issue'
  related_event_id      bigint,        -- FK into reschedule_events or cancellation_events (not enforced but implied)

  reason_code           text,          -- optional, matches reason_codes.code
  note                  text,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_inconvenience_cleaner_time
  ON inconvenience_logs (cleaner_id, created_at);

CREATE INDEX idx_inconvenience_client_time
  ON inconvenience_logs (client_id, created_at);
No need for extra pattern table; pattern thresholds use queries over this.

5. Availability, Flexibility, Badges
5.1 cleaner_availability
CREATE TABLE cleaner_availability (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id            bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  day_of_week           int NOT NULL, -- 0..6 (Sun..Sat)
  start_time            time NOT NULL,
  end_time              time NOT NULL,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_cleaner_availability_cleaner_day
  ON cleaner_availability (cleaner_id, day_of_week);
5.2 cleaner_blackout_periods
CREATE TABLE cleaner_blackout_periods (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id            bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  start_ts              timestamptz NOT NULL,
  end_ts                timestamptz NOT NULL,
  reason                text,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_cleaner_blackouts_cleaner_time
  ON cleaner_blackout_periods (cleaner_id, start_ts, end_ts);
5.3 cleaner_profile_settings
CREATE TABLE cleaner_profile_settings (
  cleaner_id            bigint PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  travel_radius_mi      int NOT NULL DEFAULT 10,
  buffer_minutes        int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
5.4 badge_assignments
Use generic badge table (can also support future badges like “Elite”, “Top Rated”, etc.)

CREATE TABLE badge_assignments (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id            bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  badge_type            text NOT NULL, -- 'low_flexibility','elite','top_rated',...
  is_active             boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT true,

  assigned_at           timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  removed_at            timestamptz,

  metadata              jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb
);

CREATE INDEX idx_badges_cleaner_type
  ON badge_assignments (cleaner_id, badge_type, is_active);
Low Flexibility Badge is one badge_type here, even if we also store flexibility_status for quick lookup.

6. Matching Metadata (Optional but Powerful)
6.1 match_recommendations (for logging only)
CREATE TABLE match_recommendations (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id                bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id),
  client_id             bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  cleaner_id            bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  match_score           numeric(6,3) NOT NULL,
  rank                  int NOT NULL,

  generated_at          timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_match_recommendations_job
  ON match_recommendations (job_id);

CREATE INDEX idx_match_recommendations_cleaner
  ON match_recommendations (cleaner_id);
Useful for debugging and future ML.
