Here’s how I’d define both of these so we’re on the same page before we actually build them.

1️⃣ Engineering Implementation Plan
(roadmap of migrations, feature flags, rollout order)

This is the “how do we ship this safely in code + DB” document.

It usually includes:

A. Phases / Milestones
A top-level breakdown like:

Phase 0 – Prep & scaffolding

Add new columns/tables (risk, reliability, events, availability)

No behavior changes yet, purely additive

Phase 1 – Passive logging

Start writing events (reschedule, cancellations, inconvenience)

Scores not shown in UI yet

Phase 2 – Score computation

Cron jobs / workers to compute risk & reliability

Internal dashboards only

Phase 3 – Soft UI rollout

Show score breakdown to cleaners

Start using scores in matching as a small weight

Phase 4 – Full policy enforcement

Risk-based restrictions

Grace logic tied in

Prepayment requirements, etc.

Phase 5 – Optimization & cleanup

Remove old legacy fields/policies

Tighten indexes, performance tuning

B. Database Migrations Plan
For each feature / table:

What new tables/columns get added

Migration scripts (e.g. 001_add_client_risk_scores.sql)

Default values / backfill strategy (how to initialize scores for existing data)

Indexing strategy for rolling-window queries

Example bullets:

Add client_risk_scores & client_risk_events

Add cleaner_events, cleaner_metrics

Add reschedule_events, cancellation_events

Add inconvenience_logs, cleaner_availability, etc.

C. Feature Flags / Toggles
A list of switches you can turn on/off to roll out in stages:

flag_enable_reliability_score_v2

flag_show_cleaner_score_breakdown_ui

flag_enable_client_risk_based_matching

flag_enforce_prepaid_for_high_risk_clients

flag_enable_inconvenience_prompt

For each flag:

Where it’s checked (API, frontend, jobs)

What “off” behavior is (legacy behavior)

Rollout strategy (internal → beta users → all users)

D. Service / Code Changes
For each service (API, worker, cron, notifications):

New endpoints (e.g. /cleaner/availability, /scores/recompute)

New business logic (reschedule/cancellation engines)

New scheduled jobs:

recompute client_risk_scores daily

recompute cleaner.reliability_score daily

This part answers: who writes what code and where.

E. Rollout Order & Risk Mitigation
For each phase:

Prereqs (DB migration X must be live before job Y)

What can go wrong (e.g., miscalculated scores, wrong fees)

Monitoring / metrics:

reschedules, # cancellations, average scores, error rates
Rollback plan:

Turn off feature flags

Revert scoring to legacy behavior

Keep raw events data for recovery

F. QA & Testing Plan
Unit tests (engines: cancellation, reschedule, scoring)

Integration tests (end-to-end booking → reschedule → cancel)

Staging scenarios:

Fake high-risk client

Fake unreliable cleaner

Verify UI behavior and no money misrouting

2️⃣ Base44 / n8n Workflow Map
(how data gets populated & updated in real time)

This is the automation blueprint: which workflows fire on which events, and what they do with the DB.

Think of it as the “wiring diagram” for:

“User rescheduled job” → log reschedule_event → adjust scores later

“Client canceled late” → write cancellation_event → move credits → log risk_event

A. Event Sources (Triggers)
List of events that start workflows, for example:

job_created

job_accepted

job_checked_in

job_checked_out

job_completed

job_reschedule_requested

job_reschedule_accepted / declined

job_cancelled

job_no_show_client / cleaner

inconvenience_rating_submitted

Each event will trigger:

A Base44/n8n flow

OR an HTTP webhook handler that then calls Base44/n8n

B. Core Workflows
You’ll have a workflow group for each subsystem:

Reliability Score Workflows

On job completion: update cleaner_metrics

On cleaner cancel/no-show: insert cleaner_events

Nightly: recompute cleaners.reliability_score

Client Risk Workflows

On client late cancel: insert client_risk_events

On client no-show: insert high-weight event

On pattern detection (3 late reschedules in 14 days): insert late_reschedule_pattern

Nightly: recompute client_risk_scores

Reschedule Workflows

On reschedule request: create reschedule_events row; evaluate reasonable/unreasonable

On accept: update job time; create events for risk/reliability if needed

On decline: mark reschedule_event declined; flag for potential cancellation follow-up

Cancellation Workflows

On cancellation request: compute bucket, fee%, grace usage

Adjust credits (client refund + cleaner comp + platform share)

Insert cancellation_events

Insert risk/reliability events

Inconvenience Workflows

On inconvenience submission: insert inconvenience_logs

Daily: run counts per client/cleaner; insert pattern events (into risk/cleaner_events)

Availability Workflows

When cleaner updates availability: store in cleaner_availability & blackouts

On reschedule/matching: call availability logic (could be in code; automation just orchestrates)

C. Workflow Structure (Typical Node Sequences)
For each workflow, a typical n8n/Base44 flow looks like:

Trigger node

Webhook or event from app/backend

Load job/client/cleaner data

Database node / API call

Decision / logic node

If <24h, else 24–48h, else >48h

If grace remaining

If risk band High/Critical

Write event/score rows

Insert into *_events tables

Update jobs, clients, cleaners, scores tables

Side effects

Send notifications (e.g. “Reschedule requested”, “Booking cancelled with fee X”)

Enqueue recompute or run inline

Logging / monitoring

Write logs to an audit table or external tool

D. Real-time vs Batch Workflows
You’ll separate:

Real-time flows (blocking UX)

Cancellation fee calculation, credit movement

Reschedule acceptance/decline

Creating events

Batch flows (cron-based)

Nightly risk recompute

Nightly reliability recompute

Pattern detection (e.g. 3+ late reschedules in 14 days)

The workflow map will explicitly say:

Which flows run immediately on user actions

Which flows run on schedule (e.g. 2 AM daily)

E. Error Handling & Idempotency
Workflow map also defines:

What happens if a flow fails mid-way:

Do we retry?

Do we queue the event?

Idempotency:

Ensure “job_cancelled” event doesn’t double-charge if retried

Use unique keys or “processed” flags per job/event

F. Monitoring & Admin Tools
Finally, the map calls out:

Flows that send metrics:

of cancellations/day
of reschedules/day
Average risk & reliability

Admin tools:

Manual score override flow

Manual badge toggle

Manual event insertion/rollback

TL;DR Difference Between the Two
Engineering Implementation Plan
= When and how we change the codebase + database, in what order, with flags and rollouts and testing.

Base44 / n8n Workflow Map
= How events move through the system, which flows fire, what they read/write, and how real-time scoring & policy logic actually executes.

We absolutely should do both:

Implementation plan → keeps the platform stable as we ship.

Workflow map → ensures every user action (reschedule, cancel, no-show, etc.) actually hits the right tables & scores.

When you’re ready, I can start with Engineering Implementation Plan first (phases, migrations, flags, order), then do the Base44/n8n workflow map right after.

✅ ITEM 1 OF 10 — Full Release Phases Overview
(The master roadmap of how PureTask ships the entire Risk/Reschedule/Reliability system safely)

This is the high-level engineering plan that ensures:

No broken behavior

No untested scoring penalties

No accidental overcharging

Zero downtime

Smooth rollout for cleaners & clients

Ability to rollback instantly

This is the same type of phased rollout companies like Uber, DoorDash, and Airbnb use for major behavior-changing features.

🚀 PHASE 0 — PREP & SCAFFOLDING (Week 1–2)
No behavior changes. No UI changes. No scores shown.
Only additive backend changes.

Tasks:
Create all new DB tables:

client_risk_scores

client_risk_events

cleaner_events

cleaner_metrics

reschedule_events

cancellation_events

inconvenience_logs

cleaner_availability

cleaner_blackout_periods

badge_assignments

cleaner_profile_settings

Add new columns to existing tables:

cleaners.reliability_score

cleaners.reliability_tier

cleaners.flexibility_status

clients.grace_cancellations_used

Add indexes (no logic yet).

Add feature flags (OFF by default).

Stub endpoints (return mock data, not real logic).

Internal QA:
Ensure migrations run cleanly in staging.

Ensure no old functionality breaks.

🚀 PHASE 1 — PASSIVE LOGGING (Week 2–4)
The platform starts recording events but does not use them yet.

Tasks:
For every reschedule → write a row in reschedule_events

For every cancellation → write row in cancellation_events

For every inconvenience score → write row in inconvenience_logs

For every punctuality/photo/communication event → write row in cleaner_events

For every late cancellation → write row in client_risk_events

Absolutely NO visible behavior changes yet.
Internal QA:
Ensure all events appear in DB

Ensure no duplicate writing

Validate timestamps & metadata

🚀 PHASE 2 — SCORING ENGINES (Week 4–6)
Now that events are logging, we turn on computation — but NOT UI visibility yet.

Tasks:
Implement Risk Score calculation engine

Nightly recompute

Band assignment logic

Implement Reliability Score 2.0 calculation engine

Weighted metric scoring

Rolling window

Tier logic

Flexibility badge logic

Store results in:

client_risk_scores

cleaners.reliability_score

cleaners.reliability_tier

Add system logs & analytics dashboards.

Feature flag:
flag_enable_score_recompute_engine = ON

Internal QA:
Compare scores vs expected values

Test rolling window logic

Test penalty decay

🚀 PHASE 3 — SOFT UI ROLLOUT (Week 6–8)
Now that scores work internally, we show the UI in a read-only manner.

Tasks:
Show Cleaner Score Breakdown UI (read-only)

Show Client Reliability/Grace breakdown UI (read-only)

DO NOT enforce policies yet.

Add informational tooltips:

“Scores update nightly.”

“This does not affect any booking behavior yet.”

Feature flags:
flag_show_cleaner_scores = ON for 5%

flag_show_client_grace_ui = ON for 5%

Gradual rollout to 100%.
Internal QA:
Ensure zero policy enforcement

Ensure UI shows correct & consistent data

🚀 PHASE 4 — FULL POLICY ENFORCEMENT (Week 8–12)
This is where the platform begins to use:

Risk score

Reliability score

Availability

Reschedule rules

Cancellation fees

Grace logic

Reasonable/unreasonable logic

Prepayment requirements

Tasks:
A. ENABLE SCORING-BASED BEHAVIOR:
Late cancellation fees enforced

Late reschedule penalties applied

Cleaner protections applied

Client risk → limitations

High-risk clients → forced prepayment

Low flexibility badge visible on profiles

Availability conflict detection active

Reschedules auto-decline if unreasonable

B. UPDATE MATCHING ENGINE:
Lower ranking for high-risk clients

Higher ranking for high-reliability cleaners

Exclude Elite cleaners from high-risk clients

Availability-based filtering

Feature flags:
flag_enforce_cancellation_policy = ON

flag_enforce_reschedule_policy = ON

flag_enable_risk_based_matching = ON

flag_enable_prepayment_for_high_risk = ON

Rollout incrementally:

5%

25%

50%

100%

Internal QA:
Verify money movements

Verify event logging

Verify policies enforced correctly

🚀 PHASE 5 — OPTIMIZATION & CLEANUP (Week 12–14)
After everything is stable:

Tasks:
Remove legacy cancellation logic

Remove legacy reschedule logic

Remove unused columns

Index optimization

Add caching for availability queries

Performance tuning

Improve matching weights

Train ML model (optional future)

✅ ITEM 2 OF 10 — Database Migration Plan
(Ordered list of migrations, what each does, and how to roll them out safely)

This is the step-by-step DB change sequence to support everything we designed, without breaking the current app.

I’ll assume Postgres and a standard migration system (Knex, Prisma, Sequelize, raw SQL, etc.).
You can adapt filenames, but the order should stay roughly like this.

🔢 Migration Sequence Overview
I’ll name them like 001_..., 002_... etc.
Each item = one migration file (or a small group if you prefer).

001 – Add core score scaffolding
002 – Add risk event logging tables
003 – Add reliability event logging tables
004 – Add reschedule & cancellation tables
005 – Add inconvenience logs + reason codes
006 – Add availability + blackout + settings
007 – Add badges table
008 – Backfill initial defaults for existing users
009 – Add basic indexes for performance
010 – (Later) cleanup legacy fields (AFTER full rollout)
I’ll break each down now.

001_add_core_score_scaffolding.sql
Goal: Add the main score fields/tables with minimal risk.

Changes:

Extend clients:

ALTER TABLE clients
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS grace_cancellations_total int NOT NULL DEFAULT 2,
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS grace_cancellations_used  int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0;
Extend cleaners:

ALTER TABLE cleaners
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS reliability_score  numeric(5,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 70,
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS reliability_tier   text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'Semi Pro',
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS flexibility_status text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'normal',
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS flexibility_badge_active boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false;
Create client_risk_scores:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS client_risk_scores (
  client_id          bigint PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES clients(id),
  risk_score         numeric(5,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  risk_band          text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'normal',
  last_recomputed_at timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
Backward compatibility:
All new fields have safe defaults. No behavior change yet.

002_add_client_risk_events.sql
Goal: Start capturing client behavior events.

Changes:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS client_risk_events (
  id          bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  client_id   bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  job_id      bigint REFERENCES jobs(id),
  event_type  text NOT NULL,
  weight      int  NOT NULL,
  metadata    jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,
  created_at  timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
Indexes:

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_client_risk_events_client_time
  ON client_risk_events (client_id, created_at);
No logic yet; just table.

003_add_cleaner_events_and_metrics.sql
Goal: Enable Reliability Score 2.0 inputs.

Changes:

cleaner_events:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_events (
  id          bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id  bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  job_id      bigint REFERENCES jobs(id),
  event_type  text NOT NULL,
  weight      int  NOT NULL,
  metadata    jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,
  created_at  timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_events_cleaner_time
  ON cleaner_events (cleaner_id, created_at);
cleaner_metrics:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_metrics (
  cleaner_id            bigint PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  total_jobs_window     int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  attended_jobs         int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  no_show_jobs          int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  on_time_checkins      int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  photo_compliant_jobs  int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  communication_ok_jobs int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  completion_ok_jobs    int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  ratings_sum           numeric(10,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  ratings_count         int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

  last_window_start     timestamptz,
  last_window_end       timestamptz,
  updated_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
004_add_reschedules_and_cancellations.sql
Goal: Persist reschedules and cancellations as first-class entities.

Changes:

reason_codes (shared):

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS reason_codes (
  id          bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  code        text NOT NULL UNIQUE,
  actor_type  text NOT NULL,
  category    text NOT NULL,
  label       text NOT NULL,
  description text NOT NULL,
  is_active   boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT true,
  created_at  timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at  timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
reschedule_events:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS reschedule_events (
  id                    bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id                bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id),
  client_id             bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  cleaner_id            bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  requested_by          text NOT NULL,
  requested_to          text NOT NULL,
  t_request             timestamptz NOT NULL,
  t_start_original      timestamptz NOT NULL,
  t_start_new           timestamptz NOT NULL,

  hours_before_original numeric(8,2) NOT NULL,
  bucket                text NOT NULL,
  reason_code           text REFERENCES reason_codes(code),

  status                text NOT NULL,
  declined_by           text,
  decline_reason_code   text REFERENCES reason_codes(code),

  is_reasonable         boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,
  metadata              jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,

  created_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at            timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_reschedules_job
  ON reschedule_events (job_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_reschedules_cleaner_time
  ON reschedule_events (cleaner_id, created_at);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_reschedules_client_time
  ON reschedule_events (client_id, created_at);
cancellation_events:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cancellation_events (
  id                      bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id                  bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id),

  cancelled_by            text NOT NULL,
  t_cancel                timestamptz NOT NULL,

  hours_before_start      numeric(8,2),
  bucket                  text,

  reason_code             text REFERENCES reason_codes(code),
  after_reschedule_declined boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,

  fee_pct                 numeric(5,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  fee_credits             int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  refund_credits          int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  cleaner_comp_credits    int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  platform_comp_credits   int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  grace_used              boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,

  metadata                jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,
  created_at              timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cancellations_job
  ON cancellation_events (job_id);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cancellations_cancelled_by_time
  ON cancellation_events (cancelled_by, created_at);
005_add_inconvenience_logs.sql
Goal: Enable the Inconvenience Score System.

Changes:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS inconvenience_logs (
  id                 bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id             bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id),
  client_id          bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  cleaner_id         bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  caused_by          text NOT NULL,  -- 'client' | 'cleaner'
  rated_by           text NOT NULL,  -- 'client' | 'cleaner'
  score              int  NOT NULL,  -- 1..4

  related_event_type text NOT NULL,  -- 'reschedule','cancel','no_show','issue'
  related_event_id   bigint,

  reason_code        text,
  note               text,

  created_at         timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_inconvenience_cleaner_time
  ON inconvenience_logs (cleaner_id, created_at);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_inconvenience_client_time
  ON inconvenience_logs (client_id, created_at);
006_add_cleaner_availability_and_blackouts.sql
Goal: Support availability & time-off.

Changes:

cleaner_availability:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_availability (
  id          bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id  bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  day_of_week int NOT NULL, -- 0..6
  start_time  time NOT NULL,
  end_time    time NOT NULL,

  created_at  timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at  timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_availability_cleaner_day
  ON cleaner_availability (cleaner_id, day_of_week);
cleaner_blackout_periods:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_blackout_periods (
  id          bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id  bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  start_ts    timestamptz NOT NULL,
  end_ts      timestamptz NOT NULL,
  reason      text,

  created_at  timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cleaner_blackouts_cleaner_time
  ON cleaner_blackout_periods (cleaner_id, start_ts, end_ts);
cleaner_profile_settings:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_profile_settings (
  cleaner_id        bigint PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  travel_radius_mi  int NOT NULL DEFAULT 10,
  buffer_minutes    int NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  created_at        timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at        timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
007_add_badge_assignments.sql
Goal: Support Low Flexibility + future badges.

Changes:

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS badge_assignments (
  id          bigserial PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id  bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),

  badge_type  text NOT NULL, -- 'low_flexibility','top_rated','elite',...
  is_active   boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT true,

  assigned_at timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  removed_at  timestamptz,

  metadata    jsonb NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_badges_cleaner_type
  ON badge_assignments (cleaner_id, badge_type, is_active);
008_backfill_initial_defaults.sql
Goal: Initialize new tables/fields for existing data.

This can be run as:

A SQL script, or

A background job (if you have millions of rows)

Examples:

Initialize client_risk_scores for all existing clients:

INSERT INTO client_risk_scores (client_id, risk_score, risk_band)
SELECT id, 0, 'normal'
FROM clients
ON CONFLICT (client_id) DO NOTHING;
Initialize cleaner_metrics:

INSERT INTO cleaner_metrics (cleaner_id)
SELECT id FROM cleaners
ON CONFLICT (cleaner_id) DO NOTHING;
Initialize cleaner_profile_settings:

INSERT INTO cleaner_profile_settings (cleaner_id)
SELECT id FROM cleaners
ON CONFLICT (cleaner_id) DO NOTHING;
Optional:
If you have historical jobs, you can run a backfill cron to populate metrics/events gradually.

009_add_additional_indexes_and_constraints.sql
Goal: Add performance-critical indexes once data exists.

Examples:

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_jobs_client_time
  ON jobs (client_id, start_time);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_jobs_cleaner_time
  ON jobs (cleaner_id, start_time);
You can also add partial indexes later as you profile queries.

010_cleanup_legacy_fields.sql (run much later)
Goal: Remove old / unused legacy columns after successful rollout.

Examples (only after you’re 100% sure):

-- Example only if you had old score fields:
-- ALTER TABLE cleaners DROP COLUMN old_reliability_score;
-- ALTER TABLE clients DROP COLUMN old_behavior_flags;
This migration is endgame, not part of initial shipping.

🧯 Rollback Strategy for Migrations
Each migration is additive (Phase 0–2).

If something goes wrong:

Temporarily disable features via feature flags.

You usually DO NOT roll back tables, just stop using them.

For catastrophic DB issues:

Use normal DB restore / backup strategy (snapshot restore).

We keep all new tables as “shadow systems” until we’re confident.

✅ ITEM 3 OF 10 — Feature Flag Architecture
Goal: define all the switches we’ll use to roll this out safely, plus what each one controls, and what “ON/OFF” means in practice.

Think of these as:

Kill switches if something misbehaves

Dials to gradually roll out behavior & UI

Guardrails while we test in production

I’ll group flags into 5 categories:

Scoring engines

UI / UX

Policy enforcement

Matching behavior

Experimental / extra controls

You don’t have to implement every single one as a separate flag; we can group some if you want. I’m intentionally being granular so you have control.

3.1 Scoring Engine Flags
These govern behind-the-scenes computation, not visible UI.

FF1 – enable_risk_score_engine
Purpose: Turn on/off the nightly/batch job that computes client_risk_scores from client_risk_events.

Used in (backend):

Risk recompute cron

Any service that writes to client_risk_scores

When OFF:

We still log client_risk_events (from Item 2), but:

client_risk_scores is either zero/unchanged

Any code that reads client_risk_scores should treat missing/zero as normal.

When ON:

Nightly job updates client_risk_scores and risk_band.

Risk bands become reliable input for other flags (matching, UI, etc.).

FF2 – enable_reliability_score_engine
Purpose: Control Reliability Score 2.0 recompute engine.

Used in (backend):

Cron/worker that computes cleaners.reliability_score & reliability_tier from cleaner_metrics + cleaner_events.

When OFF:

You may keep legacy scoring, or hold scores at default (70 / Semi Pro).

cleaner_events/cleaner_metrics still log, but no one trusts the score yet.

When ON:

New Reliability 2.0 takes effect.

All reads of cleaners.reliability_score become meaningful.

3.2 UI / UX Flags
These control what users can see, not behavior.

FF3 – show_cleaner_reliability_breakdown_ui
Purpose: Show or hide the Cleaner Score Breakdown UI.

Used in (frontend):

Cleaner profile / dashboard screen

When OFF:

Cleaners don’t see detailed breakdown; maybe just a basic label or nothing.

When ON:

Cleaners see:

Reliability score

Tier

Breakdown by attendance, punctuality, photos, etc.

Penalties list

Improvement tips

FF4 – show_client_booking_reliability_ui
Purpose: Show/hide Client’s grace usage & cancellation policy breakdown.

Used in (frontend):

Client account / “Booking Reliability” section

Job cancellation screens

When OFF:

Client sees generic “cancellation policy” text only.

When ON:

Client sees:

Grace cancellations remaining

Recent late cancels/reschedules

Clear fee rules in-context.

FF5 – show_inconvenience_prompt_ui
Purpose: Show/hide the Inconvenience Score modal (1–4 scale).

When OFF:

No inconvenience prompt is shown to either side.

Backend may still accept data (if you test manually), but normal flow never triggers it.

When ON:

After disruptive events (late reschedule/cancel/no-show), the modal shows and logs inconvenience_logs.

FF6 – show_low_flexibility_badge_ui
Purpose: Control visibility of the Low Flexibility badge.

When OFF:

We may still compute & store flexibility data in backend.

But clients do not see “Fixed Times Preferred”, and cleaners don’t see the badge label.

When ON:

Cleaner sees their own flexibility section.

Clients see “Fixed Times Preferred” note on cleaner profile & cards.

FF7 – show_risk_based_warnings_ui
Purpose: Show/hide high-risk client warnings (without changing behavior).

When OFF:

No special banners or “your options may be limited” messages.

When ON:

Client sees “Schedule Change Reminder” / “Limited rescheduling” copy.

Cleaner sees “High change frequency” tags on certain jobs.

Behavior itself is still controlled by separate enforcement flags; this just controls messaging.

3.3 Policy Enforcement Flags
These actually change business logic (fees, restrictions, penalties).

FF8 – enforce_new_cancellation_policy
Purpose: Turn on the new fee rules + grace logic.

When OFF:

Keep legacy cancellation behavior (whatever you have today).

New cancellation_events table can still be logged for analysis.

When ON:

Use:

0% >48h

50% 24–48h

100% <24h

Apply grace cancellations rules.

Move credits according to the new fee split (client refund, cleaner comp, platform).

FF9 – enforce_reschedule_policy
Purpose: Enforce the new rescheduling rules:

Mutually accepted = free, no fees

Declined → original time stands

If client then cancels → cancellation policy applies

Reasonable vs unreasonable based on availability

Late reschedules log events & may impact risk/reliability.

When OFF:

Reschedule logic may remain loose/legacy.

You can still log reschedule_events for testing.

When ON:

Full new flow is live:

reschedule_events used for decisions

Reasonable/unreasonable respected

Late reschedules affect risk/reliability.

FF10 – enforce_inconvenience_patterns
Purpose: Enable use of inconvenience patterns to modify scores.

When OFF:

Inconvenience scores are logged, but they don’t create cleaner_events or client_risk_events.

When ON:

Pattern detection jobs:

For clients: inconvenience_pattern risk events (+5/+10).

For cleaners: inconvenience_high events (−5/−10 to reliability).

FF11 – enforce_reliability_penalties
Purpose: Actually apply penalty events to Reliability Score 2.0 in a meaningful way.

When OFF:

cleaner_events may still log, but their weights don’t affect the score (or are ignored in the compute engine).

When ON:

Late reschedules, late cancels, no-shows, disputes, inconvenience patterns → all affect the computed reliability.

You can turn this on after validating the numbers for a while in read-only mode.

FF12 – enforce_client_risk_restrictions
Purpose: Use risk bands to restrict behavior.

When OFF:

Risk bands exist but don’t affect what clients can do.

When ON:

High/Critical clients:

Reduced reschedule options

Stricter cancellation leniency

Possibly blocked from Elite cleaners, etc.

FF13 – enforce_prepayment_for_high_risk
Purpose: Require prepayment / credit hold for high-risk clients.

When OFF:

All clients follow same payment flow.

When ON:

High-risk clients:

Must hold enough credits before confirming bookings.

See special “Prepayment Required” UI.

3.4 Matching Behavior Flags
These control how scores impact who gets shown / recommended.

FF14 – enable_score_based_matching
Purpose: Start using reliability score & tiers in the matching algorithm.

When OFF:

Matching may be simple: distance + availability only.

When ON:

Matching uses:

reliability_score

tier

distance score

history score, etc.

FF15 – enable_risk_aware_matching
Purpose: Make matching aware of client risk band.

When OFF:

High-risk clients see same cleaner pool as normal.

When ON:

High-risk clients:

Less likely to see Elite

More likely to match with certain cleaner segments

Cleaners see warning tags.

FF16 – enable_flexibility_aware_matching
Purpose: Make matching aware of Low Flexibility badge and client behavior.

When OFF:

Flexibility doesn’t influence ordering.

When ON:

High-risk / frequent-changer clients are less likely to be matched with low-flex cleaners.

3.5 Experimental / Advanced Flags
These are optional but useful:

FF17 – show_experimental_hints_ui
Purpose: Enable advanced hints like “Do X to reach Elite in 2 jobs.”

When OFF: Keep hints basic.

When ON: Use more experimental messaging.

FF18 – log_score_debug_info
Purpose: Extra logging/debug around score calculation.

When OFF: Normal log level.

When ON: Writes extra info per compute (for internal debugging only).

3.6 Recommended Rollout Strategy With Flags
Here’s how I’d sequence flipping them:

Phase 1 (Passive logging)

Turn ON:

enable_risk_score_engine (optional)

enable_reliability_score_engine

Keep all enforcement & UI flags OFF.

Phase 2 (Internal scoring only)

Turn ON:

log_score_debug_info

Still keep all UI & enforcement flags OFF.

Phase 3 (Soft UI)

Gradually turn ON:

show_cleaner_reliability_breakdown_ui

show_client_booking_reliability_ui

show_inconvenience_prompt_ui (maybe for 10–20% first)

show_low_flexibility_badge_ui (after data stable)

show_risk_based_warnings_ui

Phase 4 (Behavior)

Gradually turn ON:

enforce_new_cancellation_policy

enforce_reschedule_policy

enforce_inconvenience_patterns

enforce_reliability_penalties

enforce_client_risk_restrictions

enforce_prepayment_for_high_risk

enable_score_based_matching

enable_risk_aware_matching

enable_flexibility_aware_matching

Any catastrophic weirdness? → Flip all enforcement flags OFF, keep logging & scores for diagnosis.

✅ ITEM 3 STATUS: COMPLETE
We now have:

A full feature flag map

Clear ON/OFF behavior for each

Grouping by theme (scoring, UI, enforcement, matching)

A practical rollout sequence

✅ ITEM 4 OF 10 — Backend Services to Modify
Goal: spell out exactly which backend areas need changes, what each will be responsible for, and how they connect to the new tables, scores, and policies.

I’ll assume a fairly standard structure (even if in your code it’s monolithic, these can be modules):

Job / Booking Service

Scheduling & Reschedule Service

Cancellation / Payments Service

Scoring Service (Risk + Reliability)

Availability Service

Matching / Search Service

User Profile Service (Client + Cleaner)

Notifications Service

Admin / Support Tools

You can map these to actual files/services/routes later.

1️⃣ Job / Booking Service
What it handles today (likely):

Creating jobs/bookings

Assigning cleaners (directly or via matching)

Changing job status (created → accepted → in_progress → completed)

Basic credit escrow logic

New responsibilities:

Write job IDs into all downstream systems:

On job creation → base record for events (risk, reliability, reschedule, cancel)

Emit events to other services / Base44:

job_created

job_accepted

job_checked_in

job_checked_out

job_completed

job_marked_no_show_client

job_marked_no_show_cleaner

Direct DB interactions with new tables:

None heavy, mostly:

Provide job_id, client_id, cleaner_id, start_time, held_credits to other services.

Key changes:

All job mutations must be event-driven enough that Reschedule, Cancellation, Scoring workflows can hook in cleanly.

Job status transitions must be strict, so cancellation & no-show logic is reliable.

2️⃣ Scheduling & Reschedule Service
New core responsibilities:

Handle:

POST /jobs/:id/reschedule/request

POST /jobs/:id/reschedule/respond (accept/decline)

Enforce:

Mutual reschedules only (accepted → change time, else not)

Reasonable vs unreasonable rules (uses Availability Service)

Write:

reschedule_events rows

Call:

Scoring Service (to log risk/reliability events for late reschedules)

Notifications service (to notify other party)

Interactions:

Reads:

jobs (current time, status, participants)

cleaner_availability, cleaner_blackout_periods (for reasonable/unreasonable)

Writes:

reschedule_events

Updated jobs.start_time when accepted

Feature flags checked:

enforce_reschedule_policy

show_inconvenience_prompt_ui (to decide if we trigger an inconvenience prompt)

3️⃣ Cancellation / Payments Service
This is the money + fees + cancellation engine.

Endpoints / logic:

POST /jobs/:id/cancel

Internal tasks:

Compute hours_before_start

Decide bucket (gt48, 24_48, lt24, no_show)

Decide fee_pct from policy

Apply grace if allowed

Calculate:

fee_credits

refund_credits

cleaner_comp_credits

platform_comp_credits

Writes:

cancellation_events

Moves credits:

client balance

cleaner’s pending balance / earnings

platform ledger

Also:

Emits risk events (client_risk_events) for:

late cancels

no-shows

Emits reliability events (cleaner_events) for:

cleaner cancels (24–48, <24)

cleaner no-shows

Feature flags checked:

enforce_new_cancellation_policy

enforce_reliability_penalties

enforce_client_risk_restrictions

enforce_prepayment_for_high_risk

This service is critical to get right. It must be fully unit-tested.

4️⃣ Scoring Service (Risk + Reliability Engine)
This can be one service (with modules) or two.

A. Reliability Scoring Module
Responsibilities:

Nightly cron or worker:

For each cleaner:

Pull cleaner_metrics for window

Pull cleaner_events in last 60 days

Compute base score + penalties + bonuses

Write cleaners.reliability_score, reliability_tier

Real-time updates (optional optimization):

After each job completion, recalc only that cleaner (or queue a recalculation).

Reads:

cleaner_metrics

cleaner_events

Past jobs for backfill

Writes:

cleaners.reliability_score

cleaners.reliability_tier

Feature flags:

enable_reliability_score_engine

enforce_reliability_penalties

log_score_debug_info

B. Client Risk Scoring Module
Responsibilities:

Nightly cron:

For each client:

Aggregate client_risk_events over last 30–60 days

Apply decay rules

Compute risk_score and risk_band

Write to client_risk_scores

Reads:

client_risk_events

Writes:

client_risk_scores

Feature flags:

enable_risk_score_engine

enforce_client_risk_restrictions

log_score_debug_info

This service is the math brain for scores.

✅ ITEM 5 OF 10 — New Endpoints + Changes to Existing Endpoints
Goal: define the key API endpoints (or routes/handlers if monolith) that PureTask needs for:

Rescheduling

Cancellation

Availability

Scores & breakdowns

Risk-based behavior

I’ll keep them REST-style. You can adapt names, but the shape and data should stay.

1️⃣ Job / Reschedule Endpoints
1.1 POST /jobs/:jobId/reschedule/request
Who calls it:
Client or cleaner.

Purpose:
Create a reschedule request (does NOT immediately change the job time unless you auto-accept).

Request body (client example):

{
  "requested_by": "client",
  "new_start_time": "2025-03-14T15:00:00Z",
  "reason_code": "client_schedule_conflict"
}
Response (simplified):

{
  "reschedule_event_id": 1234,
  "status": "pending",  // or "accepted" if auto-accepted
  "requested_by": "client",
  "requested_to": "cleaner",
  "original_start_time": "2025-03-14T10:00:00Z",
  "new_start_time": "2025-03-14T15:00:00Z",
  "bucket": "lt24",
  "is_reasonable": true,
  "message": "Reschedule request sent to cleaner."
}
Backend actions:

Calculate hours_before_original + bucket

Call availability logic → set is_reasonable

Insert row into reschedule_events

Notify receiving party

If auto-accept allowed, update jobs.start_time and set status='accepted'

1.2 POST /jobs/:jobId/reschedule/respond
Who calls:
The other party (who received the request).

Purpose:
Accept or decline reschedule.

Request body:

{
  "reschedule_event_id": 1234,
  "action": "accept",        // or "decline"
  "decline_reason_code": "cleaner_schedule_conflict" // if action=decline
}
Response (accept):

{
  "status": "accepted",
  "job_id": 999,
  "new_start_time": "2025-03-14T15:00:00Z",
  "message": "Reschedule confirmed."
}
Response (decline):

{
  "status": "declined",
  "job_id": 999,
  "original_start_time": "2025-03-14T10:00:00Z",
  "message": "Reschedule declined. Original time remains active."
}
Backend actions:

Update reschedule_events.status + declined_by

If accepted:

Update jobs.start_time

Log events (risk/reliability) if late bucket

If declined:

Leave job time as is

Later, if requester cancels → Cancellation engine applies fee rules

2️⃣ Job / Cancellation Endpoints
2.1 POST /jobs/:jobId/cancel
Who calls:
Client or cleaner.

Purpose:
Cancel booking → apply fees, update credits, log events.

Request body:

{
  "cancelled_by": "client",
  "reason_code": "client_schedule_conflict",
  "use_grace_if_available": true
}
Response (client side):

{
  "job_id": 999,
  "status": "cancelled",
  "bucket": "lt24",
  "hours_before_start": 5.5,
  "fee_pct": 100,
  "fee_credits": 600,
  "refund_credits": 0,
  "grace_used": true,
  "message": "Booking cancelled. A grace cancellation was used to waive fees."
}
Backend actions:

Validate cancellation is allowed (job status, time)

Compute: hours_before_start + bucket

Apply cancellation policy + grace logic (if cancelled_by=client)

Compute fee_credits, refund_credits, cleaner_comp_credits, platform_comp_credits

Update client & cleaner credit balances

Insert cancellation_events

Insert client_risk_events and/or cleaner_events

Trigger notifications

2.2 POST /jobs/:jobId/mark-no-show
Who calls:
Support / system / auto-job.

Purpose:
Mark a job as no-show and invoke associated penalties/fees.

Request body:

{
  "no_show_type": "client",    // or "cleaner"
  "initiated_by": "system",    // or "support"
  "note": "Cleaner arrived and waited 20 minutes with no response from client."
}
Response:

{
  "job_id": 999,
  "status": "no_show_client",
  "client_fee_pct": 100,
  "refund_credits": 0,
  "cleaner_comp_credits": 600,
  "message": "Client marked as no-show. Cleaner compensated; no refund issued."
}
Backend actions:

Update job status (no_show_client / no_show_cleaner)

Apply no-show policy rules

Log cancellation_events with bucket=no_show

Log risk or reliability events

Notify both parties

Cleaner app (settings screen), internal services (for summary).

{

  "day_of_week": 1,
  "start_time": "09:00",
  "end_time": "17:00"

Request body:

  "reason": "Vacation"
}
Response:

{
  "id": 12,
  "start_ts": "2025-03-10T00:00:00Z",
  "end_ts": "2025-03-14T23:59:59Z",
  "reason": "Vacation"
}
3.4 POST /availability/check
Purpose:
Internal endpoint: check if cleaner is available at given time.

Request body:

{
  "cleaner_id": 555,
  "start_time": "2025-03-14T15:00:00Z",
  "end_time": "2025-03-14T18:00:00Z"
}
Response:

  "available": false,
  "reason": "conflict_existing_job",
  "conflict_job_id": 999
}
Used by rescheduling and matching engines.

✅ ITEM 6 OF 10 — Real-Time Logic Implementation Checklist
Goal: Give you a developer checklist for every real-time flow:

No ambiguity

All branches covered

Exactly what to compute, write, and trigger

I’ll break it down by flows:

Reschedule Request

Reschedule Response (accept/decline)

Cancellation

No-Show

Check-in / Check-out

Inconvenience Prompt

Availability Check

Credits & Fee Routing

Risk / Reliability Event Logging (real-time, not batch)

You can literally turn each block into code tasks.

1️⃣ Real-Time Logic — Reschedule Request
Endpoint: POST /jobs/:jobId/reschedule/request

Checklist:

Load job by jobId

Validate:

job exists

job status is reschedulable (accepted / scheduled)

job is not already completed/cancelled

Determine context:

requested_by = client | cleaner

requested_to = opposite

t_request = now()

t_start_original = job.start_time

t_start_new = payload.new_start_time

Compute timing:

hours_before_original = (t_start_original - t_request) in hours

Bucket:

>48h → 'gt48'

24–48h → '24_48'

<24h → 'lt24'

Check cleaner availability (via Availability Service):

Call /availability/check with:

cleaner_id

t_start_new, t_end_new

Get:

available: true/false

reason: ...

Determine is_reasonable:

Default: false

Set true if:

available === true

difference in days <= 7

reschedule count for job < 1

t_request < t_start_original

Insert row into reschedule_events:

with:

job_id, client_id, cleaner_id

requested_by, requested_to

t_request, t_start_original, t_start_new

hours_before_original, bucket

reason_code

status = pending

is_reasonable (true/false)

Notify receiving party (Notifications Service)

Return response:

Include:

reschedule_event_id

status: "pending"

original & new times

bucket

is_reasonable

Optional: For some simple cases (>48h, available, same day shift), you may auto-accept and immediately update the job (then skip the response phase).

2️⃣ Real-Time Logic — Reschedule Response (Accept / Decline)
Endpoint: POST /jobs/:jobId/reschedule/respond

Checklist:

Verify:

reschedule_event exists, belongs to jobId

status === 'pending'

requested_to matches current user (client/cleaner)

If action === "accept":

Update job time:

Set jobs.start_time = t_start_new

Adjust jobs.end_time if duration fixed

Update reschedule_event:

status = 'accepted'

updated_at = now()

Risk / Reliability impacts:

If requested_by = client AND bucket = 'lt24':

Insert client_risk_events:

event_type = 'late_reschedule_lt24', weight = +1

If this is 3rd in 14 days → also insert late_reschedule_pattern (+10)

If requested_by = cleaner AND bucket = 'lt24':

Insert cleaner_events:

event_type = 'late_reschedule', weight = -3

Notifications:

Notify both parties: reschedule accepted

Return success payload with new job time.

If action === "decline":

Update reschedule_event:

status = 'declined'

declined_by = current_user_type

decline_reason_code = payload.decline_reason_code

Job time remains unchanged.

No immediate penalties:

Penalties are handled later if the requester cancels (via cancellation logic).

Notifications:

Notify requester that reschedule was declined, original time remains.

Return response with original job time.

3️⃣ Real-Time Logic — Cancellation
Endpoint: POST /jobs/:jobId/cancel

Checklist:

Load job:

Validate job exists

Validate status is cancellable (scheduled / accepted)

Identify:

cancelled_by = client | cleaner

t_cancel = now()

t_start = job.start_time

Compute timing:

hours_before_start

Bucket:

>48h → 'gt48'

24–48h → '24_48'

<24h → 'lt24'

Determine if grace can be used (if cancelled_by = client):

Check:

clients.grace_cancellations_used < grace_cancellations_total

Not a no-show scenario

If use_grace_if_available = true and allowed:

grace_used = true

fee_pct = 0

If no grace or not used:

Apply standard fee rules (from policy):

gt48 → fee_pct = 0

24_48 → fee_pct = 50

lt24 → fee_pct = 100

For cleaner cancellations:

Usually fee_pct = 0 to client (full refund OR compensation separately)

Calculate credits:

held = job.held_credits

fee_credits = floor(held * fee_pct/100)

refund_credits = held - fee_credits

Split fee_credits if client late:

cleaner_comp_credits = fee_credits * cleaner_pct (e.g. 0.70 or 0.80)

platform_comp_credits = fee_credits - cleaner_comp_credits

Update balances:

Client:

credits += refund_credits

Cleaner:

pending_credits += cleaner_comp_credits (or equivalent earnings field)

Platform:

Platform ledger receives platform_comp_credits

Insert cancellation_events:

With:

job_id

cancelled_by

t_cancel

hours_before_start

bucket

reason_code

after_reschedule_declined (if applicable)

fee_pct, fee_credits, refund_credits

cleaner_comp_credits, platform_comp_credits

grace_used

Score events:

If cancelled_by = client:

If bucket = '24_48' → insert client_risk_events (cancel_24_48, +3)

If bucket = 'lt24' → cancel_lt24, +5

If no_show → no_show, +20

If cancelled_by = cleaner:

If bucket = '24_48' → cleaner_events (cancel_24_48, -8)

If bucket = 'lt24' → cancel_lt24, -12

If no-show → no_show, -25

Update job status:

status = 'cancelled' or 'no_show_*' if part of that flow

Notify both parties with fee + refund breakdown.

4️⃣ Real-Time Logic — No-Show
Endpoint: POST /jobs/:jobId/mark-no-show

Checklist:

Validate job is eligible (past start time, no check-in, etc.)

Determine:

no_show_type = client | cleaner

Call Cancellation logic with:

bucket = 'no_show'

cancelled_by = system or appropriate

Apply:

If client no-show:

Full fee to cleaner (if policy)

Risk event +20

If cleaner no-show:

Full refund to client

Reliability event -25

Update job status:

'no_show_client' or 'no_show_cleaner'

Send notifications.

5️⃣ Real-Time Logic — Check-in / Check-out
This feeds reliability (attendance, punctuality, completion).

On Check-in:

Validate:

Correct cleaner & job

Within allowed time window (e.g. 60 minutes before to some time after start)

Compute punctuality:

delta = check_in_time - scheduled_start_time

Mark on_time if |delta| <= 15 minutes (or early is allowed)

Update metrics:

attended_jobs += 1

If on_time: on_time_checkins += 1

Update job status → in_progress

Optionally emit cleaner_events for extreme lateness (manually or via batch).

On Check-out:

Validate job in in_progress

Confirm:

GPS check-out

Required photo proof uploaded

Update metrics:

completion_ok_jobs += 1

photo_compliant_jobs += 1 (if photos OK)

Update job status → completed

Trigger scoring pipeline:

Add rating when available

Update cleaner_metrics for this job

6️⃣ Real-Time Logic — Inconvenience Prompt
Endpoint: POST /jobs/:jobId/inconvenience

Checklist:

Validate:

That user is part of the job (client/cleaner)

That related event exists (reschedule/cancel/no-show)

Take payload:

caused_by

rated_by

score (1–4)

related_event_type

related_event_id

reason_code, note

Insert into inconvenience_logs.

No immediate scoring changes here — patterns are applied in batch jobs (Item 7 later).

7️⃣ Real-Time Logic — Availability Check
Used by: Reschedule, Matching.

Checklist (for /availability/check):

Load weekly availability & blackout periods for cleaner.

Check:

Does requested time fall within any availability block?

Does it overlap blackout?

Does it overlap existing job?

Buffer time honored?

Return:

available: true/false

reason: 'outside_hours' | 'blackout' | 'conflict_existing_job' | 'ok'

Optional conflict_job_id

8️⃣ Real-Time Logic — Credits & Fee Routing
This is part of Cancellation, but important enough to be explicit.

Checklist:

Use held credits on job as base.

Compute fee_pct & refund_credits.

Split fee:

cleaner_comp = fee_credits * cleaner_pct

platform_comp = fee_credits - cleaner_comp

Do all balance updates in a transaction:

If any update fails → rollback.

Write cancellation_events after successful transaction.

9️⃣ Real-Time Logging — Risk & Reliability Events
Wherever a key action happens, follow this rule:

NEVER directly adjust scores in real-time here.

Always log an event in the event table:

client_risk_events for client behaviors

cleaner_events for cleaner behaviors

Then the Scoring Service (cron / batch) uses these events to compute final scores.

Examples:

Late client cancel → add cancel_lt24, +5

Client no-show → add no_show, +20

Cleaner late cancel → cancel_lt24, -12

Cleaner no-show → no_show, -25

Client inconvenience pattern (batch) → inconvenience_pattern, +5/+10

Cleaner inconvenience pattern → inconvenience_high, -5/-10

✅ ITEM 6 STATUS: COMPLETE
You now have:

A concrete checklist for each real-time flow

Exactly what to compute and write

Clear separation of:

Real-time actions (events, fees, balances, statuses)

Batch scoring (scores themselves)

This is directly codable into Node.js services, Base44/n8n, or both.

ITEM 7 — Batch Jobs / Cron Jobs (Nightly & Scheduled Processes)

✅ ITEM 7 OF 10 — Batch Jobs / Cron Jobs
Goal: define all scheduled processes that keep Risk, Reliability, Patterns, and Cleanup running smoothly.

Everything here should be implemented as:

Cron jobs

Scheduled workers

Or Base44/n8n scheduled workflows

Key principle:
👉 Real-time flows log events. Batch flows turn events into scores, patterns, and cleanup.

I’ll break it down into 6 main scheduled jobs:

Reliability Score Recompute (Cleaners)

Client Risk Score Recompute

Inconvenience Pattern Detection

Flexibility & Badge Maintenance

Data Window Maintenance (rolling window)

Reporting / Analytics snapshots (optional but recommended)

1️⃣ Nightly Reliability Score Recompute (Cleaners)
When:

Once per night (e.g. 2:00 AM platform time)

Purpose:
Turn cleaner_metrics + cleaner_events into a fresh reliability_score and tier for each cleaner.

Steps:

For each active cleaner:

Load:

Jobs in last X days or Y jobs (e.g. last 60 days or 30 jobs)

cleaner_metrics row

cleaner_events within window

Compute base metrics:

Attendance rate = attended_jobs / total_jobs_window

On-time rate = on_time_checkins / attended_jobs

Photo compliance rate = photo_compliant_jobs / total_jobs_window

Communication compliance rate

Completion confirmation rate

Ratings avg from ratings_sum / ratings_count

Convert metrics into base points (according to your weights):

Example:

Attendance → up to +25

Punctuality → up to +20

Photo proof → up to +15

Communication → up to +10

Completion → up to +10

Ratings → up to +10

Apply penalties/bonuses:

Sum all weight values from cleaner_events within window

e.g. cancel_lt24 = -12, no_show = -25, inconvenience_high = -5, streak bonus +5, etc.

Final reliability score:

reliability_score = base_points + sum(event_weights)
clamp between 0 and 100
Determine tier:

Example:

<60 → Developing

60–74 → Semi Pro

75–89 → Pro

90–100 → Elite

Write results to cleaners table:

reliability_score

reliability_tier

Optional: log debug info if log_score_debug_info flag is ON.

Feature flag:

enable_reliability_score_engine must be ON

enforce_reliability_penalties controls whether event weights are used or ignored

2️⃣ Nightly Client Risk Score Recompute
When:

Once per night (e.g. 3:00 AM)

Purpose:
Turn client_risk_events into risk_score + risk_band.

Steps:

For each active client:

Load client_risk_events in last 14–30 days (your chosen window).

Compute raw risk:

base_risk = SUM(weight from client_risk_events in window)
Apply decay / cap:

Older events (e.g. 15–30 days old) could have reduced weight (optional).

Cap risk score between 0 and 100.

Determine risk band:

Example:

0–19 → normal

20–39 → mild

40–59 → elevated

60–79 → high

80–100 → critical

Write to client_risk_scores:

risk_score

risk_band

last_recomputed_at = now()

Optional: log changes for clients whose band changed (for support / audits).

Feature flag:

enable_risk_score_engine

3️⃣ Inconvenience Pattern Detection
When:

Once per day (maybe same time as risk/reliability jobs)

Purpose:
Convert multiple high inconvenience logs into pattern events that feed risk & reliability.

Steps:

For clients:

Query inconvenience_logs where:

caused_by = 'client'

score >= 3

created_at > now() - interval '14 days'

Group by client_id

For each client:

If count >= 3 but <5:

Insert client_risk_events:

event_type = 'inconvenience_pattern'

weight = +5

If count >= 5:

Another event, weight = +5 (total +10 for extreme pattern)

For cleaners:

Query inconvenience_logs where:

caused_by = 'cleaner'

score >= 3

created_at > now() - interval '30 days'

Group by cleaner_id

For each cleaner:

If count >= 3:

Insert cleaner_events:

event_type = 'inconvenience_high'

weight = -5

If count >= 5:

Another event, weight = -5 (total -10)

Make sure pattern jobs are idempotent:

Mark pattern windows once processed, or:

Use metadata (e.g. time-bucket key) to avoid double-inserting for same period.

Feature flag:

enforce_inconvenience_patterns

4️⃣ Flexibility & Badge Maintenance
When:

Once per day

Purpose:
Assign/remove Low Flexibility badges based on reschedule declines.

Steps:

Compute declines in last 30 days:

Query reschedule_events where:

requested_by = 'client'

requested_to = 'cleaner'

status = 'declined'

is_reasonable = true

created_at > now() - interval '30 days'

Group by cleaner.

For each cleaner:

If count >= 3:

Set cleaners.flexibility_status = 'low'

Upsert badge into badge_assignments with badge_type = 'low_flexibility', is_active = true

Else if count == 0 or <3:

If they currently have badge:

Check removal rules:

e.g. no reasonable declines in last 30 days

OR X completed jobs with no declines

Then:

Set flexibility_status = 'normal'

badge_assignments.is_active = false, removed_at = now()

Optionally log changes for transparency.

Feature flag:

show_low_flexibility_badge_ui (UI side)

Badge calculations can run regardless, but you may ignore them if flag is off.

5️⃣ Data Window Maintenance (Rolling Window Cleanup)
When:

Daily or weekly, depending on database size

Purpose:
Keep tables lean and scores focused on recent behavior.

Steps:

Prune old events (optional, or archive):

client_risk_events: delete or archive events older than, say, 1–2 years.

cleaner_events: same.

inconvenience_logs: maybe keep 6–12 months of data.

Ensure cleaner_metrics window is consistent:

Option A: metrics are always rolling, so:

Recalculate metrics for last 60 days if drift occurred.

Consistency checks:

If any job is outside the scoring window but still counted:

Adjust total_jobs_window etc.

Indexes maintenance:

Vacuum/analyze key tables (depends how you deploy; often handled by DB).

6️⃣ Reporting / Analytics Snapshots (Optional but Strongly Recommended)
These do not affect platform behavior but are great for:

Dashboards

Health metrics

Experimentation

When:

Nightly or hourly aggregates

Examples:

Snapshot table daily_score_stats:

date, avg_reliability_score, avg_risk_score, high_risk_clients_count, low_flex_cleaners_count, cancellations_lt24_count, reschedules_lt24_count
Snapshot table daily_policy_impact:

date, total_fees_collected, total_cleaner_comp, total_platform_comp, total_grace_used
These give you powerful visibility into:

Are policies too strict?

Are cancellations going down?

Are high-risk bands growing or shrinking?

Are cleaners staying happy?

You now have a full list of scheduled jobs with:

What they do

When they run

What tables they read/write

Which flags they depend on

Real-time flows (Item 6) + batch jobs (Item 7) together = complete behavior.

✅ ITEM 8 OF 10 — Internal Monitoring / Telemetry
Goal: define what we track so we can see:

Is the system behaving as intended?

Are we accidentally punishing good users or letting bad behavior slip?

Are cancellations/reschedules trending in the right direction?

Are scores and fees stable, fair, and predictable?

We’ll cover:

Core KPIs (high level)

Operational metrics (per-feature)

Alerting thresholds

Logs & tracing

Dashboards you should have

You can implement this in whatever stack you’re using (Datadog, Grafana, Mixpanel, custom admin, etc.).

1️⃣ Core KPIs
These are overall health metrics you should always be able to see.

1.1 Cancellations
Track DAILY (and show weekly trend):

total_cancellations

cancel_gt48_count

cancel_24_48_count

cancel_lt24_count

no_show_client_count

no_show_cleaner_count

And percentages:

% cancellations with fees

% no-shows out of total jobs

reschedule_requests_per_job (avg)

avg_reliability_score (across all cleaners)

median_reliability_score

distribution (bucket counts):

Developing

Semi-Pro

Pro

Elite

risk_band_counts:

normal

mild

elevated

high

critical

total_late_fees_collected_per_day

grace_cancellations_used_per_day

These help assess if fees are balanced or feel punitive.

2️⃣ Operational Metrics (Per-Feature)
Now the per-feature telemetry that proves each engine is working.

2.1 Reliability Engine
From cleaner_events & scores:

cleaner_events_count_per_type:

late_reschedule

cancel_24_48

cancel_lt24

no_show

inconvenience_high

streak_bonus

avg_reliability_score_delta_per_day

# of cleaners whose tier changed today:

upgrades count

downgrades count

ALERT if:

5% of cleaners drop more than 10 points in a single day.

average reliability score drops >5 points in a week.

2.2 Risk Engine
From client_risk_events:

risk_events_count_per_type:

late_reschedule_lt24

late_reschedule_pattern

cancel_24_48

cancel_lt24

no_show

inconvenience_pattern

# of clients changing risk_band per day

# of clients in high

# of clients in critical

ALERT if:

critical band grows rapidly (>50% in a week).

A large number of clients jump two bands at once.

2.3 Inconvenience System
From inconvenience_logs:

inconvenience_logs_count (total per day)

avg_inconvenience_score_by_caused_by:

average score when caused_by=client

average score when caused_by=cleaner

distribution of scores (1–4)

This tells you:

Are clients harming cleaners more, or vice versa?

Are people actually filling this out or ignoring it?

2.4 Availability & Flexibility
cleaner_availability_blocks_count

% cleaners with at least 1 availability block configured

% jobs created that fall within declared availability

# cleaners with low_flexibility badge active

# cleaners whose badge was removed today

ALERT if:

Most jobs are being booked outside stated availability (bug or mismatch).

2.5 Matching
avg_number_of_cleaners_shown_per_search

avg_time_to_cleaner_acceptance

match_acceptance_rate (how often first set of suggested cleaners accept)

For high-risk clients:

avg_match_success_rate

avg_time_to_match

If high-risk users suddenly can’t get matched → too strict.

3️⃣ Alerting Thresholds
You want automatic alerts when stuff breaks, not just dashboards.

Recommended alerts:
Cancellations spike

Condition: total_cancellations_today > 2x 7-day average

No-shows spike

Condition: no_show_client_count_today or no_show_cleaner_count_today > X% of total jobs.

Fees anomaly

Condition: total_late_fees_collected_today > 3x 7-day average

Or < 0.2x 7-day average after turning on policy (could mean fee logic broken).

Score drift

Condition: avg_reliability_score_today changes > ±5 points vs last week.

Condition: avg_risk_score_today jumps upward significantly.

Badge explosion

Condition: low_flexibility_badge_active count increases > 50% in one week.

Workflow failures

Any job in scoring / cancellation pipeline that fails > N times triggers alert.

4️⃣ Logs & Tracing
Beyond metrics, you need structured logs for:

Score recompute runs

Policy decisions (why a fee was X% not Y%)

Risk band changes

Tier changes

4.1 Decision Logs
For sensitive actions (fees, penalties, score changes), log:

actor_id (client/cleaner)

job_id

previous_score & new_score (for reliability/risk)

events_used (list of event_types + weights)

policy_version (if you ever version your policies)

This log allows support and engineering to answer:

“Why did my fee come out to this number?”
“Why did my score drop from 85 to 78?”

4.2 Error Logs
Failure to insert *_events

Failure to update cleaners or client_risk_scores

Exceptions in cancellation/reschedule logic

Each should log:

Input payload

Stacktrace

Whether balances were updated or not

5️⃣ Dashboards to Build
You should have at least 3 dashboards:

5.1 Ops Health Dashboard
Audience: You & support/ops.

Shows:

Total jobs/day

Cancellations (by bucket)

Reschedules (by bucket)

No-shows

Fees collected vs refunded

5.2 Cleaner Health & Supply Dashboard

5.3 Client Behavior Dashboard

Risk band distribution

Late cancels per client segment

No-show client rate

High-risk clients: count trend

Prepayment-required bookings vs normal

Inconvenience scores with caused_by=client

✅ ITEM 9 OF 10 — QA Plan / Test Scenarios
Goal: make sure all this complexity actually works and doesn’t accidentally screw cleaners or clients.

We’ll define:

Test types

Core unit test areas

Integration test flows

End-to-end scenarios

Edge cases

“Evil user” abuse tests

You can turn each bullet into test cases in Jest, Cypress, Postman collections, etc.

1️⃣ Test Types
We need coverage at 4 levels:

Unit tests – pure functions: fee calc, bucket calc, score calc

Integration tests – endpoint + DB behavior per flow

End-to-end tests – full user journeys: book → reschedule → cancel → payout

Manual / UAT – human sanity checks with realistic data and devices

2️⃣ Core Unit Test Areas
A. Time & Bucket Logic
Function: getBucket(hours_before_start)

Test:

72h → gt48

30h → 24_48

2h → lt24

negative hours (late) → treat as lt24 or no_show depending on policy

B. Fee Calculation
Function: calculateCancellationOutcome(held_credits, bucket, cancelled_by, grace_available)

Test scenarios:

Client cancels 60h before:

bucket = gt48

fee_pct = 0

refund = held

Client cancels 30h before:

bucket = 24_48

fee_pct = 50

correct split to cleaner/platform

Client cancels 5h before with grace:

bucket = lt24

grace_available = true

fee_pct = 0

Cleaner cancels 5h before:

client gets full refund

cleaner gets 0, plus reliability penalty later

C. Reasonable vs Unreasonable Reschedule
Function: isReasonableReschedule(old_time, new_time, hours_before_original, cleaner_availability, conflicts, reschedule_count_for_job)

Test:

New time inside availability, no conflict, <7-day move → true

New time outside availability → false

New time same day but 2x in a row → second one false

New time <24h but cleaner available → still true if we define it that way

D. Reliability Score Formula
Function: computeReliabilityScore(metrics, events)

Test:

Perfect metrics, no events → 100

One late client-reschedule acceptance (<24h) → -3 → 97

One cleaner late cancel (<24h) → -12

No-shows produce big drops

Boundaries: cannot go <0 or >100

E. Client Risk Score Formula
Function: computeRiskScore(events)

Test:

No events → 0, band normal

3x late reschedule → moderate band

1 no-show → jump into elevated or high

Old events decaying over time

F. Availability Check
Function: isCleanerAvailable(availabilityBlocks, blackoutPeriods, existingJobs, requestedStart, requestedEnd)

Test:

Normal day, inside block → available

Over blackout → unavailable

Overlapping existing job → unavailable

Crossing day boundary → handled correctly

3️⃣ Integration Tests (API + DB)
A. Reschedule Flow
Client requests reschedule >48h before, cleaner available

POST /jobs/:id/reschedule/request

DB: reschedule_events row created, is_reasonable = true, bucket = gt48

No penalty events logged

Client requests reschedule <24h, cleaner available

DB: bucket = lt24, is_reasonable = true

Later, cleaner accepts:

Job time updated

client_risk_events record added

Client request outside availability

is_reasonable = false

Cleaner declines → confirm no Low Flex badge event later

B. Cancellation Flow
Client cancels 30h before

POST /cancel

DB:

cancellation_events row with 24_48, fee_pct = 50

client_risk_events with type cancel_24_48

Balances: correct split

Client cancels 5h before with grace

DB:

grace_used = true

fee_pct = 0

client_risk_events may be reduced or none (depending on policy)

Cleaner cancels 3h before

DB:

cancellation_events with bucket lt24

cleaner_events penalty

Client refunded fully

C. No-Show Flow
Client no-show

Mark job no-show

DB:

cancellation_events bucket no_show

Risk event +20

Balances:

Cleaner compensated

Client not refunded

Cleaner no-show

DB:

cleaner_events with big negative weight

Balances:

Client refunded

Cleaner gets no comp

D. Inconvenience Logging
After late client reschedule:

POST /jobs/:id/inconvenience

DB: inconvenience_logs row created, linked to reschedule_events

After cleaner late cancel:

Same pattern.

4️⃣ End-to-End Scenarios
These are multi-step flows from the user perspective.

Scenario 1 — Clean Client, Clean Cleaner
Client books job → Cleaner accepts

Cleaner arrives on time, checks in, does job, checks out, gets good rating

No reschedules, no cancellations

Expected:

Reliability score for cleaner goes UP slightly

Client risk stays low

No fees, no weird logs

Scenario 2 — High-Risk Client Behavior
Client books job

Client reschedules <24h, cleaner accepts

Client later cancels <24h

Client no-shows another job

Expected:

client_risk_events filled with 3–4 events

Risk score high → band = high or critical

Risk-based UI warnings appear (with flags ON)

Prepayment required for new booking (with flags ON)

Scenario 3 — Unreliable Cleaner Behavior
Cleaner cancels inside 24h (once)

Cleaner no-shows (once)

Late arrivals / poor ratings

Expected:

Reliability score drops significantly

Tier may drop (e.g. from Pro → Semi Pro)

Score Breakdown UI clearly shows penalties

Matching might rank them lower

Scenario 4 — Reschedule Dispute Path
Client requests reschedule <24h

Cleaner declines (reasonable)

Client cannot attend original time & cancels

Expected:

Client pays late cancellation fee

Cleaner not penalized (no reliability hit)

Inconvenience log can reflect cleaner view

5️⃣ Edge Cases
A. Time Edge Cases
Job starts in <1h when client tries to reschedule:

Disallow reschedule, suggest cancel → apply late fee rules

Client tries to cancel after actual start time:

Treat as no-show (if cleaner was there) or late cancel, based on context

B. Double-Action Race Conditions
Client reschedules while cleaner is already cancelling

Two reschedule requests created quickly

Test:

Only one final job state accepted

No double-charging or double-refund

Use DB transactions & idempotency keys

C. Legacy Data
Old jobs created before new system exists

Ensure new code doesn’t crash when:

client_risk_scores missing

cleaner_metrics empty

Expectation:

Default to safe values (normal risk, base reliability), no exceptions.

6️⃣ “Evil User” Abuse Tests
These are intentional abuse scenarios to see if system is robust.

A. Client Abuse
Client constantly uses grace cancellations:

Confirm grace_cancellations_used increments properly

Once max reached, grace no longer applies

Late cancels now incur full fees

Client tries to spam reschedule button:

Flood of reschedule_events prevented (e.g. throttle)

Only most recent matters

B. Cleaner Abuse
Cleaner constantly declines reasonable reschedules:

Confirm Low Flex badge triggers

Badge removed later after good behavior

Cleaner always accepts jobs but then cancels late:

Confirm reliability drops

Confirm they potentially fall in search / matching

C. Attack on Money Flows
User tries to cancel, then retry multiple times:

Ensure idempotency: no double refunds/fees

API replay:

Cancel endpoint called twice with same job → second call should fail gracefully (“already cancelled”).

We now have:

A structured QA plan

Unit, integration, E2E, edge, and abuse tests clearly defined

Enough detail to actually implement a strong test suite

✅ ITEM 10 OF 10 — Rollout Safety & Rollback Plan
Goal: define exactly how we turn this on in production and how we turn it off or undo if something goes sideways.

We’ll cover:

Rollout stages (with flags)

What we monitor at each stage

How to pause / partially roll back

How to fully fall back to old behavior

Principles to follow during launch

1️⃣ Rollout Stages (With Flags)
We’ll use the feature flags we defined earlier and turn them on in controlled waves.

🔹 Stage 0 — Dark Launch (Infra only)
What’s ON:

DB migrations (all new tables/columns)

Event logging:

client_risk_events

cleaner_events

reschedule_events

cancellation_events

inconvenience_logs

Flags:

enable_risk_score_engine: ON (optional)

enable_reliability_score_engine: ON

Everything UI + enforcement: OFF

Behavior:

Users see NO changes.

System just logs events and maybe computes scores internally.

If something breaks:

Turn enable_*_score_engine OFF and stop recompute jobs.

Event logging can stay — it’s passive.

🔹 Stage 1 — Internal Scoring & Debug
What’s ON:

Scoring engines fully active:

enable_risk_score_engine = ON

enable_reliability_score_engine = ON

log_score_debug_info = ON (for a while)

What’s still OFF:

All enforcement flags

All UI flags (or only for internal/admin)

Behavior:

Scores are calculated nightly.

Only admins/engineers see them via internal tools.

If metrics look weird (scores too harsh, etc.):

Tweak weight values in scoring formulas.

Recompute on staging from production data snapshots until comfortable.

🔹 Stage 2 — Soft UI Rollout (Read-Only)
Turn ON gradually (e.g., 5% → 20% → 100%):

show_cleaner_reliability_breakdown_ui

show_client_booking_reliability_ui

show_inconvenience_prompt_ui (maybe to 10–20% first)

show_low_flexibility_badge_ui (optional, a bit later)

show_risk_based_warnings_ui

What’s still OFF:

enforce_new_cancellation_policy

enforce_reschedule_policy

enforce_client_risk_restrictions

enforce_prepayment_for_high_risk

Matching-related flags (enable_*matching)

Behavior:

Cleaners see score breakdowns but behavior hasn’t changed.

Clients see grace & cancellation clarity but fees are still your existing rules.

Inconvenience prompts start logging extra data.

If cleaners/client feedback is confused or negative:

You can:

Adjust copy/tooltips

Temporarily turn particular UI flags OFF without touching the engines.

🔹 Stage 3 — Policy Enforcement (Core Behavior)
This is the big one. Turn on in very small percentages first.

Flags to roll ON gradually (per cohort):

enforce_new_cancellation_policy

enforce_reschedule_policy

enforce_inconvenience_patterns

enforce_reliability_penalties

Strategy:

Start with 10% of traffic (or a test region/market).

Watch:

cancellations/fees per job

average reliability and risk

support tickets related to “fees” or “unfair penalties”

If healthy:

Gradually expand to 25% → 50% → 100%.

If something breaks (e.g., fees wrong, too harsh):

Immediately toggle OFF:

enforce_new_cancellation_policy

enforce_reschedule_policy

Platform falls back to old behavior while still logging events & scores.

🔹 Stage 4 — Risk-Based Restrictions & Matching
Once policies and scores are stable:

Flags to enable carefully:

enforce_client_risk_restrictions

enforce_prepayment_for_high_risk

enable_score_based_matching

enable_risk_aware_matching

enable_flexibility_aware_matching

Again, start with small % or single region.

Behavior:

High-risk clients see more warnings and limits.

High-risk clients may be forced to prepay.

Top cleaners are protected from high-risk clients.

Matching results favor reliable cleaners and reasonable clients.

If high-risk clients suddenly can’t get service or complaints spike:

Turn OFF:

enforce_client_risk_restrictions

enforce_prepayment_for_high_risk

And/or reduce matching weight of risk in enable_risk_aware_matching

Scores and UI can remain — just dial back how much they affect behavior.

2️⃣ What We Monitor At Each Stage
Already defined in Item 8, but specifically:

Before & after enabling each major flag, snapshot:

Cancellation rate by bucket

Late fee volume

Avg reliability score

Avg risk score

of high-risk clients
of low-flex cleaners
Support ticket volume related to:

billing

cancellations

“unfair” scores or matching

If any of these jump in a way that feels wrong → roll back that stage.

3️⃣ How to Pause or Partially Roll Back
All major enforcement behavior is behind flags. To pause the new system while keeping data:

If you see a problem:

Turn OFF:

enforce_new_cancellation_policy

enforce_reschedule_policy

enforce_client_risk_restrictions

enforce_prepayment_for_high_risk

enable_risk_aware_matching

enable_flexibility_aware_matching

If needed, enforce_reliability_penalties

Keep ON (if safe):

enable_risk_score_engine

enable_reliability_score_engine

UI flags (show_*) if they are correct

Logging & telemetry

This means:

Users might still see scores, but behavior returns to old patterns.

You can debug formulas & logic without affecting the real world.

If UI also seems wrong/confusing:

Turn OFF:

show_cleaner_reliability_breakdown_ui

show_client_booking_reliability_ui

show_risk_based_warnings_ui

show_low_flexibility_badge_ui

Now the whole system becomes “dark” again but all the historical data is still being captured and scores can be recomputed.

4️⃣ How to Fully Fall Back to Old Behavior
In a worst-case scenario (e.g., something truly misdesigned, or regulatory headaches), you want a clear, fast fallback:

Turn OFF all enforcement flags:

enforce_new_cancellation_policy

enforce_reschedule_policy

enforce_inconvenience_patterns

enforce_reliability_penalties

enforce_client_risk_restrictions

enforce_prepayment_for_high_risk

enable_score_based_matching

enable_risk_aware_matching

enable_flexibility_aware_matching

Optionally turn OFF scoring engines:

enable_risk_score_engine

enable_reliability_score_engine

Turn OFF score UIs:

show_* flags

Keep:

DB tables & logs — do not drop them.

Internal admin tools — you still might use them for analysis.

Now you’re effectively back to your previous marketplace behavior, just with a bunch of invisible logging.

5️⃣ Principles to Follow During Launch
To keep PureTask safe and trusted:

Never change money flows and scoring on the same day without flags.

First test scoring internal-only.

Then turn on fees/enforcement.

Always launch policies on weekdays, not Fridays/weekends.

You want support and engineering fully present.

Over-communicate to cleaners first.

They are your supply side and must feel protected.

A simple in-app banner or email:

“We’re rolling out a new reliability system that protects your time and rewards consistency. We’ll show your score first, then later tie it into pricing and matching.”

Treat the first 2–4 weeks as calibration.

Expect to tweak penalty weights.

Watch for unexpected side effects (like too many high-risk clients or penalties).

Err on the side of being lenient early.

Slightly under-penalize rather than over-penalize.

You can always tighten rules once you see real data.

We now have all 10 items:

Release phases

Endpoints & payloads

Real-time logic checklist

Batch jobs / cron jobs

Monitoring & telemetry

QA / test scenarios

Rollout safety & rollback plan

This is a complete technical roadmap to implement the whole system safely.
