We’re now in B: Base44 / n8n Workflow Map.
I’ll go through the workflows in order — one at a time — so you can sanity-check each.

✅ WORKFLOW 1 / 12 — Job Creation Workflow
(How a new job flows into all our downstream systems)

Goal:
When a client creates a job, we:

Create the job row

Initialize escrow/held credits

Prime the system for:

future reschedules

cancellations

scoring

matching

Emit a clean event that other workflows can subscribe to

You can implement this in Base44 or n8n — I’ll describe it as a generic flow with “nodes”.

🔹 Trigger
Event name: job_created

How it fires:

Client confirms booking in app → backend creates jobs row → backend POSTs to Base44/n8n webhook:

Example payload:

{
  "event": "job_created",
  "job_id": 999,
  "client_id": 123,
  "cleaner_id": null,              // null if not yet assigned
  "job_type": "deep_clean",
  "start_time": "2025-03-14T10:00:00Z",
  "end_time": "2025-03-14T13:00:00Z",
  "held_credits": 600
}
🔹 Workflow Steps (Node-by-node)
I’ll write it as a sequence you can literally build:

🟣 Node 1 — Webhook Trigger
Type: Webhook / HTTP Trigger

Filter: Only continue if event == "job_created"

If anything else comes in, either ignore or route to another flow.

🟣 Node 2 — Fetch Job & Client Details
Purpose: Make sure we have the full, authoritative context.

Type: DB node / HTTP call to your API

Query:

SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = :job_id

SELECT * FROM clients WHERE id = :client_id

Why:
We trust the database, not just the incoming payload.

🟣 Node 3 — Validate Job State
Checks:

Job status is created or scheduled

start_time is in the future

held_credits is present and ≥ 0

If anything is invalid:

Log error event: job_created_invalid

(Optional) notify support

End workflow

🟣 Node 4 — Initialize Scoring Context (Client)
If this is a new client or first job, we want risk scaffolding ready.

Operations:

Check if a client_risk_scores row exists for client_id

If not, insert:

INSERT INTO client_risk_scores (client_id, risk_score, risk_band)
VALUES (:client_id, 0, 'normal')
ON CONFLICT (client_id) DO NOTHING;
(Optional) Validate clients.grace_cancellations_used is not null (defaults from migrations).

🟣 Node 5 — Initialize Scoring Context (Cleaner, if pre-assigned)
If the job already has a cleaner at creation:

Check if cleaner_metrics row exists

If not, insert base row:

INSERT INTO cleaner_metrics (cleaner_id)
VALUES (:cleaner_id)
ON CONFLICT (cleaner_id) DO NOTHING;
Check if cleaner_profile_settings exists

If not, create default travel radius / buffer rows.

If cleaner is not yet assigned:

Skip this for now — it will be done later in the “job_accepted” workflow.

🟣 Node 6 — Emit “Job Ready for Matching” Event
Now that the job exists and base scaffolding is ready, let’s kick matching.

Emit internal event: job_ready_for_matching

Payload example:

{
  "event": "job_ready_for_matching",
  "job_id": 999,
  "client_id": 123,
  "job_type": "deep_clean",
  "start_time": "2025-03-14T10:00:00Z",
  "duration_minutes": 180,
  "location": {
    "lat": 37.7749,
    "lng": -122.4194
  }
}
This event can trigger:

Matching / Search workflow (Workflow 11 later)

Notifications to cleaners if you do broadcast offers

🟣 Node 7 — Optional: Create Initial Match Recommendation Log
If you want to debug or analyze matching later, you can pre-log that this job entered the system:

Insert into match_recommendations with a placeholder (no cleaners yet):

INSERT INTO match_recommendations (
  job_id, client_id, cleaner_id, match_score, rank
)
VALUES (:job_id, :client_id, NULL, 0, NULL);
Or create nothing now and let the actual matching workflow handle this.

🟣 Node 8 — Notify Client (Booking Confirmation)
This is more product UX, but part of the workflow:

Send push / email:

“Your booking is confirmed for [Date, Time]. We’ll match you with a cleaner shortly.”
or
“Your booking is confirmed with [Cleaner Name].”

Use Notification Service rather than writing email logic inside the workflow.

🟣 Node 9 — Error Handling / Logging
For each DB operation:

If it fails:

Log job_created_flow_failed with:

job_id

error message

at which node

Optionally retry (n8n/Base44 retry mechanism)

If critical (like failure to create risk scaffolding) → notify tech/support Slack channel.

🔹 Summary of Writes for Workflow 1
On a successful run, the Job Creation Workflow will:

Confirm job row is valid in jobs.

Ensure client has a row in client_risk_scores.

Optionally ensure cleaner has rows in cleaner_metrics and cleaner_profile_settings (if assigned).

Optionally initialize an entry in match_recommendations.

Emit job_ready_for_matching for downstream flows.

Trigger client notification.

🔹 Why this matters in the bigger system
This workflow:

Ensures every job is “known” to the scoring system from day 0

Sends a clean event into the Matching and Job Accepted workflows

Avoids dangling jobs that never get scored or matched properly

This is literally the “birth event” for every job in your marketplace.

If you’re happy with Workflow 1, next up in the workflow map is:

WORKFLOW 2 / 12 — Job Acceptance Workflow
(Cleaner accepts a job → attendance pipeline, protections, and matching closeout.)

If you want to continue, just say:

“Proceed with Workflow 2.”


proceed

Nice, let’s wire what happens when a cleaner actually takes the job 💪

✅ WORKFLOW 2 / 12 — Job Acceptance Workflow
Event: cleaner accepts a job (or is auto-assigned).

Goal:
When a cleaner accepts a job, the system should:

Lock in the pairing

Prepare attendance & scoring tracking

Update matching state

Notify the client

Make sure availability & conflicts are consistent

This is a Base44/n8n flow that reacts to job_accepted.

🔹 Trigger
Event name: job_accepted

Source:

Cleaner taps “Accept” in the app

OR system auto-assigns a cleaner

Example payload:

{
  "event": "job_accepted",
  "job_id": 999,
  "client_id": 123,
  "cleaner_id": 555,
  "start_time": "2025-03-14T10:00:00Z",
  "end_time": "2025-03-14T13:00:00Z"
}
🔹 Workflow Steps (Node-by-node)
🟣 Node 1 — Webhook Trigger
Trigger on job_accepted event.

Ignore if any other event type.

🟣 Node 2 — Fetch Job + Cleaner + Client
DB/API lookups:

SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = :job_id

SELECT * FROM cleaners WHERE id = :cleaner_id

SELECT * FROM clients WHERE id = :client_id

Validation:

Job status must be in created or pending_assignment.

Job must not be already accepted by another cleaner (unless you support multiple).

Start time is still in the future.

If invalid:

Log job_accepted_invalid

Optionally notify support

Stop workflow.

🟣 Node 3 — Conflict & Availability Check (safety)
Even though matching should avoid conflicts, double check:

Call /availability/check with:

cleaner_id

start_time, end_time

If available == false:

Log job_accepted_conflict

Optionally:

auto-reject acceptance, or

flag for manual review

(You can decide how strict to be here.)

🟣 Node 4 — Update Job Status & Assignment
If checks pass:

Set jobs.cleaner_id = :cleaner_id

Set jobs.status = 'accepted'

Set jobs.updated_at = now()

You might do this step in your backend first and just let this workflow follow up; that’s fine as long as state is consistent.

🟣 Node 5 — Initialize Cleaner Metrics (if missing)
Ensure:

INSERT INTO cleaner_metrics (cleaner_id)
SELECT :cleaner_id
WHERE NOT EXISTS (
  SELECT 1 FROM cleaner_metrics WHERE cleaner_id = :cleaner_id
);
Ensure:

INSERT INTO cleaner_profile_settings (cleaner_id)
SELECT :cleaner_id
WHERE NOT EXISTS (
  SELECT 1 FROM cleaner_profile_settings WHERE cleaner_id = :cleaner_id
);
This guarantees the scoring engine has a base row.

🟣 Node 6 — Attendance Tracking Setup (optional but recommended)
You may want to set up an internal “attendance timer”:

Schedule a future workflow run at start_time - X minutes:

e.g., 15–30 minutes before job start.

That future job will:

Check if cleaner has checked in yet

Help detect potential no-shows or very late arrivals

In Base44/n8n, this can be a delay node or scheduled job referencing job_id.

🟣 Node 7 — Emit Cleaner Event (Optional Positive Signal)
You can log a small positive cleaner_event for accepting jobs, especially if that matters later.

Example:

INSERT INTO cleaner_events (cleaner_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata)
VALUES (:cleaner_id, :job_id, 'job_accepted', 0, '{}');
Weight = 0 for now (no impact), but gives you a trail.

🟣 Node 8 — Update Matching State
If you have a match_recommendations table or in-memory job:

Mark this job as “matched” and close out other pending candidate suggestions.

Options:

Soft-delete or mark match_recommendations rows for this job as chosen for the selected cleaner, ignored for others.

This makes your analytics clean.

🟣 Node 9 — Notify Client
Trigger Notification Service:

Push/email to client:

“Your cleaning is confirmed with [Cleaner Name] on [Date, Time].”

Include:

Cleaner photo/name

Reliability tier/badge (if you want)

Any prep instructions

Optionally notify cleaner too:

“You’ve accepted a job with [Client Name] on [Date, Time].”

🟣 Node 10 — Error Handling / Retry
For each DB write:

If failure:

Log job_accepted_flow_failed

Include job_id, cleaner_id, error detail

Configure retries (e.g., 3 attempts with exponential backoff)

If sync with backend and automation ever disagrees, treat the backend (core app DB) as source of truth and resync from there.

🔹 Summary of Writes for Workflow 2
On a successful job_accepted workflow, we have:

jobs updated:

cleaner_id set

status = 'accepted'

cleaner_metrics & cleaner_profile_settings ensured for that cleaner.

Optionally, cleaner_events gets a job_accepted row.

Matching context updated (match_recommendations closed out, if used).

Attendance pre-check timer scheduled (optional).

Client and cleaner notified.

🔹 Why this matters in the bigger system
This workflow is the bridge from “job exists” → “cleaner is committed, and we can now enforce reliability, attendance, and fees.”

From here, the next key workflows kick in:

Check-in / Check-out

Rescheduling

Cancellation

No-show logic

Scoring

If you’re good with Workflow 2, we move to:

WORKFLOW 3 / 12 — Reschedule Request Workflow
(When client or cleaner asks to change the time, how we log it, evaluate it, and notify the other party.)

If you want to continue, just say:

“Proceed with Workflow 3.”


proceed

Nice, now we handle the chaos: reschedules 🔁

✅ WORKFLOW 3 / 12 — Reschedule Request Workflow
Event: client or cleaner requests a new time for an existing job.

Goal:
When someone hits “Reschedule”:

We validate the request

Decide if it’s reasonable or unreasonable

Log it in reschedule_events

Notify the other party

(Optionally) auto-accept in simple cases

This workflow feeds:

Client Risk Score

Cleaner Reliability (if cleaner is the one changing)

Low Flexibility badge

Inconvenience prompts later

You’ll implement this around the POST /jobs/:jobId/reschedule/request endpoint.

🔹 Trigger
Event name: job_reschedule_requested

Source:

App → backend → creates event → sends webhook to Base44/n8n with reschedule payload.

Example payload:

{
  "event": "job_reschedule_requested",
  "job_id": 999,
  "requested_by": "client",      // or 'cleaner'
  "new_start_time": "2025-03-14T15:00:00Z",
  "reason_code": "client_schedule_conflict",
  "actor_user_id": 123
}
🔹 Workflow Steps (Node-by-node)
🟣 Node 1 — Webhook Trigger
Trigger on job_reschedule_requested.

Ignore other events.

🟣 Node 2 — Load Job, Client, Cleaner, Availability
DB/API queries:

SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = :job_id

SELECT * FROM cleaners WHERE id = job.cleaner_id

SELECT * FROM clients WHERE id = job.client_id

For cleaner availability (via Availability Service or DB):

SELECT * FROM cleaner_availability WHERE cleaner_id = :cleaner_id

SELECT * FROM cleaner_blackout_periods WHERE cleaner_id = :cleaner_id AND overlaps(...)

SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE cleaner_id = :cleaner_id AND time overlaps new_start_time

🟣 Node 3 — Validate Job State
Checks:

Job exists

Job status is accepted or scheduled

Job has a cleaner_id (you only reschedule assigned jobs in this logic; pre-assignment can be separate)

new_start_time is in the future

If invalid:

Log reschedule_invalid with reason.

Optionally return error via backend (e.g., “Cannot reschedule a completed job”).

Stop workflow.

🟣 Node 4 — Compute Timing Buckets
Calculate:

t_request = now()

t_start_original = job.start_time

t_start_new = payload.new_start_time

hours_before_original = (t_start_original - t_request) in hours

Decide bucket:

>48h → 'gt48'

24–48h → '24_48'

<24h → 'lt24'

Store these for the DB insert.

🟣 Node 5 — Check Cleaner Availability for New Time
Call availability logic:

Input:

cleaner_id

new_start_time

new_end_time (= new_start_time + duration)

Output:

{
  "available": true,
  "reason": "ok" // or 'outside_hours' | 'blackout' | 'conflict_existing_job'
}
🟣 Node 6 — Determine is_reasonable Request
We define reasonable as:

Cleaner is available (available: true)

New start time is not crazy far out (e.g., within 7 days of original)

This is not the 3rd+ reschedule attempt for this job

Request happens before original start time

In the workflow:

Count previous reschedule events for this job:

SELECT COUNT(*) FROM reschedule_events
WHERE job_id = :job_id;
Set is_reasonable:

is_reasonable = (
  available == true
  AND abs(days_between_original_and_new) <= 7
  AND previous_reschedule_count < 2
  AND t_request < t_start_original
)
You can tune those rules, but that’s the idea.

🟣 Node 7 — Build requested_to & Target User
If:

requested_by = 'client' → requested_to = 'cleaner'

requested_by = 'cleaner' → requested_to = 'client'

Also determine:

The user ID of the receiving party (for notifications).

🟣 Node 8 — Insert reschedule_events Row
Write:

INSERT INTO reschedule_events (
  job_id,
  client_id,
  cleaner_id,
  requested_by,
  requested_to,
  t_request,
  t_start_original,
  t_start_new,
  hours_before_original,
  bucket,
  reason_code,
  status,
  is_reasonable,
  metadata
) VALUES (
  :job_id,
  :client_id,
  :cleaner_id,
  :requested_by,
  :requested_to,
  :t_request,
  :t_start_original,
  :t_start_new,
  :hours_before_original,
  :bucket,
  :reason_code,
  'pending',
  :is_reasonable,
  '{}'
)
RETURNING id;
Store returned reschedule_event_id for the next steps + API response.

🟣 Node 9 — (Optional) Auto-Accept Cases
You may want to auto-accept reschedules that are:

bucket = 'gt48'

is_reasonable = true

New time still within declared availability

And maybe same day or small shift

If conditions are met:

Directly update jobs.start_time to t_start_new.

Set reschedule_events.status = 'accepted'.

Send notifications to both parties: “Reschedule confirmed”.

Skip the pending state entirely.

If not auto-accepted:

Leave status as pending.

Continue to notifications for the receiving party.

🟣 Node 10 — Notify Receiving Party
If not auto-accepted:

Send a push/in-app notification to requested_to:

If cleaner is receiving:

“[Client Name] requested to reschedule your cleaning from [old time] to [new time].”

If client receiving:

“[Cleaner Name] requested to reschedule your cleaning from [old time] to [new time].”

Include:

New time

Original time

Buttons: Accept / Decline (handled in Reschedule Response Workflow 4)

🟣 Node 11 — Schedule Expiration (Optional)
You can optionally enforce a time limit for response.

Example: reschedule request expires after 12–24 hours or at t_start_original, whichever comes first.

Schedule a delayed job:

At min(t_start_original, now + 24h)

If still status = 'pending' at expiration:

Auto-decline or notify requester to choose: keep time or cancel.

This helps avoid “stuck pending” jobs.

🟣 Node 12 — Error Handling
For DB writes or availability checks:

On failure:

Log job_reschedule_request_failed with:

job_id

requested_by

new_start_time

error message

Optionally retry

If multiple retries fail, notify support.

🔹 Summary of Workflow 3 Effects
On a successful job_reschedule_requested flow:

Valid reschedule request is logged in reschedule_events.

We know:

who asked,

when,

original & new times,

time bucket,

whether it was “reasonable”.

Receiving party is notified and can accept/decline.

Auto-accept can optionally happen for safe/simple cases.

No penalties or risk changes yet — that happens on accept/decline and later cancellation.

🔹 Where This Connects
Workflow 4 (Reschedule Response) uses reschedule_event_id and is_reasonable.

Risk & Reliability engines later use:

bucket

requested_by

whether it was accepted/declined

Low Flex Badge uses:

is_reasonable = true AND status = 'declined' (by cleaner)

If this matches how you want reschedules to behave, we’ll move to:

WORKFLOW 4 / 12 — Reschedule Response Workflow
(What happens when the other side hits Accept or Decline.)

If you’re ready, just say:

“Proceed with Workflow 4.”


proceeed

Got you — let’s finish the reschedule loop 🔁

✅ WORKFLOW 4 / 12 — Reschedule Response Workflow
Event: the other party Accepts or Declines a reschedule request.

This is the partner to Workflow 3.

Goal:
When the receiving party taps Accept or Decline, we:

Update reschedule_events

Optionally update the job time

Trigger risk / reliability events (if late + accepted)

Keep original booking if declined

Notify both sides

Optionally trigger cancellation if the requester then can’t make it

This is wrapped around the API:
POST /jobs/:jobId/reschedule/respond

🔹 Trigger
Event name: job_reschedule_responded

Source:

Client or cleaner taps Accept/Decline in app

Backend validates permissions, then POSTs to workflow:

Example payload:

{
  "event": "job_reschedule_responded",
  "job_id": 999,
  "reschedule_event_id": 1234,
  "action": "accept",                   // or "decline"
  "actor_type": "cleaner",              // 'client' or 'cleaner'
  "decline_reason_code": null           // set when action = 'decline'
}
🔹 Workflow Steps (Node-by-node)
🟣 Node 1 — Webhook Trigger
Trigger only when event == "job_reschedule_responded".

🟣 Node 2 — Load Reschedule Event + Job
Queries:

SELECT * FROM reschedule_events WHERE id = :reschedule_event_id

SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = :job_id

Validate:

reschedule_events.job_id == job_id

reschedule_events.status == 'pending'

Job status is still reschedulable (accepted / scheduled)

If any invalid:

Log reschedule_response_invalid

Stop workflow (return error to app).

🟣 Node 3 — Validate Actor
We must ensure only the requested_to party can respond.

Check: actor_type == reschedule_event.requested_to

If mismatch:

Log reschedule_response_unauthorized

Return error (do not continue).

🟣 Node 4 — Branch on Action: ACCEPT vs DECLINE
✅ PATH A — ACCEPT
If action == 'accept':

🟣 Node A1 — Update Job Times
Use t_start_new from reschedule_events.

Update:

UPDATE jobs
SET start_time = reschedule_events.t_start_new,
    updated_at = now()
WHERE id = :job_id;
Optionally recompute end_time if duration is fixed.

🟣 Node A2 — Update reschedule_events Status
UPDATE reschedule_events
SET status = 'accepted',
    updated_at = now()
WHERE id = :reschedule_event_id;
🟣 Node A3 — Risk / Reliability Logging (if needed)
We don’t adjust scores directly here, but we log events to be processed by the engines.

Look at:

requested_by (client or cleaner)

bucket (gt48, 24_48, lt24)

is_reasonable (true/false)

Case 1 — Client requested, accepted by cleaner:

If bucket = 'lt24' (late change):

Insert client_risk_events:

INSERT INTO client_risk_events (client_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata)
VALUES (:client_id, :job_id, 'late_reschedule_lt24', 1, '{"source":"reschedule_accept"}');
Later, the Risk engine may:

Convert 3+ such events in 14 days to a pattern event (late_reschedule_pattern, +10).

Case 2 — Cleaner requested, accepted by client:

If bucket = 'lt24':

Insert cleaner_events:

INSERT INTO cleaner_events (cleaner_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata)
VALUES (:cleaner_id, :job_id, 'late_reschedule', -3, '{"source":"reschedule_accept"}');
No immediate score change — just logged.

🟣 Node A4 — Notify Both Parties
Use Notification service:

To client:

“Your cleaning has been rescheduled to [new date/time].”

To cleaner:

“Your cleaning with [Client Name] has been rescheduled to [new date/time].”

Include:

Job id

New start time

Any reminders.

🟣 Node A5 — Optional: Inconvenience Prompt
If bucket = 'lt24' and show_inconvenience_prompt_ui flag is ON:

Schedule or trigger an in-app modal for the non-requesting party:

If client requested and cleaner accepted → ask the cleaner:

“How inconvenient was this last-minute change?”

If cleaner requested and client accepted → ask the client.

Result will be captured via POST /jobs/:jobId/inconvenience → inconvenience_logs.

🟣 Node A6 — Done (Accept Path)
Return to backend:

status = accepted

new_start_time

✅ PATH B — DECLINE
If action == 'decline':

🟣 Node B1 — Update reschedule_events as Declined
UPDATE reschedule_events
SET status = 'declined',
    declined_by = :actor_type,
    decline_reason_code = :decline_reason_code,
    updated_at = now()
WHERE id = :reschedule_event_id;
Important: we do NOT change jobs.start_time.
The job remains at the original time.

🟣 Node B2 — Low Flexibility Badge Signal (for cleaner)
If:

actor_type = 'cleaner'

requested_by = 'client'

is_reasonable = true

bucket can be anything (usually <24h matters more, but we can log all)

Then:

We do not immediately give a badge, but we’ve just recorded a data point that will be counted by the nightly badge maintenance job.

Nothing else needed here for scoring — the pattern detection flow will handle it.

🟣 Node B3 — Notify Requester
Send notification to the requested_by party:

If client requested and cleaner declined:

“Your cleaner could not accept the new time. Your original appointment on [old date/time] is still active.”

If cleaner requested and client declined:

“The client couldn’t accept the new time. The original appointment on [old date/time] is still active.”

This is critical so the requester knows the job is still happening at the original time unless they cancel.

🟣 Node B4 — Optional: Push to Cancellation Suggestion Flow
If the requester declined reason suggests they can’t make the original time either:

e.g., reason_code = 'client_cannot_make_original_time'

You may want to:

Trigger a UI prompt to the requester:

“You declined the reschedule, but your original appointment is still scheduled. If you can’t attend, you may cancel — fees may apply.”

This can be handled on the app side using metadata in the response, not necessarily in automation.

🟣 Node B5 — Optional: Inconvenience Prompt for Requester
If bucket = 'lt24' and this decline causes stress for the requesting party, you may prompt them for inconvenience feedback.

It’s a product choice:

If client requested very late and cleaner declines → arguably that’s reasonable, so inconvenience prompt might not be necessary.

If cleaner requested late and client declines → client may feel “stuck”.

You can decide to only prompt for certain branches.

🟣 Node B6 — Done (Decline Path)
Return to backend:

status = 'declined'

original_start_time

Job stays as-is.

🔹 Error Handling & Idempotency
For reschedule responses, we must guard against double-clicking or retries.

Case: same reschedule_event_id responded twice

Before updating, always check:

If status != 'pending', do NOT re-apply.

Return a 409 / “already responded” error to backend.

On DB or workflow failure:

Log reschedule_response_failed with:

job_id

reschedule_event_id

actor_type

action

error

Configure retry for transient DB issues.

If a permanent failure, support can manually adjust reschedule_events and jobs.

🔹 How This Ties into the Whole System
After this workflow:

The reschedule event is finalized (accepted or declined).

Risk / reliability event logs are created (for late reschedules).

Low Flexibility badge has fresh data via is_reasonable + declined_by='cleaner'.

Inconvenience logs can be collected.

Job timing is correctly updated (or preserved).

This fully closes the loop started in Workflow 3.

(When a job is canceled, how we compute fees, move credits, log events, and update scores.)

Alright, time to handle the money + pain point: cancellations 💸

✅ WORKFLOW 5 / 12 — Cancellation Workflow
Event: client or cleaner cancels a job.

Goal:
When someone cancels:

We decide what bucket it’s in (gt48, 24_48, lt24, or no_show)

We compute fees, refunds, and payouts

We move credits accordingly

We log cancellation_events

We log risk & reliability events

We update job status

We notify both parties

This workflow wraps the POST /jobs/:jobId/cancel endpoint, plus is reused by no-show logic.

🔹 Trigger
Event name: job_cancelled_requested

Source:

Client taps “Cancel booking”

Cleaner taps “Cancel job”

Backend validates auth and sends:

{
  "event": "job_cancelled_requested",
  "job_id": 999,
  "cancelled_by": "client",             // 'client' | 'cleaner' | 'system'
  "reason_code": "client_schedule_conflict",
  "use_grace_if_available": true,
  "actor_user_id": 123
}
🔹 Workflow Steps (Node-by-node)
🟣 Node 1 — Webhook Trigger
Trigger when event == "job_cancelled_requested".

🟣 Node 2 — Load Job, Client, Cleaner
Queries:

SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = :job_id

SELECT * FROM clients WHERE id = jobs.client_id

SELECT * FROM cleaners WHERE id = jobs.cleaner_id (if assigned)

Validate:

Job exists

Job status is cancellable (scheduled / accepted)

Job is not already cancelled / completed / no_show_*

If invalid:

Log cancel_invalid

Return error to app.

🟣 Node 3 — Compute Timing & Bucket
Calculate:

t_now = now()

t_start = jobs.start_time

hours_before_start = (t_start - t_now) in hours

Decide bucket:

If no-show logic calling this:

bucket = 'no_show'

Else normal:

>48h → 'gt48'

24–48h → '24_48'

<24h → 'lt24'

If hours_before_start < 0 and we’re here via manual cancel → treat like lt24 or no-show depending on your rule.

🟣 Node 4 — Determine Grace Usage (Client Only)
If cancelled_by == 'client':

Check:

clients.grace_cancellations_used < grace_cancellations_total

bucket != 'no_show' (no grace on no-show)

If use_grace_if_available == true AND allowed:

grace_used = true

Else:

grace_used = false

If cancelled_by != 'client':

grace_used = false

We’ll use this when computing fee_pct.

🟣 Node 5 — Compute fee_pct
Use your policy logic:

If cancelled_by = client:

If grace_used = true → fee_pct = 0

Else:

bucket = 'gt48' → fee_pct = 0

bucket = '24_48' → fee_pct = 50

bucket = 'lt24' → fee_pct = 100

bucket = 'no_show' → fee_pct = 100

If cancelled_by = cleaner:

Client should not be penalized:

Typically: fee_pct = 0 from client’s perspective

All held credits refunded to client or re-used for another booking

Later, we log a reliability penalty for the cleaner.

You can refine these rules, but that’s the skeleton.

🟣 Node 6 — Compute Credits & Splits
Let:

held = jobs.held_credits

Then:

fee_credits = floor(held * fee_pct / 100)

refund_credits = held - fee_credits

For client cancellations where fee > 0:

Decide cleaner/platform split (e.g., 70/30 or 80/20):

cleaner_comp_credits  = fee_credits * cleaner_pct
platform_comp_credits = fee_credits - cleaner_comp_credits
For no fees:

cleaner_comp_credits = 0

platform_comp_credits = 0

For cleaner cancellations:

refund_credits = held

fee_credits = 0

cleaner_comp_credits = 0

platform_comp_credits = 0

🟣 Node 7 — Perform Credit Transfers (Transactional)
All balance changes must happen in a DB transaction.

Within transaction:

Client:

Increase client.credits by refund_credits

Cleaner:

If cleaner_comp_credits > 0:

Increase cleaner.pending_credits (or equivalent “to be paid out”)

Platform:

If platform_comp_credits > 0:

Insert into platform ledger / balance

(Optionally) Mark job escrow as cleared or zero out jobs.held_credits.

If transaction fails:

Log cancel_funds_transfer_failed

Retry or alert.

🟣 Node 8 — Insert cancellation_events Row
After successful transaction:

INSERT INTO cancellation_events (
  job_id,
  cancelled_by,
  t_cancel,
  hours_before_start,
  bucket,
  reason_code,
  after_reschedule_declined,
  fee_pct,
  fee_credits,
  refund_credits,
  cleaner_comp_credits,
  platform_comp_credits,
  grace_used,
  metadata
) VALUES (
  :job_id,
  :cancelled_by,
  :t_now,
  :hours_before_start,
  :bucket,
  :reason_code,
  :after_reschedule_declined,   -- true if last reschedule was declined by other party
  :fee_pct,
  :fee_credits,
  :refund_credits,
  :cleaner_comp_credits,
  :platform_comp_credits,
  :grace_used,
  '{}'::jsonb
)
RETURNING id;
The after_reschedule_declined flag is set if:

There was a recent reschedule request that was declined (particularly important when client is forced to cancel after cleaner declines).

🟣 Node 9 — Risk & Reliability Event Logging
Now we add scoring events, not scores.

If cancelled_by = client:

If bucket = '24_48' and NOT grace_used:

Insert client_risk_events:

event_type = 'cancel_24_48', weight = 3

If bucket = 'lt24' and NOT grace_used:

event_type = 'cancel_lt24', weight = 5

If bucket = 'no_show':

event_type = 'no_show', weight = 20

If cancelled_by = cleaner:

If bucket = '24_48':

Insert cleaner_events:

event_type = 'cancel_24_48', weight = -8

If bucket = 'lt24':

event_type = 'cancel_lt24', weight = -12

If bucket = 'no_show':

event_type = 'no_show', weight = -25

Note: these weights match what we discussed conceptually; you can tweak values later.

🟣 Node 10 — Update Job Status
Set status based on context:

If reached via normal cancel:

status = 'cancelled'

If triggered via a no-show flow:

status = 'no_show_client' or 'no_show_cleaner'

UPDATE jobs
SET status = :new_status,
    updated_at = now()
WHERE id = :job_id;
🟣 Node 11 — Notify Both Parties
Use Notification Service:

For client cancellation:

To client:

“Your booking has been cancelled. [Fee / refund summary].”

To cleaner:

“[Client Name] cancelled the job scheduled for [date/time]. You’ll receive [X] credits based on our policy (if any).”

For cleaner cancellation:

To cleaner:

“You’ve cancelled the job. Clients may see this in your reliability score.”

To client:

“[Cleaner Name] had to cancel your job. You’ve been fully refunded. You can rebook with another cleaner.”

Include clear fee breakdown:

Held credits

Fee amount

Refund amount

Grace usage if applicable

🟣 Node 12 — Inconvenience Prompt Trigger (Optional)
If:

bucket = 'lt24' or 'no_show'

AND show_inconvenience_prompt_ui is ON

Then:

Trigger an in-app modal for the counterparty asking:

“How inconvenient was this cancellation for you?”

The results go through POST /jobs/:jobId/inconvenience → inconvenience_logs.

🟣 Node 13 — Error Handling & Idempotency
Idempotency key: job_id + cancelled_by + t_cancel_rounded or, better, a cancellation token your backend provides.

Before processing, check:

If job already has a cancellation_events row:

Return idempotent response: “Job already cancelled”.

On any step failing:

Log cancel_workflow_failed + context

Roll back transaction for money movements

Alert support if funds are in unknown state

🔹 Reuse for No-Show Workflow
The No-Show Workflow (Workflow 6) can simply:

Detect no-show condition (no check-in, etc.)

Call this same Cancellation Workflow with:

cancelled_by = 'system' (or client/cleaner depending on blame)

bucket = 'no_show'

reason_code = 'no_show'

So we only maintain one fee/credit engine.

🔹 Why This Workflow Is Critical
This is where:

Your revenue,

Cleaner protection, and

Client fairness

are all enforced.

If this is stable, clear, and transparent, your marketplace feels professional and trustworthy.

If this cancellation workflow matches what you want, the next one in the map is:

🧩 Thing We Are Building: Workflow 6 — No-Show Workflow
What this workflow must handle
When a client or cleaner doesn’t show up for a job, this workflow must:

Detect the no-show condition (based on check-in / time rules)

Decide who is at fault (client vs cleaner)

Apply the same cancellation engine as Workflow 5, but with bucket = 'no_show'

Move credits correctly:

Client no-show → usually client pays, cleaner gets comp

Cleaner no-show → client refunded, cleaner penalized

Log:

cancellation_events (with bucket no_show)

client_risk_events or cleaner_events (big weights)

Update jobs.status to:

no_show_client or no_show_cleaner

Trigger notifications

Optionally prompt for Inconvenience rating

What this workflow depends on
To operate correctly, it needs:

Tables already defined:

jobs

cancellation_events

client_risk_events

cleaner_events

inconvenience_logs (optional)

Data from other parts of system:

Check-in/check-out logs (or fields on jobs)

Scheduled start time

Policies we already agreed on:

No-show is treated like worst-case cancellation

Client no-show → strong risk penalty

Cleaner no-show → strong reliability penalty

Existing workflows:

Reuses Cancellation Workflow (Workflow 5) instead of duplicating fee logic

Now I’ll build the workflow step-by-step.

✅ WORKFLOW 6 / 12 — No-Show Workflow
Event: job time passes and either client or cleaner never shows.

1️⃣ Trigger: No-Show Detection
You can do this two ways (or both):

Scheduled Check (cron-based)

A cron job runs every X minutes:

Fetch jobs where:

status = 'accepted'

start_time < now() - grace_window (e.g. 30 minutes)

No check-in recorded

For each such job, determine fault and emit job_no_show_detected.

Event-Driven Timer

When job is accepted, schedule a delayed job at start_time + grace_window

At that time, check if the relevant party checked in

If not → emit job_no_show_detected.

Standard payload for the no-show detection event:

{
  "event": "job_no_show_detected",
  "job_id": 999,
  "suspected_no_show": "client",  // or "cleaner"
  "detected_at": "2025-03-14T10:45:00Z"
}
2️⃣ Workflow Steps (Node-by-node)
🟣 Node 1 — Webhook / Event Trigger
Triggers on job_no_show_detected.

🟣 Node 2 — Load Job & Context
Fetch:

jobs row by job_id

clients row

cleaners row

Check-in records (however you store them):

e.g. job.checkin_time, job.checkout_time, or a job_checkins table

Validate:

Job exists

Job hasn’t already been completed/cancelled/no_show_*

If invalid:

Log no_show_invalid and stop.

🟣 Node 3 — Decide Who Actually No-Showed (Fault Logic)
We use business rules to decide fault.

Example rules:

If cleaner never checked in AND job has a valid address + no “access issue” reason → likely cleaner no-show.

If cleaner was on-site (check-in logged) but client never opened door / wasn’t reachable → client no-show.

If evidence is unclear → mark as system and send to support instead of auto-penalizing.

Implementation:

Check:

has_cleaner_checkin = (job.checkin_time IS NOT NULL)

client_reported_issue or cleaner_reported_issue (if you capture these)

Decide:

if suspected_no_show = 'cleaner' AND !has_cleaner_checkin:
    no_show_type = 'cleaner'
elif suspected_no_show = 'client' AND has_cleaner_checkin:
    no_show_type = 'client'
else:
    no_show_type = 'unclear'  -- send to support/manual review
If unclear:

Log no_show_unclear

Notify support

Stop or require manual resolution.

🟣 Node 4 — Map No-Show to Cancellation Call
Now that we know no_show_type (client or cleaner), we reuse the Cancellation Workflow (Workflow 5) by synthesizing a job_cancelled_requested event:

For client no-show:

{
  "event": "job_cancelled_requested",
  "job_id": 999,
  "cancelled_by": "client",          // or 'system' with metadata.fault='client'
  "reason_code": "no_show",
  "use_grace_if_available": false
}
For cleaner no-show:

{
  "event": "job_cancelled_requested",
  "job_id": 999,
  "cancelled_by": "cleaner",         // or 'system' with metadata.fault='cleaner'
  "reason_code": "no_show",
  "use_grace_if_available": false
}
You can either:

Literally fire another workflow/event into Workflow 5, or

Call the same internal function used by that workflow.

Important:
For no-shows, we always set bucket = 'no_show' in the cancellation logic.

5️⃣ Inside Cancellation (Reused Logic)
From Workflow 5, with some specifics:

bucket = 'no_show'

Fee rules:

Client no-show:

fee_pct = 100 (client loses full held credits)

Most (or all) goes to cleaner as comp, some can go to platform

Cleaner no-show:

fee_pct = 0 (client refunded fully)

Credit movements:

Client no-show:

refund_credits = 0

cleaner_comp_credits = held * cleaner_pct (e.g. 70–85%)

platform_comp_credits = held - cleaner_comp_credits

Cleaner no-show:

refund_credits = held

cleaner_comp_credits = 0

platform_comp_credits = 0

cancellation_events row:

bucket = 'no_show'

reason_code = 'no_show'

Score events:

Client no-show → client_risk_events:

event_type = 'no_show', weight = 20

Cleaner no-show → cleaner_events:

event_type = 'no_show', weight = -25

6️⃣ Update Job Status
After cancellation logic succeeds:

For client no-show:

UPDATE jobs
SET status = 'no_show_client', updated_at = now()
WHERE id = :job_id;
For cleaner no-show:

UPDATE jobs
SET status = 'no_show_cleaner', updated_at = now()
WHERE id = :job_id;
This makes job state clear in dashboards and UI.

7️⃣ Notifications
Client no-show:

To client:

“You were marked as a no-show for your cleaning on [date/time].
Credits for this booking were not refunded, according to our policy.”

To cleaner:

“Your client was a no-show. You’ll receive [X] credits for your time.”

Cleaner no-show:

To cleaner:

“You were marked as a no-show. This negatively affects your reliability score.”

To client:

“[Cleaner Name] did not arrive for your booking. You’ve been fully refunded. You can rebook with another cleaner.”

Use templates that match your tone but stay clear and respectful.

8️⃣ Optional: Inconvenience Prompts
Because no-shows are max inconvenience, you can optionally:

For client no-show:

Ask the cleaner if they want to rate inconvenience (but it’s obvious 4/4, so might be redundant).

For cleaner no-show:

Ask the client if they want to share details (could help support if there’s a pattern).

All of this goes to inconvenience_logs, later used for patterns.

9️⃣ Error Handling & Safety
Ensure idempotency:

If a job has already been processed as no-show or cancelled, do not run the cancellation engine again.

If no-show detection fires twice:

Check jobs.status:

If status IN ('no_show_client','no_show_cleaner','cancelled') → ignore.

Log:

no_show_flow_failed with job_id + reason.

🔚 Summary of Workflow 6
Thing built: No-Show Workflow

It now:

Uses time + check-in logic to detect no-shows

Decides who’s at fault (client vs cleaner)

Reuses the Cancellation Workflow with bucket = 'no_show'

Moves credits appropriately

Logs:

cancellation_events

client_risk_events or cleaner_events

Updates jobs.status to no_show_client / no_show_cleaner

Triggers proper notifications

Optionally prompts inconvenience scores

This keeps no-shows consistent with your overall cancellation and scoring logic.

(GPS check-in/out, punctuality, completion confirmation, photo proof → feeds reliability score.)

🧩 Thing We Are Building: Workflow 7 — Check-in / Check-out & Completion Workflow
What this workflow must handle
This workflow is responsible for all the on-the-day execution signals:

Cleaner GPS check-in at job start

Cleaner GPS check-out at job end

Punctuality calculation (on-time vs late)

Marking attendance (did the cleaner actually show)

Confirming photos are uploaded (before/after)

Confirming job completion (GPS + photos)

Updating cleaner_metrics & logging cleaner_events that feed Reliability 2.0

Triggering rating flow after completion

What it depends on
To operate correctly, it relies on:

Tables:

jobs

cleaner_metrics

cleaner_events

(optionally) job_photos or similar

Existing flows:

Job has been accepted (Workflow 2)

No-show workflow uses absence of check-in info

Policies we defined:

On-time = GPS check-in within 15 minutes of scheduled start (early is OK)

Attendance = any valid check-in before end_time

Completion = check-out + photos

App behavior:

Cleaner taps “Check In” and “Check Out” in the app, sending GPS & timestamps

Now I’ll build the full automation flow.

✅ WORKFLOW 7 / 12 — Check-in / Check-out & Completion Workflow
We’ll treat this as two related event flows:

job_checked_in

job_checked_out (and completion)

1️⃣ Check-in Flow — job_checked_in
🔹 Trigger
Event name: job_checked_in

Source (app → backend → workflow):

{
  "event": "job_checked_in",
  "job_id": 999,
  "cleaner_id": 555,
  "checkin_time": "2025-03-14T09:58:00Z",
  "gps": {
    "lat": 37.7749,
    "lng": -122.4194,
    "accuracy_meters": 15
  }
}
🔹 Node-by-node Steps
🟣 Node 1 — Webhook Trigger
Trigger only when event == "job_checked_in".

🟣 Node 2 — Load Job & Cleaner
Query:

SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = :job_id

Confirm jobs.cleaner_id == cleaner_id from payload.

Validate:

Job status is accepted (or scheduled)

Job not cancelled/no_show/completed

If invalid:

Log checkin_invalid and stop.

🟣 Node 3 — Validate GPS (Basic)
Rules (you can tune these):

Check that GPS coordinates are not null.

Optionally confirm distance to job address is within X meters (if you store client coords).

If way off:

Mark metadata in the event:

gps_valid = false

Still log, but maybe flag for review.

🟣 Node 4 — Compute Punctuality
Let:

t_start = jobs.start_time

t_checkin = checkin_time

Compute:

delta_minutes = (t_checkin - t_start) in minutes

Define punctuality:

If delta_minutes <= 15 and delta_minutes >= -60 (up to 1h early) → on-time

If delta_minutes > 15 → late

If delta_minutes < -60 (way too early) → treat as early but still on-time or flag – your choice

Set flags:

attended = true
on_time = (delta_minutes <= 15)
🟣 Node 5 — Update Job Status
Set:

jobs.status = 'in_progress'

jobs.checkin_time = t_checkin

Optionally store jobs.checkin_gps = gps json

🟣 Node 6 — Update cleaner_metrics for Attendance
In cleaner_metrics row for this cleaner:

total_jobs_window += 1 (if you count at start)

attended_jobs += 1

If on_time:

on_time_checkins += 1

You can also choose to increment total_jobs_window at completion instead; just be consistent.

🟣 Node 7 — Log cleaner_events (Optional)
You can log punctuality as events for reliability:

Always log:

INSERT INTO cleaner_events (cleaner_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata)
VALUES (
  :cleaner_id,
  :job_id,
  'checkin',
  0,
  jsonb_build_object(
    'delta_minutes', :delta_minutes,
    'on_time', :on_time
  )
);
If very late (e.g., delta_minutes > 30), you might add a small negative event:

INSERT INTO cleaner_events (cleaner_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata)
VALUES (
  :cleaner_id,
  :job_id,
  'late_checkin',
  -2,
  jsonb_build_object('delta_minutes', :delta_minutes)
);
(You can also handle this in batch later instead.)

🟣 Node 8 — Notify Client (Optional)
If you want:

Send notification to client:

“Your cleaner has arrived and started your cleaning.”

This increases trust.

🟣 Node 9 — Error Handling
If any DB update fails:

Log checkin_flow_failed with job_id, cleaner_id, error

Retry or alert support if persistent.

2️⃣ Check-out & Completion Flow — job_checked_out
🔹 Trigger
Event name: job_checked_out

Source:

{
  "event": "job_checked_out",
  "job_id": 999,
  "cleaner_id": 555,
  "checkout_time": "2025-03-14T13:05:00Z",
  "gps": {
    "lat": 37.7750,
    "lng": -122.4193
  }
}
🔹 Node-by-node Steps
🟣 Node 1 — Webhook Trigger
Trigger when event == "job_checked_out".

🟣 Node 2 — Load Job & Cleaner
Query:

SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = :job_id

Verify jobs.cleaner_id == cleaner_id.

Confirm jobs.status = 'in_progress'.

If invalid:

Log checkout_invalid

Stop.

🟣 Node 3 — Validate GPS (basic like check-in)
Confirm non-null GPS.

Optionally check within range of job address.

If invalid, log metadata but still proceed.

🟣 Node 4 — Confirm Photos & Completion Requirements
If you require photo proof:

Query job_photos (or your equivalent) for this job:

Count how many photos exist

Confirm at least 3 total (before+after)

If not enough photos:

Option 1: block check-out in the app (best UX)

Option 2: allow check-out but mark:

photo_compliant = (photo_count >= 3)
🟣 Node 5 — Mark Job Completed
Update jobs:

UPDATE jobs
SET status       = 'completed',
    checkout_time = :checkout_time,
    updated_at   = now()
WHERE id = :job_id;
You can also log total duration difference if needed.

🟣 Node 6 — Update cleaner_metrics for Completion
In cleaner_metrics for this cleaner & window:

completion_ok_jobs += 1

If photo_compliant:

photo_compliant_jobs += 1

If you track communication:

If there was at least one message exchange (fetched from messages table), increment:

communication_ok_jobs += 1

🟣 Node 7 — Log cleaner_events for Completion Proof
Insert event:

INSERT INTO cleaner_events (cleaner_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata)
VALUES (
  :cleaner_id,
  :job_id,
  'job_completed',
  0,
  jsonb_build_object(
    'photo_compliant', :photo_compliant,
    'has_checkout_gps', true
  )
);
If photo_compliant = false, you may also log:

INSERT INTO cleaner_events (cleaner_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata)
VALUES (
  :cleaner_id,
  :job_id,
  'missing_photos',
  -3,
  '{}'::jsonb
);
That -3 feeds into Reliability 2.0.

🟣 Node 8 — Trigger Rating Flow
After completion:

Schedule or immediately send a rating prompt to the client:

“How was your cleaning with [Cleaner Name]?” (1–5 stars)

You can do this via:

Notification Service → links to rating screen

Or an in-app auto-modal

Once rating is submitted, another workflow (not this one) will:

Insert rating

Update cleaner_metrics.ratings_sum + ratings_count

Possibly log cleaner_events e.g. rating_5, rating_1 etc.

🟣 Node 9 — Signal Payout / Earnings Flow (Future)
Optionally emit event:

{
  "event": "job_completed_for_payout",
  "job_id": 999,
  "cleaner_id": 555
}
This would tie into your payouts / escrow release workflows (which you already have in your bigger system).

🟣 Node 10 — Error Handling
If job status update fails, log checkout_status_update_failed.

If metric updates fail, log checkout_metrics_failed.

Make sure payout-related events don’t fire if the job wasn’t truly completed.

🔚 Summary of Workflow 7
Thing built: Check-in/Check-out & Completion Workflow

Now it:

Logs cleaner attendance and punctuality from check-in

Moves job → in_progress on check-in

Confirms photo compliance + completion via check-out

Moves job → completed

Updates cleaner_metrics for:

attendance

on-time rate

completion

photo proof

Logs cleaner_events that our Reliability Engine uses

Kicks off rating & payout flows

This is a major backbone of Reliability Score 2.0.

Next in our workflow roadmap is:

Workflow 8 — Inconvenience Log Workflow
(When a party submits “how inconvenient was this?” after a reschedule/cancel/no-show and how we log & later use that.)

If you want to keep going, just say:

“Proceed with Workflow 8.”


proceed

Love the momentum, let’s keep it clean and structured 👇

🧩 Thing We Are Building: Workflow 8 — Inconvenience Log Workflow
What this workflow must handle
This is the “human feelings” layer.

When a client or cleaner answers:

“How inconvenient was this?” (1–4)

after a reschedule, cancellation, or no-show, this workflow must:

Validate who is rating and what event they’re rating

Record the inconvenience into inconvenience_logs

Tag who caused the inconvenience (client vs cleaner)

Tag what it’s tied to:

reschedule

cancellation

no_show

Do nothing punitive immediately

Feed future pattern detection jobs that:

Add risk events to clients who constantly inconvenience cleaners

Add reliability penalties to cleaners who constantly inconvenience clients

What it depends on
It relies on:

Tables:

inconvenience_logs

reschedule_events

cancellation_events

(sometimes) jobs, client_risk_events, cleaner_events

The user-facing endpoint:

POST /jobs/:jobId/inconvenience

Policies we decided:

Score scale: 1–4

High scores (3–4) = meaningful inconvenience

Pattern detection happens in a nightly batch, not real-time here

Now we wire the workflow.

✅ WORKFLOW 8 / 12 — Inconvenience Log Workflow
This is triggered whenever someone submits the inconvenience form in the app.

1️⃣ Trigger
Event name: job_inconvenience_submitted

Source:

The app calls POST /jobs/:jobId/inconvenience, backend validates and then posts to automation:

{
  "event": "job_inconvenience_submitted",
  "job_id": 999,
  "client_id": 123,
  "cleaner_id": 555,
  "rated_by": "cleaner",           // or 'client'
  "caused_by": "client",           // or 'cleaner'
  "score": 3,                      // 1..4
  "related_event_type": "reschedule",   // 'reschedule' | 'cancel' | 'no_show'
  "related_event_id": 321,              // id in reschedule_events or cancellation_events
  "reason_code": "client_schedule_conflict",
  "note": "Changed time the same morning and I lost another job."
}
2️⃣ Workflow Steps (Node-by-node)
🟣 Node 1 — Webhook Trigger
Fire only on event == "job_inconvenience_submitted".

🟣 Node 2 — Basic Validation
Check:

score is between 1 and 4

rated_by in (client, cleaner)

caused_by in (client, cleaner)

related_event_type in (reschedule, cancel, no_show)

If any invalid:

Log inconvenience_invalid_payload with job_id

Stop.

🟣 Node 3 — Load Job & Event Context
Queries:

SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = :job_id

If related_event_type = 'reschedule':

SELECT * FROM reschedule_events WHERE id = :related_event_id

If related_event_type IN ('cancel','no_show'):

SELECT * FROM cancellation_events WHERE id = :related_event_id

Validate:

That the job_id on the related event matches this job_id.

That the rated_by user is indeed part of the job (client or cleaner).

If mismatched:

Log inconvenience_event_mismatch and stop.

🟣 Node 4 — Insert into inconvenience_logs
Create a single authoritative log row:

INSERT INTO inconvenience_logs (
  job_id,
  client_id,
  cleaner_id,
  caused_by,
  rated_by,
  score,
  related_event_type,
  related_event_id,
  reason_code,
  note,
  created_at
) VALUES (
  :job_id,
  :client_id,
  :cleaner_id,
  :caused_by,
  :rated_by,
  :score,
  :related_event_type,
  :related_event_id,
  :reason_code,
  :note,
  now()
)
RETURNING id;
No scoring changes directly here.

This is pure data collection.

🟣 Node 5 — Optional: Immediate UX Feedback
You can send a simple acknowledgement (via backend / app, not necessarily automation):

“Thanks, your feedback has been recorded. We use this to improve reliability and fairness on the platform.”

No penalties visible here.

🟣 Node 6 — Optional: Trigger Support Flag for Extreme Cases
If:

score = 4

AND related_event_type = 'no_show'

AND caused_by = 'cleaner' (or repeated caused_by = 'client' for same pair)

You may:

Emit event: support_review_recommended with:

job_id, client_id, cleaner_id, score, notes

This lets human support manually review egregious cases.

🟣 Node 7 — Error Handling
On any DB error:

Log inconvenience_log_failed with context.

Optionally retry.

Worst case: user’s feedback is lost, but core booking logic is unaffected.

🔁 How This Connects to Patterns & Scores
Workflow 8 only logs. The actual “use this to tweak scores” happens in batch (we already defined that in Item 7 – Batch Jobs).

Recap of that connection:

Nightly Inconvenience Pattern Job reads inconvenience_logs:

For clients (caused_by = 'client', score >= 3):

If ≥ 3 in 14 days → add client_risk_events (inconvenience_pattern, +5)

If ≥ 5 in 14 days → add another +5

For cleaners (caused_by = 'cleaner', score >= 3):

If ≥ 3 in 30 days → add cleaner_events (inconvenience_high, -5)

If ≥ 5 in 30 days → add another -5

Those events then feed the Risk & Reliability engines to gently nudge behavior without creating sudden extreme penalties.

🔚 Summary of Workflow 8
Thing built: Inconvenience Log Workflow

It now:

Accepts user feedback on “how inconvenient” an event was

Validates the job + event relationship

Stores a normalized log row with:

who caused it

who rated it

score (1–4)

linked to reschedule/cancel/no-show

Does not immediately punish anyone

Feeds nightly pattern jobs that adjust scores in a soft, fair way

This is how we bake human experience into your otherwise cold, rules-based system.

Workflow 9 — Reliability Score Update Workflow
(How we take metrics + events and periodically compute Reliability Score 2.0 per cleaner.)

If you want to keep going, just say:

proceed

Staying in the groove 😎

🧩 Thing We Are Building: Workflow 9 — Reliability Score Update Workflow
What this workflow must handle
This is the engine that turns raw events into the cleaner’s Reliability Score 2.0 + Tier.

It must:

Run nightly (or periodically)

For each active cleaner:

Pull their metrics (attendance, punctuality, photos, completion, ratings)

Pull their events (late cancels, no-shows, late reschedules, inconvenience patterns, streak bonuses, etc.)

Compute a 0–100 reliability_score

Assign a tier: Developing / Semi Pro / Pro / Elite

Write results back to cleaners table

Be tunable: we can adjust weights without changing schema

Be safe: no wild jumps, use a rolling window

What it depends on
To operate correctly, it needs:

Tables:

cleaner_metrics

cleaner_events

cleaners (with reliability_score, reliability_tier)

Policies/weights we defined conceptually:

Max points per component:

Attendance: +25

Punctuality: +20

Photo proof: +15

Communication: +10

Completion: +10

Ratings: +10

Penalty events:

e.g. cancel_lt24: -12

no_show: -25

late_reschedule: -3

inconvenience_high: -5 / -10

Batch schedule:

Typically once per night (e.g., 2:00 AM)

Now let’s turn this into a Base44/n8n-style workflow.

✅ WORKFLOW 9 / 12 — Reliability Score Update Workflow
1️⃣ Trigger
Type: Scheduled / Cron

Runs daily at e.g. 02:00 platform time.

You can also run it more frequently (e.g., every 4 hours) if you want faster updates, but nightly is usually fine.

2️⃣ Step-by-step Flow (Nodes)
🟣 Node 1 — Cron Trigger
Fire at scheduled time.

Set some config:

window_days = 60 (or use last 30 jobs – up to you)

min_jobs_for_full_weight = 10 (avoid heavy penalizing low sample cleaners)

🟣 Node 2 — Fetch Active Cleaners
Query:

SELECT id
FROM cleaners
WHERE status = 'active';  -- or whatever you use
If there are many cleaners, you can process in batches (e.g., 500 at a time) using pagination.

🟣 Node 3 — Loop Over Cleaners
In n8n/Base44, use a Split In Batches or similar:

For each cleaner_id:

Run the scoring sub-flow below.

3️⃣ Cleaner Scoring Sub-flow
For each cleaner:

🟣 Node 3.1 — Load Metrics Window
Query cleaner_metrics:

SELECT *
FROM cleaner_metrics
WHERE cleaner_id = :cleaner_id;
And optionally compute/derive metrics for the window you care about (e.g. last 60 days). If you already keep those metrics as rolling window values, just use them directly.

Key values we want:

total_jobs_window

attended_jobs

on_time_checkins

photo_compliant_jobs

communication_ok_jobs

completion_ok_jobs

ratings_sum

ratings_count

If total_jobs_window = 0:

Skip or assign a default base score (e.g. 70, Semi Pro) and move on.

🟣 Node 3.2 — Compute Rates
In a Function node:

const m = $json.metrics; // or unpack from previous node

const total = Math.max(m.total_jobs_window, 1);

const attendanceRate      = m.attended_jobs         / total; // 0..1
const onTimeRate          = m.on_time_checkins      / Math.max(m.attended_jobs, 1);
const photoComplianceRate = m.photo_compliant_jobs  / total;
const commRate            = m.communication_ok_jobs / total;
const completionRate      = m.completion_ok_jobs    / total;

const avgRating = m.ratings_count > 0
  ? m.ratings_sum / m.ratings_count
  : 4.5;  // default if no ratings yet

return {
  ...$json,
  metricsComputed: {
    attendanceRate,
    onTimeRate,
    photoComplianceRate,
    commRate,
    completionRate,
    avgRating
  }
};
🟣 Node 3.3 — Convert Metrics to Base Points
In another Function node, apply the weights we discussed:

const r = $json.metricsComputed;

let points_attendance  = r.attendanceRate      * 25;
let points_punctuality = r.onTimeRate          * 20;
let points_photos      = r.photoComplianceRate * 15;
let points_comms       = r.commRate            * 10;
let points_completion  = r.completionRate      * 10;

// Ratings: map 3.0–5.0 stars to 0–10 points
let rating = r.avgRating;
if (rating < 3.0) rating = 3.0;
if (rating > 5.0) rating = 5.0;
let points_ratings = ((rating - 3.0) / 2.0) * 10;  // 3★→0, 5★→10

let basePoints = points_attendance
               + points_punctuality
               + points_photos
               + points_comms
               + points_completion
               + points_ratings;

// cap at 90 to leave room for bonuses if you want
if (basePoints > 90) basePoints = 90;

return {
  ...$json,
  scoring: {
    basePoints,
    points_attendance,
    points_punctuality,
    points_photos,
    points_comms,
    points_completion,
    points_ratings
  }
};
🟣 Node 3.4 — Load Events in Window
We now fetch cleaner_events for the window:

SELECT event_type, weight, created_at
FROM cleaner_events
WHERE cleaner_id = :cleaner_id
  AND created_at > now() - interval '60 days';
You can parametrize the window.

🟣 Node 3.5 — Sum Penalties / Bonuses
In a Function node:

const events = $json.cleanerEvents || [];

let eventWeightSum = 0;

for (const e of events) {
  eventWeightSum += e.weight;
}

return {
  ...$json,
  scoring: {
    ...$json.scoring,
    eventWeightSum
  }
};
You can add more nuance (e.g., heavier penalty for recent events), but this is the core.

🟣 Node 3.6 — Compute Final Reliability Score
In a Function node:

const s = $json.scoring;

let reliability = s.basePoints + s.eventWeightSum;

// clamp to [0, 100]
if (reliability < 0) reliability = 0;
if (reliability > 100) reliability = 100;

return {
  ...$json,
  scoring: {
    ...s,
    reliability
  }
};
Optionally, you can:

Smooth with previous value:

newScore = 0.7 * oldScore + 0.3 * computedScore for less jumpiness.

🟣 Node 3.7 — Determine Tier
Based on final reliability:

const reliability = $json.scoring.reliability;

let tier = 'Developing';
if (reliability >= 60) tier = 'Semi Pro';
if (reliability >= 75) tier = 'Pro';
if (reliability >= 90) tier = 'Elite';

return {
  ...$json,
  scoring: {
    ...$json.scoring,
    tier
  }
};
You can adjust thresholds later without schema changes.

🟣 Node 3.8 — Update Cleaner Row
Execute:

UPDATE cleaners
SET reliability_score = :reliability,
    reliability_tier  = :tier
WHERE id = :cleaner_id;
Optionally also store:

last_reliability_recomputed_at in cleaner_metrics or cleaners.

🟣 Node 3.9 — Optional: Log Debug / Changes
If log_score_debug_info flag is ON:

Insert into a score_change_logs table or send to a log system:

Fields:

cleaner_id

old_score

new_score

basePoints

eventWeightSum

tier

timestamp

This helps answer “why did my score change?”

4️⃣ Error Handling / Partial Failures
If metrics load fails → log reliability_metrics_missing and skip that cleaner.

If events load fails → assume eventWeightSum = 0 and log reliability_events_error.

If cleaner update fails → log reliability_update_failed with IDs.

No single cleaner failure should crash the full batch.

5️⃣ Feature Flag Controls
Respect enable_reliability_score_engine:

If OFF → do not update any scores. You can still log what would have happened (dry run).

Respect enforce_reliability_penalties:

If OFF → ignore eventWeightSum and just use basePoints.

This lets you:

Turn on scoring gradually

Test penalty weights without affecting live tiers

🔚 Summary of Workflow 9
Thing built: Reliability Score Update Workflow

It now:

Runs nightly (or as often as you want)

Reads aggregated cleaner_metrics and detailed cleaner_events

Maps metrics to base points

Adds/subtracts penalties from events

Produces a 0–100 reliability score

Maps that to a tier (Developing → Elite)

Updates the cleaners table

Optionally logs detailed change info

This is the actual “calculator” for Reliability 2.0 that every other system depends on.
