Workflow 10 — Client Risk Score Update Workflow
(Nightly job that turns client_risk_events into a consolidated risk score + risk band.)

If you want to continue, just say:

“Proceed with Workflow 10.”


proceed

Got it, staying in our structure 👌

🧩 Thing We Are Building: Workflow 10 — Client Risk Score Update Workflow
What this workflow must handle
This is the Client Risk Engine — the counterpart to Reliability.

It must:

Run nightly (or periodically)

For each active client:

Read their client_risk_events over a recent window (e.g. last 14–30 days)

Sum up the weights (late cancels, late reschedules, no-shows, inconvenience patterns, etc.)

Apply optional decay for older events

Compute a 0–100 risk_score

Assign a risk_band (normal → mild → elevated → high → critical)

Write results to client_risk_scores

Be tunable via event weights without changing schema

Be safe: no insane jumps, just logical accumulation

What it depends on
It relies on:

Tables:

client_risk_events

client_risk_scores

clients

Event types already being logged by other workflows:

late_reschedule_lt24

late_reschedule_pattern

cancel_24_48

cancel_lt24

no_show

inconvenience_pattern

A chosen time window:

We’ve talked about ~14-day rolling window for triggers

Feature flags:

enable_risk_score_engine

enforce_client_risk_restrictions (uses the result later)

Now let’s turn that into a concrete Base44/n8n-type batch workflow.

✅ WORKFLOW 10 / 12 — Client Risk Score Update Workflow
1️⃣ Trigger
Type: Scheduled / Cron

Runs daily at e.g. 03:00 platform time.

You can adjust frequency (nightly is good enough).

2️⃣ High-Level Flow
Cron fires

Fetch all active clients

For each client:

Load recent client_risk_events

Compute weighted risk score in a window

Clamp to 0–100

Derive risk_band from thresholds

Update client_risk_scores

3️⃣ Node-by-node
🟣 Node 1 — Cron Trigger
Configure:

schedule = daily at 03:00

window_days = 30 (or 14 – we’ll assume 30 for scoring, 14 for some pattern triggers)

If enable_risk_score_engine is OFF:

Exit early (no-op, or run in dry-run mode if you want logs only).

🟣 Node 2 — Fetch Active Clients
Query:

SELECT id
FROM clients
WHERE status = 'active';  -- or however you define active
Use batching for large volumes.

🟣 Node 3 — Loop Over Clients
Use a batch/split node to process each client_id individually.

4️⃣ Client Sub-flow (Per Client)
🟣 Node 3.1 — Load Risk Events in Window
For each client_id:

SELECT event_type, weight, created_at
FROM client_risk_events
WHERE client_id = :client_id
  AND created_at > now() - interval '30 days'
ORDER BY created_at ASC;
We get an array of events with weights.

🟣 Node 3.2 — Handle “No Events” Case
In a Function node:

const events = $json.clientRiskEvents || [];

if (events.length === 0) {
  return {
    ...$json,
    riskCalc: {
      rawScore: 0,
      finalScore: 0,
      riskBand: 'normal'
    }
  };
}
If no events:

risk_score = 0

band = normal

We’ll still update client_risk_scores so it’s consistent.

🟣 Node 3.3 — Compute Raw Risk Score (With Optional Decay)
We want recency to matter more but keep it simple.

Example approach:

Events from last 14 days → full weight

Events from 15–30 days → e.g. 50% weight

Function node:

const events = $json.clientRiskEvents;

const now = new Date();
let rawScore = 0;

for (const e of events) {
  const createdAt = new Date(e.created_at);
  const diffDays = (now - createdAt) / (1000 * 60 * 60 * 24);

  let multiplier = 1.0;
  if (diffDays > 14 && diffDays <= 30) {
    multiplier = 0.5; // older events have half effect
  }

  rawScore += e.weight * multiplier;
}

// prevent negative if you ever add negative events later
if (rawScore < 0) rawScore = 0;

return {
  ...$json,
  riskCalc: {
    rawScore
  }
};
🟣 Node 3.4 — Normalize / Clamp Final Score to 0–100
You can choose a simple mapping, e.g.:

finalScore = min(rawScore, 100)

Or, if you want:

finalScore = min(rawScore * scale_factor, 100) if rawScore tends to be small.

For now, keep it simple:

let rawScore = $json.riskCalc.rawScore;

// Optionally, apply some smoothing with previous score; we’ll handle that later.
if (rawScore > 100) rawScore = 100;

return {
  ...$json,
  riskCalc: {
    ...$json.riskCalc,
    finalScore: rawScore
  }
};
🟣 Node 3.5 — Determine Risk Band
Based on finalScore:

Example thresholds:

0–19 → normal

20–39 → mild

40–59 → elevated

60–79 → high

80–100 → critical

Function node:

const score = $json.riskCalc.finalScore;
let band = 'normal';

if (score >= 20) band = 'mild';
if (score >= 40) band = 'elevated';
if (score >= 60) band = 'high';
if (score >= 80) band = 'critical';

return {
  ...$json,
  riskCalc: {
    ...$json.riskCalc,
    riskBand: band
  }
};
You can tweak thresholds later if you see too many users in specific bands.

🟣 Node 3.6 — Optional Smoothing with Previous Score
To avoid big jumps, especially when events expire, we can blend with prior value.

First, load previous risk_score if exists:

SELECT risk_score
FROM client_risk_scores
WHERE client_id = :client_id;
Then in a function:

const current = $json.riskCalc.finalScore;
const prev = $json.prevRiskScore != null ? $json.prevRiskScore : current;

const alpha = 0.7; // weight for previous score
const smoothed = alpha * prev + (1 - alpha) * current;

return {
  ...$json,
  riskCalc: {
    ...$json.riskCalc,
    finalScore: smoothed
  }
};
Then recalc band based on smoothed if you want. Or you can base band on raw; your choice.

🟣 Node 3.7 — Upsert into client_risk_scores
SQL:

INSERT INTO client_risk_scores (client_id, risk_score, risk_band, last_recomputed_at)
VALUES (:client_id, :risk_score, :risk_band, now())
ON CONFLICT (client_id)
DO UPDATE SET
  risk_score = EXCLUDED.risk_score,
  risk_band = EXCLUDED.risk_band,
  last_recomputed_at = EXCLUDED.last_recomputed_at;
Where:

:risk_score = riskCalc.finalScore

:risk_band = riskCalc.riskBand

🟣 Node 3.8 — Optional: Log Band Changes
If you want to track transitions (for ops & support):

Load previous risk_band in Node 3.6

If old_band != new_band:

Insert into a small log table client_risk_band_changes or send to logs:

Fields:

client_id

old_band

new_band

timestamp

This is helpful when support wonders: “Why is this client suddenly high risk?”

5️⃣ Error Handling
If event query fails:

Log risk_events_load_failed with client_id

Optionally skip or treat as rawScore = 0

If upsert fails:

Log risk_score_update_failed with client_id / error

Do not crash the whole batch; move on to next client

No single client should break the global run.

6️⃣ Feature Flags
If enable_risk_score_engine is OFF:

Skip updating client_risk_scores, maybe log a “dry run” somewhere.

Downstream features (like matching & restrictions) will:

Read risk_band and apply behavior only when:

enforce_client_risk_restrictions is ON

enforce_prepayment_for_high_risk is ON

enable_risk_aware_matching is ON

So you can test this engine in isolation first.

🔚 Summary of Workflow 10
Thing built: Client Risk Score Update Workflow

It now:

Runs nightly

Reads each client’s client_risk_events for the last N days

Sums weighted events into a rawScore

Applies optional decay based on age of events

Clamps and smooths to a risk_score between 0 and 100

Maps that score into a risk_band (normal → critical)

Upserts the results into client_risk_scores

Optionally logs band changes for support/ops visibility

This is the engine that powers:

Risk-based restrictions

Prepayment requirements

Matching protection for cleaners

Internal trust & safety tooling

Next up in the workflow roadmap:

Workflow 11 — Matching / Search Workflow
(How we use reliability, risk, availability, and preferences to rank & filter cleaners for a job.)

If you want to continue, say:

“Proceed with Workflow 11.”


proceed

Perfect, we’re in the fun part now — who gets shown to who 🚦

🧩 Thing We Are Building: Workflow 11 — Matching / Search Workflow
What this workflow must handle
This is the brain that picks which cleaners a client sees and in what order.

It must:

Take a job (or search query) with:

location

time window

job type

client_id

Build a candidate pool of eligible cleaners

Filter by:

availability

distance

tier (if relevant)

status (active, verified, etc.)

Rank candidates using:

Reliability score + tier

Distance

Client-specific factors:

client risk band

cleaner flexibility badge

historical relationship (repeat client)

Respect feature flags:

enable_score_based_matching

enable_risk_aware_matching

enable_flexibility_aware_matching

Optionally:

Store match rows in match_recommendations

Trigger notifications to top cleaners (offers)

Support both:

“Search screen” (client browsing)

“Suggest cleaners for this job” (internal auto-match)

What it depends on
It uses:

Tables:

jobs

cleaners

cleaner_availability / cleaner_blackout_periods

client_risk_scores

cleaners.reliability_score + reliability_tier

badge_assignments or cleaners.flexibility_status

(optional) match_recommendations, job_history

Existing events:

job_ready_for_matching (from Workflow 1)

Feature flags:

enable_score_based_matching

enable_risk_aware_matching

enable_flexibility_aware_matching

Now let’s build it.

✅ WORKFLOW 11 / 12 — Matching / Search Workflow
We’ll support two entry modes:

Internal “match this job” (auto suggestions)

Client search (“show me cleaners for this time/place”)

Under the hood, the logic is mostly the same.

1️⃣ Trigger A — job_ready_for_matching (Internal Auto-Match)
Event payload example:

{
  "event": "job_ready_for_matching",
  "job_id": 999,
  "client_id": 123,
  "job_type": "deep_clean",
  "start_time": "2025-03-14T10:00:00Z",
  "duration_minutes": 180,
  "location": {
    "lat": 37.7749,
    "lng": -122.4194
  }
}
2️⃣ Trigger B — “Search Cleaners” (API-driven)
Your API might call the workflow internally with:

{
  "event": "search_cleaners",
  "client_id": 123,
  "job_type": "standard_clean",
  "desired_start_time": "2025-03-14T10:00:00Z",
  "duration_minutes": 180,
  "location": {
    "lat": 37.7749,
    "lng": -122.4194
  },
  "max_results": 20
}
We’ll treat both events the same after the first step.

3️⃣ Node-by-node Matching Flow
🟣 Node 1 — Trigger
If event == "job_ready_for_matching" → load job by job_id and extract:

client_id, start_time, duration, location, job_type

If event == "search_cleaners" → use payload directly.

Normalize into a single internal object:

{
  "client_id": 123,
  "job_type": "deep_clean",
  "start_time": "2025-03-14T10:00:00Z",
  "duration_minutes": 180,
  "lat": 37.7749,
  "lng": -122.4194,
  "max_results": 20,
  "job_id": 999  // null for generic search
}
🟣 Node 2 — Fetch Client Risk & Preferences
Query:

SELECT risk_score, risk_band
FROM client_risk_scores
WHERE client_id = :client_id;
If no row:

Default to risk_band = 'normal', risk_score = 0.

Optionally, also load:

client_flexibility_profile (if we later use it).

🟣 Node 3 — Build Base Cleaner Candidate Pool
Goal: get a rough set of cleaners near the location and active.

Query (simplified):

SELECT
  c.id AS cleaner_id,
  c.reliability_score,
  c.reliability_tier,
  c.home_lat,
  c.home_lng,
  c.flexibility_status,      -- e.g. 'normal' | 'low'
  c.status                   -- e.g. 'active'
FROM cleaners c
WHERE
  c.status = 'active'
  AND c.reliability_score IS NOT NULL
  -- optional: c.reliability_score >= some minimum
  -- optional: filter by job_type compatibility (e.g., deep clean, move-out)
  -- NOTE: distance filter will be approximate first, then refined
;
You can pre-limit by:

Geographic rough bounding box (e.g., within ~30 miles) based on lat/lng.

This gives you a list of candidate cleaners before detailed filters.

🟣 Node 4 — Filter by Availability & Conflicts
For each candidate cleaner (in a loop or batched):

Call availability engine or check directly:

-- pseudo:
is_available = availability_check(cleaner_id, start_time, end_time);
Filter out those not available.

After this step, you have:

[
  {
    "cleaner_id": 555,
    "reliability_score": 88,
    "reliability_tier": "Pro",
    "flexibility_status": "normal",
    "distance_miles": 5.2
    // ...
  },
  ...
]
(We’ll compute distance_miles in the next node.)

🟣 Node 5 — Compute Distance
In a JS Function node:

Use haversine or similar to compute distance between job lat/lng and cleaner home/base lat/lng (or typical service radius center).

Example pseudo:

function haversineMiles(lat1, lon1, lat2, lon2) {
  // classic formula; you can plug your actual code here
}

for each cleaner candidate:
  distance_miles = haversineMiles(job.lat, job.lng, cleaner.home_lat, cleaner.home_lng)
You can discard cleaners with:

distance_miles > cleaner.travel_radius_mi

Or some absolute max like 30 miles.

🟣 Node 6 — Fetch Cleaner Badges / Flags
Lookup:

SELECT badge_type, is_active
FROM badge_assignments
WHERE cleaner_id IN (...ids) AND is_active = true;
Map to each cleaner:

hasLowFlexBadge = true/false

Or use cleaners.flexibility_status if you stored it there instead.

🟣 Node 7 — Fetch Job History (Repeat Client Bonus)
Optional but powerful:

For each cleaner:

SELECT COUNT(*) AS past_jobs_count
FROM jobs
WHERE jobs.client_id = :client_id
  AND jobs.cleaner_id = :cleaner_id
  AND jobs.status = 'completed';
Use past_jobs_count to give a boost if they’ve worked together before.

🟣 Node 8 — Compute Match Score per Cleaner
Now the fun part: ranking formula.

We define components:

R = normalized reliability (0–1) from 0–100 score

D = distance contribution (closer = higher)

H = history bonus (repeat client)

F = flexibility compatibility (low-flex cleaner vs high-risk/chaotic client)

RiskFilter = apply penalties or exclusions if client is high risk

In a JS Function node, per cleaner:

const reliability = cleaner.reliability_score; // 0..100
const tier = cleaner.reliability_tier;
const distance = cleaner.distance_miles;
const hasLowFlex = cleaner.flexibility_status === 'low';
const pastJobs = cleaner.past_jobs_count || 0;
const clientRiskBand = job.client_risk_band; // normal..critical

// Normalize reliability
const R = reliability / 100;

// Distance: simple transform where closer is better; e.g., 0 at 30mi, 1 at 0mi
const maxDist = 30; // tune this
let D = 1 - Math.min(distance, maxDist) / maxDist;
if (D < 0) D = 0;

// History bonus
let H = 0;
if (pastJobs >= 3) H = 0.1;
else if (pastJobs >= 1) H = 0.05;

// Flexibility factor
let F = 0; // neutral

// If risk-aware & flexibility-aware matching enabled, adjust:
if (hasLowFlex && (clientRiskBand === 'elevated' || clientRiskBand === 'high' || clientRiskBand === 'critical')) {
  // low-flex cleaner + chaotic client = bad match
  F = -0.2;
}

// Additional risk-based adjustments:
let RiskPenalty = 0;
if (clientRiskBand === 'high' || clientRiskBand === 'critical') {
  // optionally penalize matching with top-tier cleaners to protect them
  if (tier === 'Elite') {
    RiskPenalty = -0.2;
  }
}

// Base match score weighted sum
let score = 0;
if ($env.enable_score_based_matching) {
  score =
    0.5 * R +   // reliability weight
    0.3 * D +   // distance weight
    0.1 * H +   // history weight
    0.1 * F;    // flexibility adjustment
} else {
  // fallback: distance-only
  score = D;
}

// Apply risk penalty if risk-aware matching ON
if ($env.enable_risk_aware_matching) {
  score += RiskPenalty;
}

// Clamp to [0,1]
if (score < 0) score = 0;
if (score > 1) score = 1;

cleaner.match_score = score;
You can implement $env.enable_* as feature flag lookups.

🟣 Node 9 — Filter / Exclude by Risk Rules (Optional)
If enforce_client_risk_restrictions is ON:

For clientRiskBand = 'critical':

Exclude cleaners with:

tier = 'Elite'

OR extremely high reliability (protect your best supply)

For high:

Maybe only soften scores, not exclude.

In code:

if ($env.enforce_client_risk_restrictions) {
  if (clientRiskBand === 'critical' && tier === 'Elite') {
    // Remove from candidate list
    cleaner.excluded_due_to_risk = true;
  }
}
Then filter out excluded_due_to_risk cleaners.

🟣 Node 10 — Sort & Limit Results
Sort candidates descending by match_score.

Keep up to max_results (default 20 or so).

Now you have the final ranked list.

🟣 Node 11 — Store in match_recommendations (Optional but Recommended)
If this event is for a specific job (not a generic search):

INSERT INTO match_recommendations (
  job_id,
  client_id,
  cleaner_id,
  match_score,
  rank,
  created_at
)
VALUES
  -- one row per cleaner in sorted order
This is super helpful for:

Debugging matching decisions

Auditing “why did we pick this cleaner?”

Running experiments later

For client search without a job_id, you can skip this or use a temporary search_id.

🟣 Node 12 — Notify Top Cleaners (Auto-Match Flow)
For internal matching (job_ready_for_matching):

Take top N (e.g., 3–5) cleaners.

Fire notifications:

“New job available: [Job Type], [Location], [Time].”

If you have an offer/claim system:

Attach job details (id, pay in credits) so they can accept (which triggers Workflow 2: Job Acceptance).

🟣 Node 13 — Return Results (Search API Flow)
For search:

The API returns to client:

{
  "cleaners": [
    {
      "id": 555,
      "name": "Alex",
      "tier": "Elite",
      "reliability_score": 93,
      "distance_miles": 3.2,
      "match_score": 0.91,
      "flexibility_status": "normal",
      "badges": ["Elite", "Top Rated"],
      "rate_range": [600, 850]
    },
    ...
  ]
}
UI doesn’t need to know about risk bands or penalties — just gets a sorted list, plus display info.

🟣 Node 14 — Error Handling
If:

Candidate query fails → log matching_candidates_failed, return empty list + fail gracefully.

Availability check fails → handle with fallback:

Treat as not available, or

Retry a few times.

If the entire flow fails for a job:

Log matching_failed, include job_id and client_id.

Optionally notify support or fall back to simple distance-based matching.

🔚 Summary of Workflow 11
Thing built: Matching / Search Workflow

It now:

Listens to:

job_ready_for_matching (auto-match)

search_cleaners (client browse)

Builds a candidate pool of active, available cleaners near the client

Pulls:

reliability score + tier

distance

low-flex badge / flexibility status

client’s risk band

job history with the client

Computes a match_score per cleaner (0–1) using weighted components

Optionally:

Applies risk-based exclusions or penalties

Avoids pairing high-risk clients with your top, least-flexible cleaners

Sorts and returns the best matches

Optionally logs into match_recommendations and notifies top cleaners

This is the heart of how PureTask will feel smart, fair, and protective for both sides.

We now have 11 of the 12 workflows mapped.

(How support can view, override, and correct scores, events, and edge cases.)

Inconvenience logs

A penalty was unfair

Add/remove client_risk_events

Force re-run of risk or reliability calculation for a specific user

What it depends on
It uses:

Tables:

jobs

reschedule_events

cancellation_events

client_risk_events

client_risk_scores

cleaner_events

cleaner_metrics

cleaners (score + tier)

Reliability Score Update (Workflow 9)

✅ WORKFLOW 12 / 12 — Admin / Support Tooling Workflow
We’ll define a set of admin endpoints + back-office flows, each implemented via Base44/n8n or your backend + SQL, but conceptually they’re workflows too.

1️⃣ Admin View — Cleaner Reliability Profile
Admin endpoint (read):
GET /admin/cleaners/:cleanerId/reliability

What it should show (pulled via workflow):

From cleaners:

reliability_score

reliability_tier

From cleaner_metrics:

total_jobs_window

attended_jobs

on_time_checkins

photo_compliant_jobs

communication_ok_jobs

completion_ok_jobs

ratings_sum, ratings_count

From cleaner_events:

List of events in last 60–90 days:

event_type, weight, created_at, job_id, metadata

From badge_assignments:

Active badges: low_flexibility, etc.

Workflow steps (read-only):

Trigger: admin UI calls endpoint

Query multiple tables

Aggregate into a JSON payload

No writes, no side effects

This is just data aggregation for support dashboards.

2️⃣ Admin View — Client Risk Profile
Admin endpoint (read):
GET /admin/clients/:clientId/risk

What it should show:

From client_risk_scores:

risk_score, risk_band, last_recomputed_at

From client_risk_events (last 60–90 days):

event_type, weight, created_at, job_id

From cancellation_events and reschedule_events:

Summary:

late cancels

late reschedules

no-shows

From inconvenience_logs where caused_by = 'client':

Score distribution, count, recent comments

Again, read-only aggregation.

3️⃣ Admin Action — Adjust Cleaner Reliability (Events & Overrides)
Admin endpoint (write):
POST /admin/cleaners/:cleanerId/adjust-reliability

What it should support:

Option A: Add or modify an event (preferred)

e.g., support decides that a late cancel was actually client’s fault, not cleaner’s → add a positive or remove a negative event

Option B: Direct score override (temporary)

e.g., “set this cleaner to 80 for now” (less ideal, but sometimes needed)

Workflow for Option A (best practice):

Request example:

{
  "action": "add_event",                   // or 'remove_event'
  "job_id": 999,
  "event_type": "manual_adjustment",
  "weight": 5,
  "reason": "Penalty was incorrectly applied; support corrected it."
}
Steps:

Validate admin permissions.

Insert into cleaner_events:

INSERT INTO cleaner_events (
  cleaner_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata, created_at
) VALUES (
  :cleaner_id,
  :job_id,
  'manual_adjustment',
  :weight,
  jsonb_build_object('reason', :reason),
  now()
);
Optionally trigger a single-cleaner recompute:

emit event recompute_reliability_for_cleaner with cleaner_id

a smaller version of Workflow 9 runs just for them.

Workflow for Option B (direct override, discouraged but possible):

Request example:

{
  "action": "override_score",
  "new_score": 82,
  "reason": "Manual override due to special case."
}
Steps:

Validate admin.

Update cleaners.reliability_score = new_score.

Insert a cleaner_events record with event_type = 'manual_override' for audit.

Record in a separate score_overrides table:

INSERT INTO score_overrides (
  subject_type,
  subject_id,
  old_score,
  new_score,
  reason,
  created_by,
  created_at
)
VALUES ('cleaner', :cleaner_id, :old_score, :new_score, :reason, :admin_id, now());
4️⃣ Admin Action — Adjust Client Risk
Admin endpoint (write):
POST /admin/clients/:clientId/adjust-risk

Supports actions:

Add/remove client risk events

Temporary score override

Option A: add/remove event (preferred)

Request example:

{
  "action": "add_event",
  "job_id": 999,
  "event_type": "manual_adjustment",
  "weight": -5,
  "reason": "We determined client was not at fault."
}
Steps:

Insert into client_risk_events:

INSERT INTO client_risk_events (
  client_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata, created_at
) VALUES (
  :client_id,
  :job_id,
  'manual_adjustment',
  :weight,
  jsonb_build_object('reason', :reason),
  now()
);
Emit recompute_risk_for_client event → mini version of Workflow 10 for this client.

Option B: direct override

Similar pattern as with cleaners:

Update client_risk_scores.risk_score and risk_band

Log in score_overrides with subject_type = 'client'.

5️⃣ Admin Action — Fix No-Show / Cancellation Errors
Sometimes no-show or cancellation is logged incorrectly. We need a clean workflow to fix it.

Admin endpoint:
POST /admin/jobs/:jobId/fix-cancellation

Request example:

{
  "action": "reclassify",
  "new_status": "cancelled",          // or 'no_show_client', 'no_show_cleaner'
  "correct_cancelled_by": "client",   // or 'cleaner'
  "reason": "Cleaner actually arrived; client never opened door, but system mis-logged."
}
Workflow:

Load jobs, cancellation_events, client_risk_events, cleaner_events.

Reverse old cancellation impacts:

If previously marked no_show_cleaner incorrectly:

Delete or insert balancing cleaner_events (e.g. manual_adjustment +25)

Adjust credits if necessary (only via carefully designed admin tooling!)

Insert a new cancellation_events record with corrected data (or update existing one if safe).

Update job status to the correct final value.

Log an admin audit record for this change.

This is advanced and sensitive, so:

All money moves should be tracked

You may limit this to a senior admin role

6️⃣ Admin Action — Grace Cancellations Adjust
Admin endpoint:
POST /admin/clients/:clientId/grace-cancellations

Request example:

{
  "action": "grant_extra",
  "extra_grace": 1,
  "reason": "Longtime good client, one-time exception."
}
Workflow:

Update clients.grace_cancellations_total += extra_grace.

Insert audit log row: grace_adjustments table.

Or:

{
  "action": "reset_used",
  "reason": "System bug miscounted grace cancels."
}
→ Set clients.grace_cancellations_used = 0 and log it.

7️⃣ Admin Action — Badge Management (Low Flexibility)
Admin endpoint:
POST /admin/cleaners/:cleanerId/badges

Request example:

{
  "badge_type": "low_flexibility",
  "action": "force_add",    // or 'force_remove'
  "reason": "Pattern confirms low-flex behavior." 
}
Workflow:

If force_add:

Upsert into badge_assignments with is_active = true

Set cleaners.flexibility_status = 'low'

If force_remove:

Set badge_assignments.is_active = false and removed_at = now()

Set cleaners.flexibility_status = 'normal'

Always log in a badge_override_logs table for audit.

8️⃣ Admin Action — Trigger Recompute Manually
Admin endpoint:
POST /admin/cleaners/:id/recompute-reliability
POST /admin/clients/:id/recompute-risk

Workflow:

Emit events:

recompute_reliability_for_cleaner

recompute_risk_for_client

And then have smaller versions of Workflow 9 and 10 that only process that single user, triggered immediately rather than waiting for the nightly batch.

This is great after manual adjustments so scores refresh instantly.

9️⃣ Admin Dashboard — One-Page “Case View”
Support will love a one-page view per job that aggregates:

Job core info (time, type, status, credits)

Cleaner:

reliability score & tier

recent reliability events associated with that job

Client:

risk band & risk score

risk events associated with that job

Reschedule history:

All reschedule_events for that job

Cancellation / no-show details:

cancellation_events row

Inconvenience logs:

What cleaner/client reported about this job

This “case view” doesn’t need its own workflow; it’s just multiple queries aggregated behind something like:

GET /admin/jobs/:jobId/full-case

But it uses all the pieces we just defined.

can u explain our new rescheduling system 

Our new rescheduling system is basically:
“Everybody can adjust when life happens, but last-minute changes have a cost and we track patterns on BOTH sides.”

I’ll break it down in plain language.

1. Who can reschedule?
Client can request a new time

Cleaner can request a new time

The other party must Accept or Decline

If both agree, it’s a reschedule (not a cancel).

If they don’t agree, the job stays at the original time – and if the requester can’t make it, they have to cancel (and possibly pay fees).

2. Time windows (the core buckets)
Everything is based on how long before the original start time the reschedule happens:

More than 48 hours before → >48h

24–48 hours before → 24_48

Less than 24 hours before → <24h (this is “late change” territory)

These buckets affect how we treat the request and what gets logged.

3. “Reasonable” vs “Unreasonable” reschedules
When someone clicks Reschedule, the system checks if the new time is reasonable.

A reschedule is considered reasonable if:

The cleaner is available at the new time (within their set availability & radius)

The new time is not crazy far out (e.g., within about a week from the original)

This isn’t the 3rd+ reschedule for the same job

The request is made before the original start time (not after it already started)

If those conditions fail → the request is marked unreasonable.

Why this matters:

Reasonable request + cleaner declines → counts toward “Low Flexibility” patterns if this happens often.

Unreasonable request + cleaner declines → no penalty; they’re protected.

4. What happens when the client requests a reschedule?
4.1 Flow
Client chooses new time + reason

System:

Checks cleaner availability

Calculates bucket (>48h, 24_48, <24h)

Tags is_reasonable true/false

Cleaner gets a pending request:

Can Accept or Decline

4.2 If the cleaner ACCEPTS
Job moves to the new time.

If it was:

➜ More than 48 hours (>48h)
No one gets penalized.

It’s just a normal schedule change.

➜ 24–48 hours (24_48)
Still generally treated as okay, but:

We log that the client moved the job relatively close to the time.

These events can contribute to patterns over time.

➜ Less than 24 hours (<24h) – “late reschedule”
Cleaner is not punished for being flexible.

We log a client risk event like “late_reschedule_lt24”

If the client does this repeatedly (e.g., 3+ in ~14 days), their risk score rises and they get treated as more chaotic:

May face stricter rules (forced prepay, less leniency, etc. later)

Cleaner can also rate Inconvenience (1–4). High scores feed patterns.

4.3 If the cleaner DECLINES
The job stays at the original time.

Two key consequences:

Client must either:

Keep the original time

Or cancel, and if it’s inside 24h/48h, pay the normal cancellation fee

Cleaner side:

If the request was unreasonable → no issue.

If the request was reasonable and this cleaner often declines reasonable reschedules:

They can eventually get a “Low Flexibility” flag/badge from pattern detection.

So:

Cleaner isn’t punished for saying “No, that time doesn’t work”,
but if they always say no to fair requests, the system eventually marks them as low-flex.

5. What happens when the cleaner requests a reschedule?
Same mechanics, flipped roles:

Cleaner proposes new time + reason

System checks: availability, bucket, reasonable/unreasonable

Client can Accept or Decline

5.1 If the client ACCEPTS
Job moves to new time.

Effects:

➜ If it’s >48h
No penalty, just a normal adjustment.

➜ If it’s 24–48h
Logged, may be used in patterns but usually low impact.

➜ If it’s <24h (late change from cleaner)
We log a cleaner reliability event like late_reschedule with a small negative weight (e.g. −3).

This gently pulls down their Reliability over time if they do it often.

The client can also rate inconvenience.

This reflects:

If the cleaner is moving things last-minute, they should absorb a bit of the reliability cost.

5.2 If the client DECLINES
Job stays at original time.

Cleaner is still expected to show up at the original time.

If the cleaner later cancels or no-shows → normal late cancel/no-show penalties apply.

6. What about last-minute reschedules inside 24h?
This is the most important edge case you care about.

🔹 If client asks to reschedule inside 24h
Cleaner can:

Accept → get the job at new time, no hit to their score.

Decline → keep the original time.

Client:

If they still can’t do the original time and cancel:

They pay the late cancellation fee (e.g. 100% inside <24h).

They may get a risk event (“late_cancel_lt24”).

If this happens repeatedly → risk band goes up.

This protects the cleaner from being pushed around just because the client wants to move things last minute.

🔹 If cleaner asks to reschedule inside 24h
Client can:

Accept → job moves, small reliability penalty to cleaner (late_reschedule −3).

Decline → job stays, cleaner must still show up.

If cleaner later cancels inside 24h:

It becomes a late cancellation with a much bigger penalty (e.g. cancel_lt24 −12, plus possible tier impact).

So the system:

Encourages cleaners to plan ahead

Lets them ask for a reschedule when absolutely needed

But doesn’t let them spam late moves without reliability consequences

7. Inconvenience Score: the “emotional thermometer”
After certain reschedule/cancel events (especially late ones), the non-requesting party may see:

“How inconvenient was this?”
1 = Not really
2 = A little
3 = Quite inconvenient
4 = Very disruptive

We log:

Who rated (client or cleaner)

Who caused the inconvenience (client or cleaner)

The score (1–4)

Whether it was connected to reschedule, cancel, or no-show

We don’t immediately punish anyone for a single 3 or 4.
Instead we use patterns:

If a client keeps generating score 3–4 inconvenience for multiple cleaners in 14 days:

We add extra risk events → their Client Risk Score goes up.

If a cleaner keeps generating 3–4 inconvenience scores:

We add extra reliability penalties → their Reliability Score drips down gently.

This captures real human pain without letting a single bad interaction ruin someone.

8. How all this ties into Scores & Matching
For Cleaners (Reliability 2.0)
Rescheduling impacts them via:

Late reschedules THEY initiate (<24h) → small negative event

Late cancels / no-shows → big negative events

Repeated declines of reasonable reschedules → Low Flexibility badge through patterns, not instant punishment

Inconvenience patterns → small negative nudges over time

For Clients (Risk Score)
Rescheduling impacts them via:

Late reschedules THEY initiate (<24h) → risk events

Late cancels / no-shows → bigger risk events

Inconvenience patterns (3–4 ratings from cleaners) → risk increases

Over time:

High-risk clients might face:

Less lenient rules

Forced prepay

Less access to top-tier, low-flex cleaners

High-reliability cleaners:

Get better positioning, better hourly ranges, more repeat clients

9. Simple mental model (how to explain to cleaners & clients)
You can explain the system like this in your app copy:

You can always ask to reschedule.
If both sides agree, it’s fine.

The earlier you reschedule, the easier it is for everyone.
Last-minute changes may affect your reliability (for cleaners) or your risk profile (for clients), especially if it happens often.

If you often reschedule or cancel last minute, the system will protect the other party and prioritize more reliable behavior.

If you want, next step I can do one of these:

Write a clean, client-facing explanation of rescheduling for your website / app.

Write a cleaner-facing guide: “How reschedules affect your Reliability Score.”

Or make a policy-style document: “PureTask Rescheduling Policy (Official)” that we can later tweak with a lawyer.

1️⃣ Database Schema (Postgres)
File: schema_core.sql

-- ===========================
-- CORE ENTITIES
-- ===========================

CREATE TABLE clients (
  id              UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  email           TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL,
  created_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE TABLE cleaners (
  id                 UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  email              TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL,
  reliability_score  INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 75,
  reliability_tier   TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'SemiPro', -- Developing | SemiPro | Pro | Elite
  flexibility_status TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'normal',   -- normal | low
  home_lat           DOUBLE PRECISION,
  home_lng           DOUBLE PRECISION,
  travel_radius_mi   DOUBLE PRECISION DEFAULT 25,
  created_at         TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE TABLE jobs (
  id              UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  client_id       UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  cleaner_id      UUID REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  job_type        TEXT NOT NULL,                     -- e.g. standard_clean, deep_clean
  start_time      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
  end_time        TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
  status          TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'scheduled', -- scheduled | accepted | in_progress | completed | cancelled | no_show_client | no_show_cleaner
  held_credits    INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  checkin_time    TIMESTAMPTZ,
  checkout_time   TIMESTAMPTZ,
  created_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_jobs_client_id ON jobs(client_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_jobs_cleaner_id ON jobs(cleaner_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_jobs_start_time ON jobs(start_time);


-- ===========================
-- CLIENT RISK SYSTEM
-- ===========================

CREATE TABLE client_risk_scores (
  client_id          UUID PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES clients(id),
  risk_score         INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,    -- 0-100
  risk_band          TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'normal', -- normal | mild | elevated | high | critical
  last_recomputed_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE TABLE client_risk_events (
  id          BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  client_id   UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  job_id      UUID REFERENCES jobs(id),
  event_type  TEXT NOT NULL,         -- cancel_lt24, cancel_24_48, no_show, late_reschedule_lt24, inconvenience_pattern, manual_adjustment, ...
  weight      INTEGER NOT NULL,      -- positive increases risk
  metadata    JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,
  created_at  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_client_risk_events_client_id ON client_risk_events(client_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_client_risk_events_created_at ON client_risk_events(created_at);


-- ===========================
-- CLEANER RELIABILITY SYSTEM
-- ===========================

CREATE TABLE cleaner_metrics (
  cleaner_id           UUID PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  total_jobs_window    INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  attended_jobs        INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  on_time_checkins     INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  photo_compliant_jobs INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  communication_ok_jobs INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  completion_ok_jobs   INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  ratings_sum          INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  ratings_count        INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  last_recomputed_at   TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE TABLE cleaner_events (
  id          BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id  UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  job_id      UUID REFERENCES jobs(id),
  event_type  TEXT NOT NULL,        -- cancel_lt24, no_show, late_reschedule, missing_photos, inconvenience_high, manual_adjustment, ...
  weight      INTEGER NOT NULL,     -- negative hurts reliability, positive boosts
  metadata    JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,
  created_at  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_cleaner_events_cleaner_id ON cleaner_events(cleaner_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_cleaner_events_created_at ON cleaner_events(created_at);


-- ===========================
-- RESCHEDULING SYSTEM
-- ===========================

CREATE TABLE reschedule_events (
  id                    BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id                UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id),
  client_id             UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  cleaner_id            UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  requested_by          TEXT NOT NULL, -- client | cleaner
  requested_to          TEXT NOT NULL, -- client | cleaner
  t_request             TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
  t_start_original      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
  t_start_new           TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
  hours_before_original NUMERIC NOT NULL,
  bucket                TEXT NOT NULL, -- gt48 | 24_48 | lt24
  reason_code           TEXT NOT NULL, -- schedule_conflict, emergency, etc.
  status                TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending', -- pending | accepted | declined
  is_reasonable         BOOLEAN NOT NULL,
  declined_by           TEXT,          -- client | cleaner
  decline_reason_code   TEXT,
  metadata              JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,
  created_at            TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at            TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_reschedule_events_job_id ON reschedule_events(job_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_reschedule_events_client_id ON reschedule_events(client_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_reschedule_events_cleaner_id ON reschedule_events(cleaner_id);


-- ===========================
-- CANCELLATION SYSTEM
-- ===========================

CREATE TABLE cancellation_events (
  id                     BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id                 UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id),
  cancelled_by           TEXT NOT NULL, -- client | cleaner | system
  t_cancel               TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
  hours_before_start     NUMERIC NOT NULL,
  bucket                 TEXT NOT NULL, -- gt48 | 24_48 | lt24 | no_show
  reason_code            TEXT NOT NULL,
  after_reschedule_declined BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false,
  fee_pct                INTEGER NOT NULL,
  fee_credits            INTEGER NOT NULL,
  refund_credits         INTEGER NOT NULL,
  cleaner_comp_credits   INTEGER NOT NULL,
  platform_comp_credits  INTEGER NOT NULL,
  grace_used             BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false,
  metadata               JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,
  created_at             TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_cancellation_events_job_id ON cancellation_events(job_id);


-- ===========================
-- MATCHING SYSTEM
-- ===========================

CREATE TABLE match_recommendations (
  id          BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id      UUID REFERENCES jobs(id),
  client_id   UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES clients(id),
  cleaner_id  UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES cleaners(id),
  match_score NUMERIC NOT NULL,
  rank        INTEGER,
  created_at  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX idx_match_recs_job_id ON match_recommendations(job_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_match_recs_cleaner_id ON match_recommendations(cleaner_id);

// src/core/types.ts

export type TimeBucket = 'gt48' | '24_48' | 'lt24' | 'no_show';

export type RiskBand = 'normal' | 'mild' | 'elevated' | 'high' | 'critical';

export type ReliabilityTier = 'Developing' | 'SemiPro' | 'Pro' | 'Elite';

export type RescheduleStatus = 'pending' | 'accepted' | 'declined';

export type RescheduleActor = 'client' | 'cleaner';

export interface Location {
  lat: number;
  lng: number;
}

export interface Job {
  id: string;
  clientId: string;
  cleanerId: string | null;
  jobType: string;
  startTime: Date;
  endTime: Date;
  status: string;
  heldCredits: number;
  checkinTime?: Date | null;
  checkoutTime?: Date | null;
  location?: Location;
}

export interface Cleaner {
  id: string;
  reliabilityScore: number;
  reliabilityTier: ReliabilityTier;
  flexibilityStatus: 'normal' | 'low';
  homeLat: number | null;
  homeLng: number | null;
  travelRadiusMi: number;
}

export interface ClientRiskScore {
  clientId: string;
  riskScore: number;
  riskBand: RiskBand;
}

}

  punctualityMax: 20,
  photosMax: 15,
  communicationMax: 10,
  completionMax: 10,
  ratingsMax: 10,
};

export const RISK_BAND_THRESHOLDS = {
  mild: 20,
  elevated: 40,
  high: 60,
  critical: 80,
};

  distance: 0.3,
  history: 0.1,

3️⃣ Client Risk Score Service
File: src/core/ClientRiskService.ts

// src/core/ClientRiskService.ts

import { Pool } from 'pg';
import { RiskBand } from './types';
import { RISK_BAND_THRESHOLDS } from './config';

export class ClientRiskService {
  constructor(private db: Pool) {}

  async logEvent(params: {
    clientId: string;
    jobId?: string;
    eventType: string;
    weight: number;
    metadata?: any;
  }) {
    const { clientId, jobId, eventType, weight, metadata = {} } = params;

    await this.db.query(
      `
      INSERT INTO client_risk_events (client_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata)
      VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4, $5)
      `,
      [clientId, jobId ?? null, eventType, weight, metadata]
    );
  }

  private computeBand(score: number): RiskBand {
    const { mild, elevated, high, critical } = RISK_BAND_THRESHOLDS;
    if (score >= critical) return 'critical';
    if (score >= high) return 'high';
    if (score >= elevated) return 'elevated';
    if (score >= mild) return 'mild';
    return 'normal';
  }

  async recomputeForClient(clientId: string): Promise<void> {
    // load events from last 30 days with simple decay
    const { rows } = await this.db.query(
      `
      SELECT weight, created_at
      FROM client_risk_events
      WHERE client_id = $1
        AND created_at > now() - interval '30 days'
      ORDER BY created_at ASC
      `,
      [clientId]
    );

    if (rows.length === 0) {
      await this.db.query(
        `
        INSERT INTO client_risk_scores (client_id, risk_score, risk_band, last_recomputed_at)
        VALUES ($1, 0, 'normal', now())
        ON CONFLICT (client_id)
        DO UPDATE SET risk_score = EXCLUDED.risk_score,
                      risk_band = EXCLUDED.risk_band,
                      last_recomputed_at = EXCLUDED.last_recomputed_at
        `,
        [clientId]
      );
      return;
    }

    let rawScore = 0;
    const now = Date.now();

    for (const row of rows) {
      const weight: number = row.weight;
      const createdAt = new Date(row.created_at).getTime();
      const diffDays = (now - createdAt) / (1000 * 60 * 60 * 24);

      let multiplier = 1.0;
      if (diffDays > 14 && diffDays <= 30) multiplier = 0.5;

      rawScore += weight * multiplier;
    }

    if (rawScore < 0) rawScore = 0;
    if (rawScore > 100) rawScore = 100;

    const band = this.computeBand(rawScore);

    await this.db.query(
      `
      INSERT INTO client_risk_scores (client_id, risk_score, risk_band, last_recomputed_at)
      VALUES ($1, $2, $3, now())
      ON CONFLICT (client_id)
      DO UPDATE SET risk_score = EXCLUDED.risk_score,
                    risk_band = EXCLUDED.risk_band,
                    last_recomputed_at = EXCLUDED.last_recomputed_at
      `,
      [clientId, Math.round(rawScore), band]
    );
  }
}
4️⃣ Cleaner Reliability Score Service
File: src/core/ReliabilityService.ts

// src/core/ReliabilityService.ts

import { Pool } from 'pg';
import { ReliabilityTier } from './types';
import { RELIABILITY_WEIGHTS } from './config';

export class ReliabilityService {
  constructor(private db: Pool) {}

  async logEvent(params: {
    cleanerId: string;
    jobId?: string;
    eventType: string;
    weight: number;
    metadata?: any;
  }) {
    const { cleanerId, jobId, eventType, weight, metadata = {} } = params;

    await this.db.query(
      `
      INSERT INTO cleaner_events (cleaner_id, job_id, event_type, weight, metadata)
      VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4, $5)
      `,
      [cleanerId, jobId ?? null, eventType, weight, metadata]
    );
  }

  private computeTier(score: number): ReliabilityTier {
    if (score >= 90) return 'Elite';
    if (score >= 75) return 'Pro';
    if (score >= 60) return 'SemiPro';
    return 'Developing';
  }

  async recomputeForCleaner(cleanerId: string): Promise<void> {
    const metricsRes = await this.db.query(
      `
      SELECT *
      FROM cleaner_metrics
      WHERE cleaner_id = $1
      `,
      [cleanerId]
    );

    if (metricsRes.rows.length === 0) return;

    const m = metricsRes.rows[0];
    const total = Math.max(m.total_jobs_window, 1);

    const attendanceRate = m.attended_jobs / total;
    const onTimeRate = m.attended_jobs > 0 ? m.on_time_checkins / m.attended_jobs : 1;
    const photoRate = m.photo_compliant_jobs / total;
    const commRate = m.communication_ok_jobs / total;
    const completionRate = m.completion_ok_jobs / total;
    const avgRating =
      m.ratings_count > 0 ? m.ratings_sum / m.ratings_count : 4.5;

    const w = RELIABILITY_WEIGHTS;

    let pointsAttendance = attendanceRate * w.attendanceMax;
    let pointsPunctuality = onTimeRate * w.punctualityMax;
    let pointsPhotos = photoRate * w.photosMax;
    let pointsComms = commRate * w.communicationMax;
    let pointsCompletion = completionRate * w.completionMax;

    let rating = avgRating;
    if (rating < 3) rating = 3;
    if (rating > 5) rating = 5;
    let pointsRatings = ((rating - 3) / 2) * w.ratingsMax;

    let basePoints =
      pointsAttendance +
      pointsPunctuality +
      pointsPhotos +
      pointsComms +
      pointsCompletion +
      pointsRatings;

    if (basePoints > 90) basePoints = 90;

    // sum event weights in last 60 days
    const eventsRes = await this.db.query(
      `
      SELECT weight
      FROM cleaner_events
      WHERE cleaner_id = $1
        AND created_at > now() - interval '60 days'
      `,
      [cleanerId]
    );

    let eventWeightSum = 0;
    for (const row of eventsRes.rows) {
      eventWeightSum += row.weight;
    }

    let reliability = basePoints + eventWeightSum;
    if (reliability < 0) reliability = 0;
    if (reliability > 100) reliability = 100;

    const tier = this.computeTier(reliability);

    await this.db.query(
      `
      UPDATE cleaners
      SET reliability_score = $2,
          reliability_tier  = $3
      WHERE id = $1
      `,
      [cleanerId, Math.round(reliability), tier]
    );

    await this.db.query(
      `
      UPDATE cleaner_metrics
      SET last_recomputed_at = now()
      WHERE cleaner_id = $1
      `,
      [cleanerId]
    );
  }
}
5️⃣ Rescheduling Service
File: src/core/RescheduleService.ts

// src/core/RescheduleService.ts

import { Pool } from 'pg';
import {
  RescheduleRequestInput,
  RescheduleResponseInput,
  RescheduleActor,
  TimeBucket,
} from './types';
import { ReliabilityService } from './ReliabilityService';
import { ClientRiskService } from './ClientRiskService';

export class RescheduleService {
  constructor(
    private db: Pool,
    private reliability: ReliabilityService,
    private risk: ClientRiskService
  ) {}

  private computeBucket(tRequest: Date, tStartOriginal: Date): TimeBucket {
    const diffHours =
      (tStartOriginal.getTime() - tRequest.getTime()) / (1000 * 60 * 60);
    if (diffHours <= 0) return 'lt24';
    if (diffHours < 24) return 'lt24';
    if (diffHours <= 48) return '24_48';
    return 'gt48';
  }

  private async isReasonable(
    cleanerId: string,
    jobId: string,
    tStartOriginal: Date,
    tStartNew: Date
  ): Promise<boolean> {
    // simplistic: check that new time is within 7 days and cleaner has no conflict
    const diffDays =
      Math.abs(tStartNew.getTime() - tStartOriginal.getTime()) /
      (1000 * 60 * 60 * 24);
    if (diffDays > 7) return false;

    // Count previous reschedules for this job
    const { rows } = await this.db.query(
      `SELECT COUNT(*)::int AS cnt FROM reschedule_events WHERE job_id = $1`,
      [jobId]
    );
    const count = rows[0]?.cnt ?? 0;
    if (count >= 2) return false;

    // TODO: use availability blocks + existing jobs to validate.
    return true;
  }

  async requestReschedule(input: RescheduleRequestInput) {
    const { jobId, requestedBy, newStartTime, reasonCode } = input;

    const jobRes = await this.db.query(
      `SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = $1`,
      [jobId]
    );
    if (jobRes.rows.length === 0) {
      throw new Error('Job not found');
    }
    const job = jobRes.rows[0];

    if (!job.cleaner_id) {
      throw new Error('Job must have a cleaner assigned to reschedule');
    }

    const tRequest = new Date();
    const tStartOriginal = new Date(job.start_time);
    const bucket = this.computeBucket(tRequest, tStartOriginal);
    const isReasonable = await this.isReasonable(
      job.cleaner_id,
      jobId,
      tStartOriginal,
      newStartTime
    );

    const requestedTo: RescheduleActor =
      requestedBy === 'client' ? 'cleaner' : 'client';

    const insertRes = await this.db.query(
      `
      INSERT INTO reschedule_events (
        job_id, client_id, cleaner_id,
        requested_by, requested_to,
        t_request, t_start_original, t_start_new,
        hours_before_original, bucket, reason_code,
        status, is_reasonable
      )
      VALUES (
        $1, $2, $3,
        $4, $5,
        $6, $7, $8,
        EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM ($7 - $6))/3600,
        $9, $10,
        'pending', $11
      )
      RETURNING id
      `,
      [
        jobId,
        job.client_id,
        job.cleaner_id,
        requestedBy,
        requestedTo,
        tRequest,
        tStartOriginal,
        newStartTime,
        bucket,
        reasonCode,
        isReasonable,
      ]
    );

    const rescheduleEventId = insertRes.rows[0].id;
    return { rescheduleEventId, bucket, isReasonable };
  }

  async respondToReschedule(input: RescheduleResponseInput) {
    const { rescheduleEventId, jobId, action, actorType, declineReasonCode } =
      input;

    const resRes = await this.db.query(
      `SELECT * FROM reschedule_events WHERE id = $1`,
      [rescheduleEventId]
    );
    if (resRes.rows.length === 0) throw new Error('Reschedule event not found');
    const ev = resRes.rows[0];

    if (ev.job_id !== jobId) throw new Error('Job mismatch for reschedule');
    if (ev.status !== 'pending') throw new Error('Reschedule already resolved');
    if (ev.requested_to !== actorType) throw new Error('Unauthorized actor');

    const jobRes = await this.db.query(
      `SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = $1`,
      [jobId]
    );
    const job = jobRes.rows[0];

    if (action === 'accept') {
      // Update job time
      await this.db.query(
        `
        UPDATE jobs
        SET start_time = $2, updated_at = now()
        WHERE id = $1
        `,
        [jobId, ev.t_start_new]
      );

      await this.db.query(
        `
        UPDATE reschedule_events
        SET status = 'accepted', updated_at = now()
        WHERE id = $1
        `,
        [rescheduleEventId]
      );

      // Scoring side-effects for late reschedules
      if (ev.bucket === 'lt24') {
        if (ev.requested_by === 'client') {
          await this.risk.logEvent({
            clientId: job.client_id,
            jobId,
            eventType: 'late_reschedule_lt24',
            weight: 3,
            metadata: { source: 'reschedule_accept' },
          });
        } else if (ev.requested_by === 'cleaner') {
          await this.reliability.logEvent({
            cleanerId: job.cleaner_id,
            jobId,
            eventType: 'late_reschedule',
            weight: -3,
            metadata: { source: 'reschedule_accept' },
          });
        }
      }

      return { status: 'accepted' as const };
    }

    // DECLINE
    await this.db.query(
      `
      UPDATE reschedule_events
      SET status = 'declined',
          declined_by = $2,
          decline_reason_code = $3,
          updated_at = now()
      WHERE id = $1
      `,
      [rescheduleEventId, actorType, declineReasonCode ?? null]
    );

    // Low Flexibility signal (cleaner declines reasonable client request)
    if (
      actorType === 'cleaner' &&
      ev.requested_by === 'client' &&
      ev.is_reasonable
    ) {
      await this.reliability.logEvent({
        cleanerId: job.cleaner_id,
        jobId,
        eventType: 'declined_reasonable_reschedule',
        weight: 0, // pattern job will interpret
        metadata: {},
      });
    }

    return { status: 'declined' as const };
  }
}
6️⃣ Cancellation Service
File: src/core/CancellationService.ts

// src/core/CancellationService.ts

import { Pool } from 'pg';
import { CancellationInput, TimeBucket } from './types';
import { CANCELLATION_CONFIG } from './config';
import { ClientRiskService } from './ClientRiskService';
import { ReliabilityService } from './ReliabilityService';

export class CancellationService {
  constructor(
    private db: Pool,
    private risk: ClientRiskService,
    private reliability: ReliabilityService
  ) {}

  private computeBucket(now: Date, startTime: Date): TimeBucket {
    const diffHours =
      (startTime.getTime() - now.getTime()) / (1000 * 60 * 60);
    if (diffHours <= 0) return 'no_show';
    if (diffHours < 24) return 'lt24';
    if (diffHours <= 48) return '24_48';
    return 'gt48';
  }

  async cancelJob(input: CancellationInput) {
    const { jobId, cancelledBy, reasonCode, useGraceIfAvailable = true } =
      input;

    const jobRes = await this.db.query(
      `SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = $1`,
      [jobId]
    );
    if (jobRes.rows.length === 0) throw new Error('Job not found');
    const job = jobRes.rows[0];

    const now = new Date();
    const startTime = new Date(job.start_time);
    const bucket = this.computeBucket(now, startTime);

    // Load client (for grace and risk)
    const clientRes = await this.db.query(
      `SELECT * FROM clients WHERE id = $1`,
      [job.client_id]
    );
    const client = clientRes.rows[0];

    // NOTE: you need grace columns on clients; using defaults here
    const graceTotal = client.grace_cancellations_total ?? 0;
    const graceUsed = client.grace_cancellations_used ?? 0;

    let graceUsedNow = false;
    if (
      cancelledBy === 'client' &&
      useGraceIfAvailable &&
      graceUsed < graceTotal &&
      bucket !== 'no_show'
    ) {
      graceUsedNow = true;
    }

    const held = job.held_credits;
    const cfg =
      cancelledBy === 'client'
        ? CANCELLATION_CONFIG.client
        : CANCELLATION_CONFIG.cleaner;

    let feePct = cfg[bucket].feePct;

    if (graceUsedNow) feePct = 0;

    const feeCredits = Math.floor((held * feePct) / 100);
    const refundCredits = held - feeCredits;

    let cleanerComp = 0;
    let platformComp = 0;

    if (cancelledBy === 'client' && feeCredits > 0) {
      cleanerComp = Math.floor(
        feeCredits * CANCELLATION_CONFIG.cleanerFeeSharePct
      );
      platformComp = feeCredits - cleanerComp;
    }

    // Transaction: adjust balances + insert cancellation
    const clientId = job.client_id;
    const cleanerId = job.cleaner_id;

    await this.db.query('BEGIN');

    try {
      // credits back to client
      if (refundCredits > 0) {
        await this.db.query(
          `UPDATE clients SET credits = COALESCE(credits,0) + $2 WHERE id = $1`,
          [clientId, refundCredits]
        );
      }

      // cleaner comp
      if (cleanerComp > 0 && cleanerId) {
        await this.db.query(
          `UPDATE cleaners SET pending_credits = COALESCE(pending_credits,0) + $2 WHERE id = $1`,
          [cleanerId, cleanerComp]
        );
      }

      // platform comp goes to an internal ledger (left as TODO)
      // TODO: insert into platform_ledger table

      if (graceUsedNow) {
        await this.db.query(
          `
          UPDATE clients
          SET grace_cancellations_used = COALESCE(grace_cancellations_used,0) + 1
          WHERE id = $1
          `,
          [clientId]
        );
      }

      await this.db.query(
        `
        INSERT INTO cancellation_events (
          job_id, cancelled_by, t_cancel, hours_before_start, bucket, reason_code,
          fee_pct, fee_credits, refund_credits, cleaner_comp_credits, platform_comp_credits, grace_used
        )
        VALUES (
          $1, $2, now(),
          EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM ($3 - now()))/3600,
          $4, $5,
          $6, $7, $8, $9, $10, $11
        )
        `,
        [
          jobId,
          cancelledBy,
          startTime,
          bucket,
          reasonCode,
          feePct,
          feeCredits,
          refundCredits,
          cleanerComp,
          platformComp,
          graceUsedNow,
        ]
      );

      const newStatus =
        bucket === 'no_show'
          ? cancelledBy === 'client'
            ? 'no_show_client'
            : 'no_show_cleaner'
          : 'cancelled';

      await this.db.query(
        `UPDATE jobs SET status = $2, updated_at = now() WHERE id = $1`,
        [jobId, newStatus]
      );

      await this.db.query('COMMIT');
    } catch (err) {
      await this.db.query('ROLLBACK');
      throw err;
    }

    // scoring side-effects
    if (cancelledBy === 'client') {
      if (!graceUsedNow) {
        if (bucket === '24_48') {
          await this.risk.logEvent({
            clientId,
            jobId,
            eventType: 'cancel_24_48',
            weight: 3,
            metadata: {},
          });
        } else if (bucket === 'lt24') {
          await this.risk.logEvent({
            clientId,
            jobId,
            eventType: 'cancel_lt24',
            weight: 5,
            metadata: {},
          });
        } else if (bucket === 'no_show') {
          await this.risk.logEvent({
            clientId,
            jobId,
            eventType: 'no_show',
            weight: 20,
            metadata: {},
          });
        }
      }
    } else if (cancelledBy === 'cleaner' && cleanerId) {
      if (bucket === '24_48') {
        await this.reliability.logEvent({
          cleanerId,
          jobId,
          eventType: 'cancel_24_48',
          weight: -8,
          metadata: {},
        });
      } else if (bucket === 'lt24') {
        await this.reliability.logEvent({
          cleanerId,
          jobId,
          eventType: 'cancel_lt24',
          weight: -12,
          metadata: {},
        });
      } else if (bucket === 'no_show') {
        await this.reliability.logEvent({
          cleanerId,
          jobId,
          eventType: 'no_show',
          weight: -25,
          metadata: {},
        });
      }
    }

    return {
      bucket,
      feePct,
      feeCredits,
      refundCredits,
      cleanerComp,
      platformComp,
      graceUsed: graceUsedNow,
    };
  }
}
7️⃣ Matching Service
File: src/core/MatchingService.ts

// src/core/MatchingService.ts

import { Pool } from 'pg';
import { Location, ReliabilityTier } from './types';
import { MATCHING_WEIGHTS } from './config';

function haversineMiles(lat1: number, lon1: number, lat2: number, lon2: number) {
  const toRad = (v: number) => (v * Math.PI) / 180;
  const R = 3958.8; // miles
  const dLat = toRad(lat2 - lat1);
  const dLon = toRad(lon2 - lon1);
  const a =
    Math.sin(dLat / 2) * Math.sin(dLat / 2) +
    Math.cos(toRad(lat1)) *
      Math.cos(toRad(lat2)) *
      Math.sin(dLon / 2) *
      Math.sin(dLon / 2);
  const c = 2 * Math.atan2(Math.sqrt(a), Math.sqrt(1 - a));
  return R * c;
}

export class MatchingService {
  constructor(private db: Pool) {}

  async getMatchesForJob(params: {
    jobId: string;
    clientId: string;
    jobType: string;
    startTime: Date;
    durationMinutes: number;
    location: Location;
    maxResults?: number;
    enableScoreBasedMatching?: boolean;
    enableRiskAwareMatching?: boolean;
    enforceClientRiskRestrictions?: boolean;
  }) {
    const {
      jobId,
      clientId,
      jobType,
      startTime,
      durationMinutes,
      location,
      maxResults = 20,
      enableScoreBasedMatching = true,
      enableRiskAwareMatching = true,
      enforceClientRiskRestrictions = true,
    } = params;

    // load client risk band
    const riskRes = await this.db.query(
      `SELECT risk_score, risk_band FROM client_risk_scores WHERE client_id = $1`,
      [clientId]
    );
    const riskRow = riskRes.rows[0] ?? { risk_score: 0, risk_band: 'normal' };
    const clientRiskBand: string = riskRow.risk_band;

    // base cleaner candidates
    const cleanersRes = await this.db.query(
      `
      SELECT
        id,
        reliability_score,
        reliability_tier,
        flexibility_status,
        home_lat,
        home_lng,
        travel_radius_mi
      FROM cleaners
      WHERE status = 'active'
      `
    );
    const candidates = cleanersRes.rows as Array<{
      id: string;
      reliability_score: number;
      reliability_tier: ReliabilityTier;
      flexibility_status: string;
      home_lat: number | null;
      home_lng: number | null;
      travel_radius_mi: number;
    }>;

    // pre-load job history counts for repeat client bonus
    const historyRes = await this.db.query(
      `
      SELECT cleaner_id, COUNT(*)::int AS cnt
      FROM jobs
      WHERE client_id = $1
        AND status = 'completed'
      GROUP BY cleaner_id
      `,
      [clientId]
    );
    const historyMap = new Map<string, number>();
    for (const row of historyRes.rows) {
      historyMap.set(row.cleaner_id, row.cnt);
    }

    const maxDist = 30;

    const scored: Array<any> = [];

    for (const c of candidates) {
      if (c.home_lat == null || c.home_lng == null) continue;

      const distanceMiles = haversineMiles(
        location.lat,
        location.lng,
        c.home_lat,
        c.home_lng
      );

      if (distanceMiles > Math.min(c.travel_radius_mi, maxDist)) continue;

      // TODO: availability check: ensure no conflicting jobs for this time

      const reliability = c.reliability_score ?? 0;
      const R = reliability / 100;

      let D = 1 - Math.min(distanceMiles, maxDist) / maxDist;
      if (D < 0) D = 0;

      const pastJobs = historyMap.get(c.id) ?? 0;
      let H = 0;
      if (pastJobs >= 3) H = 0.1;
      else if (pastJobs >= 1) H = 0.05;

      const hasLowFlex = c.flexibility_status === 'low';

      let F = 0;
      if (
        hasLowFlex &&
        (clientRiskBand === 'elevated' ||
          clientRiskBand === 'high' ||
          clientRiskBand === 'critical')
      ) {
        F = -0.2;
      }

      let RiskPenalty = 0;
      if (enableRiskAwareMatching) {
        if (
          (clientRiskBand === 'high' || clientRiskBand === 'critical') &&
          c.reliability_tier === 'Elite'
        ) {
          RiskPenalty = -0.2;
        }
      }

      const w = MATCHING_WEIGHTS;

      let matchScore: number;
      if (enableScoreBasedMatching) {
        matchScore =
          w.reliability * R + w.distance * D + w.history * H + w.flexibility * F;
      } else {
        matchScore = D;
      }

      matchScore += RiskPenalty;

      if (matchScore < 0) matchScore = 0;
      if (matchScore > 1) matchScore = 1;

      let excludedDueToRisk = false;
      if (enforceClientRiskRestrictions) {
        if (clientRiskBand === 'critical' && c.reliability_tier === 'Elite') {
          excludedDueToRisk = true;
        }
      }

      if (!excludedDueToRisk) {
        scored.push({
          cleanerId: c.id,
          reliabilityScore: reliability,
          reliabilityTier: c.reliability_tier,
          flexibilityStatus: c.flexibility_status,
          distanceMiles,
          pastJobs,
          matchScore,
        });
      }
    }

    scored.sort((a, b) => b.matchScore - a.matchScore);

    const top = scored.slice(0, maxResults);

    // log recommendations
    for (let i = 0; i < top.length; i++) {
      const c = top[i];
      await this.db.query(
        `
        INSERT INTO match_recommendations (job_id, client_id, cleaner_id, match_score, rank)
        VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4, $5)
        `,
        [jobId, clientId, c.cleanerId, c.matchScore, i + 1]
      );
    }

    return top;
  }
}
How to Use / Wire This
Run schema_core.sql against your Postgres.

In Node:

// src/index.ts
import { Pool } from 'pg';
import { ClientRiskService } from './core/ClientRiskService';
import { ReliabilityService } from './core/ReliabilityService';
import { RescheduleService } from './core/RescheduleService';
import { CancellationService } from './core/CancellationService';
import { MatchingService } from './core/MatchingService';

const pool = new Pool({ connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL });

const riskService = new ClientRiskService(pool);
const reliabilityService = new ReliabilityService(pool);
const rescheduleService = new RescheduleService(
  pool,
  reliabilityService,
  riskService
);
const cancellationService = new CancellationService(
  pool,
  riskService,
  reliabilityService
);
const matchingService = new MatchingService(pool);
